Stoning on the Fourth Day: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the time for stoning on the fourth day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the time for stoning on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah and apply the ruling in a given scenario based on the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Stoning on the 13th: Abu Hanifa allows from dawn (disliked), the Sahibayn require after midday.

The fourth day of stoning (13th Dhul Hijjah) is a point of intra-Hanafi disagreement. This lesson examines the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, their qiyas arguments, and the practical consequence for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the time in question
The act is stoning the three pillars on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah). Identify the key time boundary: before midday vs. after midday.
This distinction is the core of the dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his analogy
Abu Hanifa holds that the time extends from dawn to sunset. Stoning before midday is makruh (disliked), after midday is sunnah. He analogizes to the first day (Yawm al-Nahr) where stoning is also allowed from dawn.
The first day has a special ruling due to it being the day of Nahr.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their analogy
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the time is only after midday, and stoning before is invalid. They analogize to the second and third days (11th and 12th) where stoning is only valid after zuhr.
The second and third days are considered the regular days of stoning.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a pilgrim stones before zuhr on the 13th, according to Abu Hanifa it is valid (though disliked) and no makeup is needed; according to the Sahibayn, it is invalid and must be repeated after zuhr.
This difference affects the pilgrim's obligation and the need for a dam if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما اليوم الرابع : فعند أبي حنيفة : من طلوع الفجر إلى الغروب، إلا أن ما قبل الزوال : مكروه، وما بعده: مسنون. فإذا أراد أن يتعجَلَ النَّفْرَ : نَفَر إلى مكة . وإن أراد أن يقيم : رمي الجمار الثلاث في يــوم الـرابـع بعد زوال الشمس . وعندهما: وقته ما بعد الزوال، ولا يجوز قبله؛ قياساً على اليوم الثاني والثالث. وأبو حنيفة قاسه على اليوم الأول. فإذا غربت الشمس يوم الرابع: لا يجوز أن يرمي بالليل؛ لأنه قد مضى وقت الرمي، فسقط فعله، ويجب عليه دم للسقوط. ذكره الحُجَندي. * قوله: (فإذا أراد أن يتعجل النفرَ : نَفَرَ إلى مكة، وإن أراد أن يقيم: رمي الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الرابع بعد زوال الشمس). النَّفْرُ: بسكون الفاء: وهو الرجوع. فاليوم الأول: يسمى يوم النحر، والثاني: يوم القر: بالقاف؛ لأن الناس يقرون فيه، والثالث: النفر الأول. وإنما يجوز النفر فيه قبل طلوع الفجر من يوم الرابع، أما إذا طلع الفجر: تعين عليه الرمي. ويوم الرابع: يسمى يوم النفر الثاني. ويوم الرابع: هو يوم الثالث عشر، فمتى طلع الفجر فيه وهو بمنى: لزمه الوقوف للرمي؛ لدخول وقت الرمي.
As for the fourth day, according to Abu Hanifa: from dawn to sunset, except that before midday is disliked, and after midday is recommended. So if he wishes to hasten the departure, he leaves to Makkah; and if he wishes to stay, he stones the three pillars on the fourth day after midday. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): its time is after midday, and it is not allowed before it, by analogy to the second and third days. And Abu Hanifa analogized it to the first day. When the sun sets on the fourth day, it is not allowed to stone at night, because the time for stoning has passed, so its performance is dropped, and a dam is required for the omission. Mentioned by al-Hujandi. His statement: (If he wishes to hasten the departure, he leaves to Makkah; and if he wishes to stay, he stones the three pillars on the fourth day after midday). Al-Nafr (with sukun on the fa) means returning. So the first day is called Yawm al-Nahr, the second: Yawm al-Qarr (with qaf) because people settle, the third: al-Nafr al-Awwal. And the departure (nafr) is only permitted on it before dawn of the fourth day. But if dawn breaks, he is obligated to stone. The fourth day is called Yawm al-Nafr al-Thani. And the fourth day is the thirteenth. So when dawn breaks on it while he is in Mina, he must stay for stoning because the time for stoning has entered.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage addresses the timing for stoning on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah), which is the second day of departure (nafr). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa holds that the time for stoning on this day spans from dawn to sunset, but stoning before midday is makruh (disliked) while after midday is sunnah (recommended). The two companions restrict the time to after midday only, by analogy (qiyas) with the second and third days (11th and 12th), where stoning is not valid before zuhr. Abu Hanifa, however, analogizes it to the first day (the Day of Nahr), where stoning was permissible from dawn (though makruh before sunrise? Actually on the first day, stoning is only at Jamrat al-Aqaba and its time is from dawn to sunset). The practical difference: if a pilgrim stones before zuhr on the 13th, according to Abu Hanifa, it is valid but disliked; according to the two, it is invalid and must be repeated. The text also explains that if a pilgrim chooses to leave (nafr) on the third day (12th), he may depart before dawn of the fourth. But if dawn breaks on the 13th while he is still in Mina, he must stay and stone. After sunset on the 13th, stoning is not permitted, and leaving it out requires a dam (sacrifice). The passage also clarifies the names of the days: Yawm al-Nahr (10th), Yawm al-Qarr (11th), Yawm al-Nafr al-Awwal (12th), and Yawm al-Nafr al-Thani (13th).

Key Terms
النفر (al-nafr): departure from Mina back to Makkah after completing the stoning
يوم القر (yawm al-qarr): the second day (11th) when pilgrims settle in Mina
النفر الأول (al-nafr al-awwal): the third day (12th) when departure is permitted after stoning
النفر الثاني (al-nafr al-thani): the fourth day (13th) after complete stoning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling for stoning the pillars before midday on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah)?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh)
C) It is recommended (sunnah)
D) It is not allowed at all

Key Takeaway
The time for stoning on the fourth day (13th) is disputed among Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa permits it from dawn (makruh before zuhr), while the Sahibayn restrict it to after midday.

Abu Hanifa's Permission for Stoning Before Noon on the Fourth Day
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on stoning before noon on the fourth day of Tashreeq and explain the istihsan reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits stoning before noon on the fourth day using istihsan; the Sahibayn require after noon.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi dispute about the timing of ramy (stoning) on the fourth day of Tashreeq. The fourth day exhibits leniency because pilgrims may leave Mina early, and Abu Hanifa extends that leniency to the stoning time. The Sahibayn, however, maintain the general rule requiring stoning after noon. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh qiyas against istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Disputed Issue
The act is ramy (stoning) on the fourth day of Tashreeq. The specific issue is whether it is permissible to perform this stoning before noon (after dawn) or only after noon.
The fourth day is part of the days of Tashreeq; the first three days require stoning after noon by consensus.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa holds that stoning before noon is permissible (ja'iz). His proof: the verse (2:203) shows leniency by allowing early departure on the fourth day; using istihsan, this leniency should extend to the timing of stoning itself.
The author states 'huwa istihsan' — this is juristic preference overriding strict analogy.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that stoning before noon is not permissible (la yajuz). They rely on qiyas: since stoning on the first three days must be after noon, the fourth day should follow the same rule for uniformity and precaution.
Their position aligns with the general principle that all stoning is after noon, as the Prophet did.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
If a pilgrim stones before noon on the fourth day, the act is valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid according to the Sahibayn. According to the Sahibayn, the pilgrim would need to repeat the stoning after noon.
This difference affects whether the pilgrim's Hajj is complete without repeating the ramy.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
Although this passage does not state the tarjih explicitly, later Hanafi sources (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) adopt the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi — stoning on the fourth day is only valid after noon. This is more cautious and follows the majority practice.
The mufta bihi is not the position of Imam Abu Hanifa due to tarjih based on precaution (ihtiyat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قدم الرمي في هذا اليوم قبل الزوال بعد طلوع الفجر : جاز عند أبي حنيفة . والأفضل أن يقيم بمنى؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام وقف حتى رمي الجمار في اليوم الرابع). وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن تَعَجَلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ ) . البقرة / ٢٠٣، وهما اليوم الثاني والثالث من أيام النحر وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن تَأَخَّرَ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ ) : أي تأخر إلى اليوم الرابع. قوله: (فإن قدم الرمي في هذا اليوم يعني يوم الرابع (قبل الزوال بعد طلوع الفجر : جاز عند أبي حنيفة)، وهو استحسان؛ لأنه لما ظهر أثر التخفيف في هذا اليوم في حق الترك : فلأن يظهر في جوازه في الأوقات كلها أولى. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا يجوز الرمي فيه إلا بعد الزوال.
If he performs the stoning on this day before noon after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. And the best is that he stays in Mina because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stopped until the stoning of the jamarat on the fourth day. And as for His statement: 'So whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him' (Al-Baqarah 2:203) – these are the second and third days of the days of Nahr. And His statement: 'And whoever delays, there is no sin upon him' – meaning he delays until the fourth day. His statement: (If he performs the stoning on this day, meaning the fourth day, before noon after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa), and this is istihsan because since the effect of lightening appeared on this day with regard to leaving [the stoning], it is more appropriate that it appears in its permissibility at all times. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Stoning on it is not permissible except after noon.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of stoning the jamarat on the fourth day of Tashreeq. Abu Hanifa holds that stoning before noon is permissible, based on istihsan (juristic preference). He argues that since Allah has permitted leaving Mina early on that day (showing leniency), it follows that stoning should also be allowed at any time before noon. The Qur'anic verse (2:203) is cited to show that haste is permitted on days two and three, implying that the fourth day also has a lenient ruling. However, the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, maintain that stoning on the fourth day is only valid after noon, in line with the general rule for all days of Tashreeq. The commentary notes that the best practice is to stay in Mina and follow the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
الرمي (al-ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: abandoning strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling due to a stronger evidence or need.
يوم الرابع (yawm al-rabi'): The fourth day of the days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhu al-Hijjah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is stoning permissible on the fourth day of Tashreeq?
A) Only after noon
B) After sunrise before noon
C) At any time of the day
D) Only after sunset

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits stoning before noon on the fourth day via istihsan, but the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view requiring after noon; both are valid Hanafi positions.

Post-Stoning Etiquette: Disliked Acts and Sunnahs
Lists disliked actions and recommended practices after stoning in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on post-stoning etiquette: identify disliked actions, recommend practices, and explain the absence of penalty for leaving Mina.

Core Idea
Staying in Mina after stoning is sunnah; sending luggage early is makruh; leaving incurs no penalty.

After completing the stoning ritual in Mina, the pilgrim enters a period of rest and optional rituals. This lesson from the Hanafi school clarifies which actions are disliked (makruh), which are recommended (sunnah), and what consequences follow if one chooses to leave Mina during the nights of Tashreeq. The rulings are based on the practice of the Companions, especially Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disliked actions
List the two actions explicitly mentioned as makruh: staying outside Mina during the nights of Tashreeq and sending heavy luggage to Mecca before finishing the stoning.
The disliked status is derived from the practice of Umar and the distraction it causes.
2
Explain the rationale for dislike
Understand why these actions are disliked: they occupy the heart and distract from the sunnah of stoning or from worship. The text draws an analogy with placing objects behind one's back during prayer.
The key phrase is 'يوجب شغل قلبه' (causes occupation of the heart).
3
Identify the recommended action
When departing to Mecca, the pilgrim should alight at al-Muhassab (al-Abtah) and stop to supplicate. This is a sunnah.
Al-Muhassab is a valley between Mina and Mecca.
4
Determine the consequence of leaving Mina
If a pilgrim intentionally stays outside Mina (e.g., in Mecca) during the nights, no compensation (dam) is required because staying in Mina is not a wajib act of Hajj; it is only a convenience for stoning.
The text says 'فتركه لا يوجب الجبر' (its abandonment does not require compensation).
5
Distinguish between fard/wajib and this case
Understand the Hanafi distinction: wajib acts require dam when missed, but staying in Mina is not even wajib; it is a sunnah. Hence, no penalty.
This highlights the practical difference between fard/wajib and sunnah/mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره أن يبيت ليالي منى إلا بمنى، «وكان عمر رضي الله عنه يؤدب على ترك المقام بها»(۲). كذا في «الهداية»(۳). ويكره أن يقدم الإنسانُ ثَقَلَه إلى مكة . ويقيم بها حتى يرمي . فإذا نَفَرَ إلى مكة : نزل بالمُحَصَّب . فإن بات في غيرها متعمداً: لا يلزمه شيء عندنا؛ لأنه وجب ليسهل عليه الرمي في أيامه، فلم يكن من أفعال الحج، فتركه لا يوجب الجبر. كذا في «النهاية». قوله : (ويكره أن يقدم الإنسانُ ثَقَلَه إلى مكة، ويقيم حتى يرمي). ثقله : بفتح الثاء والقاف، وهو متاعه وخدمه، وقد روي «أن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يمنع من ذلك، ويؤدب عليه»(۱). و لأنه يوجب شغل قلبه، فيمنعه من إتمام سنة الرمي. وكذا يكره للإنسان أن يجعل شيئاً من حوائجه خلفه ويصلي، مثل النعل، وشبهه؛ لأنه يُشغل قلبه، فلا يتفرغ للعبادة على وجهها؛ لأن قلبه حيث رحله ومتاعه. * قوله: (فإذا نفر إلى مكة نزل بالمُحَصَّب)، وهو الأبطح، يعني إذا فرغ من رمي الجمار، ومضى إلى مكة : أتى وادي الأبطح، ووقف فيه ساعة على راحلته يدعو. (۱) قال في نصب الراية :۸۸/۳: غريب وقال روى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه (١٥٦٢٧) قال عمر رضي الله عنه : من قدم ثقله من منى ليلة نفر : فلا حج له.
And it is disliked to spend the nights of Mina except in Mina. 'And Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to discipline for abandoning staying there.' (Thus in al-Hidayah). And it is disliked for a person to send his heavy luggage to Mecca, and he stays there until he stones. Then when he departs to Mecca, he alights at al-Muhassab. And if he intentionally stays in other than it, nothing is required from him in our school because it (staying) was prescribed to facilitate stoning in its days, so it is not from the actions of Hajj, so its abandonment does not require compensation. Thus in al-Nihaya. His statement: (And it is disliked for a person to send his heavy luggage to Mecca and stays until he stones). Thaqaluh: with fath on tha and qaf, meaning his belongings and servants. And it has been narrated that Umar (RA) used to prevent and discipline for that. And because it causes his heart to be occupied, preventing him from completing the sunnah of stoning. Similarly, it is disliked for a person to put something of his needs behind him and pray, such as a sandal and the like, because it occupies his heart, so he is not free for worship in its proper manner, for his heart is where his luggage and belongings are. His statement: (So when he departs to Mecca, he alights at al-Muhassab), which is al-Abtah, meaning when he finishes stoning the jamarat and proceeds to Mecca, he comes to the valley of al-Abtah and stops there for a while on his mount supplicating.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage contains a series of rulings related to the days after stoning in Mina. It begins by stating that it is makruh (disliked) to spend the nights of the Tashreeq days (11th, 12th, 13th) outside Mina, and Umar (RA) used to discipline those who did so. Then it mentions that it is also disliked to send one’s heavy luggage (thaqal) to Mecca before completing the stoning, as this distracts the heart. The analogy is drawn to a praying person who places objects behind him, which is also disliked for the same reason. After finishing stoning, when the pilgrim departs to Mecca, it is sunnah to alight at al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah), a valley between Mina and Mecca, and stop there for a while in supplication. Finally, the passage addresses the ruling for one who intentionally stays outside Mina (i.e., in Mecca) during these nights: no penalty (dam) is required because staying in Mina is not an integral part of Hajj; it is only a convenience for stoning. This is based on the end of the Hajj actions, and the compensation for leaving a wajib is not incurred here because it is not from the wajibat of Hajj.

Key Terms
الثقل (al-thaqal): Heavy luggage, including belongings and servants, sent ahead to Mecca.
المحصب (al-muhassab): A place between Mina and Mecca, also known as al-Abtah, where the pilgrim stops after stoning before entering Mecca.
الجبر (al-jabr): Compensation (dam) required for omitting a wajib act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on sending one's heavy luggage to Mecca before completing the stoning?
A) It is prohibited (haram)
B) It is disliked (makruh)
C) It is recommended (sunnah)
D) It is obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, after stoning, staying in Mina is sunnah, sending luggage early is makruh, and leaving does not require a dam.

Ruling on Sending Baggage Ahead and Staying at Muhassab
Ruling on baggage and overnight stay at Muhassab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending heavy baggage to Mecca before ramy and identify the recommended stay at Muhassab.

Core Idea
Sending baggage ahead distracts the heart from the sunnah of ramy – it is makruh, not haram.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies two practical issues for the pilgrim: whether to send belongings ahead to Mecca before the day of throwing pebbles (ramy), and where to stay after completing the ramy. The author rules that the first is makruh (disliked) due to its distraction from the sunnah, while the second—staying at Muhassab—is a recommended practice. A precedent from Caliph Umar reinforces the ruling, and a weaker narration even suggests it invalidates the Hajj, but the relied-upon view is that it is merely makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
What are the two acts being ruled upon? One is sending baggage ahead (makruh), the other is staying at Muhassab (sunnah).
The text clearly states 'yukrahu' for the first and recommends the second.
2
Examine the proof for the first ruling
The author cites the practice of Umar (ra) who forbade and disciplined for sending baggage ahead. This is a dalil indicating disapproval.
The proof is from qawl al-sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the 'illa (cause)
Why is it makruh? Because it preoccupies the heart, distracting from the sunnah of ramy. The author also draws an analogy to placing objects behind oneself during prayer.
The 'illa is shughl al-qalb (occupying the heart).
4
Consider the authority weight
The text notes a stronger narration from Umar (ra) saying 'no Hajj', but the commentator declares it gharib (weak), so the mufta bihi remains makruh.
Always check the strength of riwayah when a ruling seems severe.
5
Apply the ruling practically
A pilgrim should avoid sending baggage to Mecca before finishing ramy, and after ramy, it is sunnah to stay at Muhassab briefly to supplicate.
Staying elsewhere deliberately has no penalty.

Source Text

كتاب الحج ويُكْرَهُ أن يقدم الإنسانُ ثَقَلَه إلى مكة . ويقيم بها حتى يرمي . فإذا نَفَرَ إلى مكة : نزل بالمُحَصَّب . فإن بات في غيرها متعمداً: لا يلزمه شيء عندنا؛ لأنه وجب ليسهل عليه الرمي في أيامه، فلم يكن من أفعال الحج، فتركه لا يوجب الجبر. كذا في «النهاية». قوله : (ويكره أن يقدم الإنسانُ ثَقَلَه إلى مكة، ويقيم حتى يرمي). ثقله : بفتح الثاء والقاف، وهو متاعه وخدمه، وقد روي «أن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يمنع من ذلك، ويؤدب عليه»(۱). ولأنه يوجب شغل قلبه، فيمنعه من إتمام سنة الرمي. وكذا يكره للإنسان أن يجعل شيئاً من حوائجه خلفه ويصلي، مثل النعل، وشبهه؛ لأنه يُشغل قلبه، فلا يتفرغ للعبادة على وجهها؛ لأن قلبه حيث رحله ومتاعه. * قوله: (فإذا نفر إلى مكة نزل بالمُحَصَّب)، وهو الأبطح، يعني إذا فرغ من رمي الجمار، ومضى إلى مكة : أتى وادي الأبطح، ووقف فيه ساعة على راحلته يدعو. (۱) قال في نصب الراية :۸۸/۳: غريب وقال روى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه (١٥٦٢٧) قال عمر رضي الله عنه : من قدم ثقله من منى ليلة نفر : فلا حج له.
Chapter of Hajj. It is disliked (makruh) for a person to send his heavy baggage (thaqal) to Mecca and stay there until he throws the pebbles (ramy). When he departs to Mecca, he should stay at al-Muhassab. If he deliberately stays overnight elsewhere, nothing is incumbent upon him according to us; because it was prescribed to facilitate ramy during its days, so it was not one of the actions of Hajj; leaving it does not require compensation (jabr). Thus in al-Nihayah. His statement: (It is disliked for a person to send his heavy baggage to Mecca and stay until he throws). 'Thaqal' with fathah on tha and qaf: his belongings and servants. It has been narrated that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to forbid that and discipline for it. And because it preoccupies his heart, preventing him from completing the sunnah of ramy. Similarly, it is disliked for a person to place something of his needs behind him while praying, such as a sandal or the like, because it occupies his heart and he does not devote himself to worship properly; for his heart is where his belongings and baggage are. * His statement: (When he departs to Mecca, he stays at al-Muhassab) – it is al-Abtah. Meaning when he finishes throwing the pebbles and goes to Mecca, he comes to the valley of al-Abtah, stops there for a moment on his mount supplicating. (1) He said in Nasb al-Raya 3/88: Gharib. And he said: Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf (15627): 'Umar said: Whoever sends his baggage from Mina on the night of departure, has no Hajj.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of Hajj, addressing two issues: sending baggage ahead to Mecca before completing ramy, and the recommended stay at Muhassab. The author begins by stating that it is makruh (disliked) to send one's heavy baggage (thaqal: belongings and servants) to Mecca and for the pilgrim to stay there until the time of ramy. The reason given is that this preoccupies the heart and distracts from properly performing the sunnah of ramy. A precedent from Caliph Umar is cited: he used to forbid this practice and discipline those who did it. The commentator draws an analogy to prayer: placing objects like sandals behind oneself is similarly disliked because it distracts the heart. The second part discusses the recommended practice after completing ramy: when departing from Mina to Mecca, the pilgrim should stay at al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah), stopping there on his mount to make supplication. This is considered a sunnah. The footnote adds a stronger narration: 'Umar reportedly said that sending baggage from Mina on the night of departure invalidates the Hajj, but this narration is considered gharib (weak) per Nasb al-Raya.

Key Terms
ثقل (thaqal): Heavy baggage, including belongings and servants, that a pilgrim sends ahead to Mecca.
المحصب (al-Muhassab): A place between Mina and Mecca (al-Abtah) where pilgrims are recommended to stay after throwing pebbles.
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a pilgrim sending his heavy baggage to Mecca before the day of ramy?
A) It is wajib to send it ahead.
B) It is makruh (disliked).
C) It is haram (prohibited).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Sending heavy baggage to Mecca before completing the ramy is makruh (disliked) because it distracts the heart; staying at Muhassab after ramy is a sunnah, not wajib.

Tawaf al-Sadr: The Farewell Circumambulation
Description and ruling of the farewell circumambulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr in the Hanafi school, identify who is exempt, and explain the evidence for its wajib status.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for non-Makkans as a farewell to the House.

After completing the rituals of Hajj, pilgrims are required to perform a final circumambulation before leaving Mecca. This act, known as Tawaf al-Sadr or Tawaf al-Wada', carries a specific ruling in the Hanafi school that distinguishes between residents of Mecca and others. In this lesson, we examine the passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayra that explains its obligation, its performance, and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Tawaf al-Sadr is and its legal status. The passage states it is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the people of Mecca. Note the exemption for Makkans.
The text also mentions alternative names: Tawaf al-Wada' and Khayf Bani Kinana.
2
Understand the manner of performance
The tawaf consists of seven circuits without ramal (hurrying) because there is no sa'y after it. Also note the concession for menstruating women to omit it, and the sunnah of praying two rak'ahs after it.
No sa'y is performed after this tawaf because sa'y is not repeated in Hajj.
3
Locate the evidence
The passage cites Sahih Muslim for the Prophet's practice of staying at Muhassab, which is related to the sunnah of staying (nuzul) associated with this tawaf. The primary dalil for the wajib ruling is the rationale of farewell, not a specific textual proof in this passage.
The footnote refers to Sahih Muslim (1310) and Nasb al-Raya.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school considers Tawaf al-Sadr wajib, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. Understand the practical consequence: omission of a wajib requires compensation (dam), while omission of a sunnah does not.
This difference affects the pilgrim's liability if the tawaf is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، لا يَرْمُلُ فيها، وهذا طوافُ الصَّدَر، وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة ويقال له: خَيْف بني كنانة والنزول به سنةٌ عندنا؛ «لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام نزل به قصداً»(۱). طواف الوداع :] قوله : (ثم يدخل مكة، فيطوف بالبيت سبعة أشواط لا يرمل فيها)؛ لأنه لا سعي بعده. ورخص للنساء الحيض في تركه. ولا يسعى بعده؛ لأن السعي لا يتكرر. ويصلي ركعتي الطواف بعده؛ لأن ختم كل طواف بركعتين، سواء كان الطواف فرضاً أو نفلاً. كذا في «النهاية». قوله: (وهذا الطواف طوافُ الصَّدَر، ويسمى: طواف الوداع: بفتح الواو، وطواف آخر عهد بالبيت ؛ لأنه يودع البيت، ويصدر عنه. ويدخل وقته إذا حلَّ له النفر الأول. * قوله: (وهو واجب، إلا على أهل مكة ؛ لأنه يجب لمفارقة البيت وتوديعه، وهم يفارقونه، ولا يصدرون عنه. (۱) صحیح مسلم (۱۳۱۰) ، وينظر نصب الراية ٨٨/٣.
Chapter of Hajj. Then he circumambulates the House seven circuits without hurrying (ramal) in them, and this is Tawaf al-Sadr, and it is obligatory (wajib) except for the people of Mecca. It is also called Khayf Bani Kinana, and staying there is a sunnah according to us, 'because the Prophet (peace be upon him) intentionally stayed there' (1). Tawaf al-Wada':] His statement: (Then he enters Mecca and circumambulates the House seven circuits without ramal in them) because there is no sa'y after it. A concession is given for menstruating women to omit it. And he does not perform sa'y after it because sa'y is not repeated. He prays two rak'ahs of tawaf after it because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is obligatory or supererogatory. Thus in al-Nihayah. His statement: (This tawaf is Tawaf al-Sadr, also called Tawaf al-Wada' with fatha on the waw, and the last tawaf of the House because he bids farewell to the House and departs from it. Its time enters when the first departure (al-nafr al-awwal) becomes permissible for him. * His statement: (It is obligatory except for the people of Mecca) because it is required for parting from the House and bidding farewell, and they (the Makkans) part from it (every day) and do not depart from it. (1) Sahih Muslim (1310), and see Nasb al-Raya 3/88.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage explains Tawaf al-Sadr (also called Tawaf al-Wada', the farewell circumambulation) after completing the Hajj rituals. The author states that the pilgrim should perform seven circuits of the Kaaba without ramal (hurrying) because there is no sa'y after this tawaf. A concession is given for menstruating women: they are not required to perform it. The pilgrim prays two rak'ahs after the tawaf, as is the practice for all circumambulations. The tawaf is described as wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the residents of Mecca. The reason is that it is for bidding farewell to the House; Makkans do not need to say farewell since they do not depart from the city. Its time begins when the pilgrim is permitted to perform the first departure (al-nafr al-awwal) from Mina. The footnote cites Sahih Muslim as evidence for the Prophet's practice of staying at Muhassab (which is sometimes associated with this tawaf).

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed after completing Hajj rituals before leaving Mecca.
رمل (ramal): Hurrying with short steps during tawaf, which is omitted here because there is no sa'y after this tawaf.
النفر الأول (al-nafr al-awwal): The first permissible departure from Mina on the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah after completing ramy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wajib.
B) Sunnah.
C) Haram.
D) Mustahab.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr is a wajib act for non-Makkans, omitted at the cost of a compensation sacrifice.

Obligation of Tawaf al-Sadr and Its Exceptions
Explains obligation of farewell tawaf, exception for Makkans, and recourse if missed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr, identify who is exempt, and apply the compensation rule when it is missed.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all pilgrims except Makkans; omission requires a dam, not Hajj invalidation.

Tawaf al-Sadr, also called Tawaf al-Wada', is the final circumambulation of the Kaaba before leaving Makkah after Hajj. The Hanafi school treats it as a wajib—an obligation whose proof is strong but zanni—rather than a rukn. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, the exemption for residents of Makkah and its environs, and the consequences for a pilgrim who departs without performing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the passage describes a specific tawaf (7 circuits, no ramal) performed after the Hajj rites, and the ruling: wajib for all except the people of Makkah.
The term 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh means an obligation established by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
2
Locate the Dalil and Trace Its Implications
Find the hadith quoted: 'Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last act be tawaf of the House.' The imperative 'falyakun' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul, making the tawaf wajib.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which explains why the ruling is wajib not fard.
3
Identify the Exceptions
Note the exception for 'Ahl Makkah' and those in their status (people of the miqat and closer). Also note the concession for menstruating women to omit the tawaf.
Makkans are exempt because they do not actually depart from the House; they can enter and exit without ihram.
4
Analyze the Consequence of Omission
Study the scenarios: if one misses the tawaf and remembers before passing the miqat, he should return; if after passing the miqat, he must offer a dam. If he returns, he does so with an 'umrah, then performs the tawaf.
Returning with 'umrah is necessary because the pilgrim has already left the state of ihram and must re-enter it.
5
Consider the Intra-Hanafi Variant
Note Abu Hanifah's recommendation: if a pilgrim stays in Makkah after Tawaf al-Sadr until 'isha, it is mustahabb to perform another tawaf to avoid a gap. The default view is that no additional tawaf is needed.
This is a difference within the school; the mufta bihi is the default view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، لا يَرْمُلُ فيها، وهذا طوافُ الصَّدَر، وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة. ويقال له: خَيْف بني كنانة والنزول به سنةٌ عندنا؛ «لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام نزل به قصداً».
طواف الوداع :]
قوله : (ثم يدخل مكة، فيطوف بالبيت سبعة أشواط لا يرمل فيها)؛ لأنه لا سعي بعده. ورخص للنساء الحيض في تركه. ولا يسعى بعده؛ لأن السعي لا يتكرر. ويصلي ركعتي الطواف بعده؛ لأن ختم كل طواف بركعتين، سواء كان الطواف فرضاً أو نفلاً. كذا في «النهاية».
قوله: (وهذا الطواف طوافُ الصَّدَر، ويسمى: طواف الوداع: بفتح الواو، وطواف آخر عهد بالبيت ؛ لأنه يودع البيت، ويصدر عنه. ويدخل وقته إذا حلَّ له النفر الأول.
* قوله: (وهو واجب، إلا على أهل مكة ؛ لأنه يجب لمفارقة البيت وتوديعه، وهم يفارقونه، ولا يصدرون عنه.
ثم يعود إلى أهله.
وكذا من كان في حكم أهل مكة من أهل المواقيت، ومن دونها إلى مكة؛ لأنهم في حكم أهل مكة ؛ بدليل جواز دخولهم مكة بغير إحرام. وإنما كان طواف الصدر واجباً؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «مَن حج هذا البيت فليكن آخر عهده به الطواف»، والأمر للوجوب. فإن تشاغل بمكة بعد طواف الصدر: فليس عليه طواف آخر. وعن أبي حنيفة : أنه إذا أقام بعده إلى العشاء: استحب له أن يطوف طوافاً آخر ؛ ليكون مودعاً للبيت من غير فاصلة.
ومن نفر، ولم يطف للصدر : فإنه يرجع ما لم يتجاوز الميقات، فإن ذكر بعد مجاوزته الميقات: لم يرجع، ويلزمه دم.
فإن رجع: رجع بعمرة، ويبتدئ بطوافها؛ لأنه تعين عليه بالإحرام، فإذا فرغ من عمرته : طاف للصدر، وسقط عنه الدم.
قوله: (ثم يعود إلى أهله).
في هذا إشارة إلى كراهة المجاورة، وقد صرح به في المستصفى».
The Book of Hajj. Then he circumambulates the House seven circuits, not jogging in them, and this is the Farewell Circumambulation (Tawaf al-Sadar), and it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah. It is also called Khayf Bani Kinanah, and alighting at it is sunnah according to us because the Prophet (peace be upon him) alighted there intentionally. Section on Farewell Tawaf: His saying: (Then he enters Makkah and circumambulates the House seven circuits without jogging) because there is no sa'y after it. And concession was given for menstruating women to omit it. And he does not perform sa'y after it because sa'y is not repeated. And he prays two rak'ahs after the tawaf because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is obligatory or supererogatory. So said in al-Nihayah. His saying: (This tawaf is Tawaf al-Sadar, and it is called Tawaf al-Wada' [with fatha on the waw], and the last tawaf at the House, because he bids farewell to the House and departs from it. Its time enters when the first departure [al-nafr al-awwal] becomes permissible for him.) His saying: (And it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah because it is required for leaving the House and bidding it farewell, and they [the Makkans] are not leaving it, nor do they depart from it. Then he returns to his family.) Likewise, anyone who is in the same status as the people of Makkah from among the people of the miqat and those between the miqat and Makkah, because they are in the same status as the people of Makkah as evidenced by the permissibility of their entering Makkah without ihram. And Tawaf al-Sadar is obligatory because of his saying (peace be upon him): “Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last act be tawaf of the House.” And the command indicates obligation. If he busies himself in Makkah after Tawaf al-Sadar, there is no other tawaf upon him. And from Abu Hanifah: if he stays after it until the evening prayer (al-'isha'), it is recommended (mustahabb) for him to perform another tawaf to bid farewell to the House without any gap. And if someone departs without performing Tawaf al-Sadar, he should return as long as he has not passed the miqat. If he remembers after passing the miqat, he should not return, and a dam (blood sacrifice) becomes obligatory upon him. If he returns, he returns with an 'umrah, and begins with its tawaf because it is incumbent upon him due to the ihram. When he completes his 'umrah, he performs Tawaf al-Sadar, and the dam is waived. His saying: (Then he returns to his family.) In this there is an indication of the disapproval (karahah) of residing [in Makkah after Hajj], and it is explicitly stated in al-Mustasfa.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah explains the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr (also called Tawaf al-Wada'), which is the farewell circumambulation performed after completing the rites of Hajj before leaving Makkah. The author first establishes that this tawaf consists of seven circuits without ramal (jogging) because there is no sa'y after it. It is a separate tawaf from the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) and the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah). The text states that it is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the people of Makkah and those who are in their status, i.e., residents of the miqat areas or the sacred precincts, because they do not actually depart from Makkah after the Hajj. The proof given is the hadith: “Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last act be tawaf of the House,” which is an imperative indicating obligation according to Hanafi usul. The text then discusses concessions: menstruating women are excused from this tawaf. It also notes that one does not perform sa'y after it because sa'y is not repeated. After the tawaf, one prays two rak'ahs, as is the case for any tawaf. The time for Tawaf al-Sadar begins when the pilgrim becomes eligible for the first departure (al-nafr al-awwal), i.e., after the days of tashriq. The passage then addresses the scenario where a pilgrim busies himself in Makkah after performing Tawaf al-Sadar: no additional tawaf is required, but according to Abu Hanifah, if he remains until the evening prayer, it is mustahabb to perform another farewell tawaf to avoid a gap. Regarding one who departs without performing Tawaf al-Sadar: he must return as long as he has not passed the miqat; if he passes it, he does not return but instead must offer a dam (blood sacrifice). If he returns, he must do so with the intention of performing 'umrah, starting with its tawaf, then after completing the 'umrah he performs Tawaf al-Sadar, and the dam is dropped. Finally, the text indicates that it is makruh (disliked) to reside in Makkah after the Hajj without returning home, as stated in al-Mustasfa.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawāf al-Ṣadar): The farewell circumambulation performed after completing the rites of Hajj before leaving Makkah.
طواف الوداع (Tawāf al-Wadā‘): Synonym for Tawaf al-Sadar, meaning farewell tawaf.
واجب (Wājib): An obligation established by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.
أهل مكة (Ahl Makkah): Residents of Makkah and those in their legal status, including those living within the miqat boundaries or closer to Makkah.
دم (Dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep or equivalent) required as compensation for omitting a wajib of Hajj or 'umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All pilgrims except the people of Makkah
B) Only menstruating women
C) Only the sick
D) All pilgrims are required to perform it without exception

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr is a wajib of Hajj; its omission is compensated by a dam, not by repeating Hajj, and Makkans are exempt because they do not depart from the House.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Obligation, Proof, and Consequences
Ruling on the farewell tawaf with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf al-sadr, identify its dalil (hadith proof), and apply the consequences for omitting it (dam or return with umra).

Core Idea
Tawaf al-sadr is wajib; omission requires compensation—either return before the miqat or sacrifice a dam.

After completing the rituals of Hajj, the pilgrim is required to perform a farewell tawaf called tawaf al-sadr. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that this tawaf is obligatory (wajib), based on a direct command of the Prophet ﷺ, and outlines what a pilgrim must do if they leave Mecca without performing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on tawaf al-sadr. Identify the hukm level: wajib. Note who it applies to—the pilgrim and those in the ruling of Meccans.
The act is tawaf al-sadr, performed after all Hajj rituals.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last act be the tawaf.' This is a direct command (amr).
Hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (falyakun) indicates obligation (wujub). Thus the hadith proves that tawaf al-sadr is wajib.
Al-amr yufidu al-wujub is the principle.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi variant
If the pilgrim stays in Mecca after tawaf al-sadr until 'isha, Abu Hanifa recommends (istihbab) performing an extra tawaf to avoid a long interval. This does not change the wajib status of the original tawaf.
The recommended act is mustahabb, not wajib.
5
Apply the consequences for omission
If someone leaves without tawaf al-sadr: if still within the miqat, they must return and perform it; if they have passed the miqat, they do not return but must offer dam. If they return after passing the miqat, they must do so with umra, then perform tawaf al-sadr, and the dam is dropped.
The miqat is the boundary around Mecca; passing it triggers the obligation of dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعود إلى أهله. وكذا من كان في حكم أهل مكة من أهل المواقيت، ومن دونها إلى مكة؛ لأنهم في حكم أهل مكة ; بدليل جواز دخولهم مكة بغير إحرام. وإنما كان طواف الصدر واجباً؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من حج هذا البيت فليكن آخر عهده به الطواف)، والأمر للوجوب. فإن تشاغل بمكة بعد طواف الصدر: فليس عليه طواف آخر. وعن أبي حنيفة : أنه إذا أقام بعده إلى العشاء(۲): استحب له أن يطوف طوافاً آخر ; ليكون مودعاً للبيت من غير فاصلة. ومن نفر، ولم يطف للصدر : فإنه يرجع ما لم يتجاوز الميقات، فإن ذكر بعد مجاوزته الميقات: لم يرجع، ويلزمه دم. فإن رجع: رجع بعمرة، ويبتدئ بطوافها; لأنه تعين عليه بالإحرام، فإذا فرغ من عمرته : طاف للصدر، وسقط عنه الدم.
Then he returns to his family. Similarly, one who is in the ruling of the people of Mecca, from the people of the miqat and those within it to Mecca, because they are in the ruling of the people of Mecca, evidenced by the permissibility of their entering Mecca without ihram. And indeed tawaf al-sadr is wajib because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last act be the tawaf.' And the command indicates obligation. If he engages in business in Mecca after tawaf al-sadr, there is no other tawaf upon him. And from Abu Hanifa: that if he stays after it until al-'isha, it is mustahabb for him to perform another tawaf so that he farewells the House without interval. And whoever leaves and does not perform tawaf al-sadr: he returns as long as he has not passed the miqat; if he remembers after passing the miqat, he does not return, and a dam is incumbent on him. If he returns, he returns with an 'umra, and begins with its tawaf because it has become determined upon him by the ihram. When he completes his 'umra, he performs tawaf al-sadr, and the dam is dropped from him.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by stating the general rule: the pilgrim returns home after Hajj. It then addresses those under the ruling of Meccans—people of the miqat areas or within—who are like Meccans in that they may enter Mecca without ihram. For them, tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf) is wajib. The proof is the Prophet's hadith 'Let his last act be the tawaf.' In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates wujub. If after tawaf al-sadr the pilgrim busies himself with trade in Mecca, no extra tawaf is required. However, according to a narration from Abu Hanifa, if he stays until the 'isha prayer, it is mustahabb to perform another tawaf to complete the farewell without an interval. If someone departs without tawaf al-sadr, he must return if he has not yet passed the miqat. If he has passed the miqat, he does not return but owes a dam (sacrifice). If he does return, he must do so with the intention of 'umra, beginning with its tawaf because the ihram for 'umra is required. After completing the 'umra, he performs tawaf al-sadr, and the dam is no longer necessary.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing Hajj rituals, deemed wajib.
الميقات (al-miqt): The boundary (place or time) for returning to perform tawaf al-sadr if one leaves without it.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as compensation for omitting a wajib act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on tawaf al-sadr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-sadr is wajib; if omitted, the pilgrim must either return before the miqat or offer a dam; if returning after passing the miqat, he must do so with umra.

Tawaf al-Qudum Falls if One Goes Directly to 'Arafat
Ruling on tawaf al-qudum dropping when not entering Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tawaf al-qudum when the pilgrim does not enter Mecca and explain the analogy with tahiyyat al-masjid.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum drops if you don't enter Mecca; it's sunnah, no compensation.

In Hajj, the pilgrim who enters Mecca is recommended to perform tawaf al-qudum as a greeting. But what if the pilgrim goes directly to 'Arafat without entering the city? This passage clarifies that the tawaf drops entirely, and no compensatory sacrifice is required. The ruling is supported by a clear analogy with the greeting of the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf). The text states that it 'falls' (saqata) if the muhrim does not enter Mecca.
The ruling is that the tawaf is not required; it is not wajib or fard.
2
Understand the condition for the sunnah
The sunnah of tawaf al-qudum is conditional upon entering Mecca (dakhul Makkah). If entry does not occur, the sunnah does not apply.
Entry means physically crossing the boundary of Mecca with the intention to perform Hajj or 'Umra.
3
Recognize the proof by analogy
The author draws an analogy (qiyas) with tahiyyat al-masjid: just as tahiyyat al-masjid is not required if one does not enter the mosque, similarly tawaf al-qudum is not required if one does not enter Mecca.
The common cause ('illa) is the lack of entry.
4
Confirm the consequence of omission
Since tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah, omitting it does not require any compensation (jabar), such as a dam (sacrifice).
In Hanafi fiqh, only wajib omissions require compensation; sunnah omissions do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن لم يدخل المُحْرِم مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات، ووقف بها على ما قدمناه: فقد سقط عنه طواف القدوم)؛ لأنه إنما يلزمه لدخول مكة، ولم يدخل، كما لا تلزمه تحية المسجد إذا لم يدخله. * قوله: (ولا) شيء عليه لتركه ; لأنه سُنَّةٌ، وبترك السنن لا الجابر.
His statement: (If the muhrim does not enter Mecca and proceeds to 'Arafat and stands there as we have previously mentioned: then tawaf al-qudum has dropped from him) because it is only required for entering Mecca, and he did not enter, just as the tahiyyat of the mosque is not required if he does not enter it. * His statement: (And nothing) is upon him for leaving it, because it is a sunnah, and for leaving sunan, no compensator [is required].
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a proof by analogy. It addresses the case of a pilgrim (muhrim) who does not enter Mecca on his way to 'Arafat but proceeds directly to 'Arafat and stands there. The commentator explains that tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) is not obligatory because it is only required upon entering Mecca. Since the pilgrim did not enter Mecca, the tawaf falls. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) with the tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting of the mosque): just as one is not required to perform tahiyyat al-masjid if one does not enter the mosque, similarly tawaf al-qudum is not required if one does not enter Mecca. The text then adds that no compensation (dam) is due for leaving tawaf al-qudum because it is a sunnah, not a wajib. In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a sunnah does not require any jabar (compensatory act).

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The arrival tawaf performed upon entering Mecca for Hajj or 'Umra; it is sunnah.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The two-rak'ah prayer performed upon entering a mosque to greet it; it is sunnah.
جابر (jabar): A compensatory act (e.g., dam, sadaqah) required for omitting a wajib; not required for sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on tawaf al-qudum if a pilgrim goes directly to 'Arafat without entering Mecca?
A) It is still wajib and must be performed later
B) It is dropped and no compensation is required
C) It is dropped but a dam is required
D) It becomes mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah that drops if the pilgrim does not enter Mecca; no compensation is required for its omission.

Ruling on Residing in Mecca After Hajj (Mujawara): Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-school difference on residing in Mecca after Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on mujawara and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa dislikes residing in Mecca after Hajj; the Sahibayn commend it — a difference rooted in spiritual caution versus virtue.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayirah presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the ruling of mujawara (staying in Mecca after completing Hajj). While Abu Hanifa considers it makruh tanzihi due to the potential for diminished reverence and increased gravity of sin, his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that it is not makruh and even preferable. Understanding this difference helps us appreciate the range of valid opinion within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The act is mujawara: residing in Mecca after completing Hajj. State the ruling according to Abu Hanifa (makruh tanzih) and according to the Sahibayn (not makruh, rather afdal).
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
His reasoning: fear of boredom (leading to disrespect), loss of reverence/heebah, and the fact that sin in Mecca is more severe. Thus, staying may lead to greater spiritual harm.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning
Their reasoning is not explicitly given, but it is understood that they emphasize the virtue of staying in the sacred territory and the spiritual benefits of proximity to the Haram.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: should one avoid staying or seek to stay? According to Abu Hanifa, one should leave; according to the Sahibayn, staying is better.
5
Note the absence of tarjih
The text does not indicate which position is relied upon (mufta bihi). Later Hanafi works often adopt the Sahibayn's view due to ease, but this is not in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال: تكره المجاورة بمكة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لخوف الملل، وقلة الحرمة، وسقوط الهيبة، وخوف الوقوع في الذنب، فإن الذنب فيها عظيم القبح، منه في غيرها. أقبح وعندهما لا تكره المجاورة، بل هي أفضل.
So he said: Residing in Mecca is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, due to fear of boredom, lack of reverence, loss of awe, and fear of falling into sin, for sin there is greater in ugliness than elsewhere. And according to the two, residing is not disliked; rather it is better.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mujawara (residing in Mecca after completing Hajj). According to Abu Hanifa, it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) because of the potential consequences: boredom leading to disrespect, diminished reverence for the holy city, and the heightened gravity of sin in Mecca. Since the sacredness of Mecca makes sins more severe, there is a risk of committing sin. Therefore, it is better to leave. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not consider mujawara makruh; rather, they deem it afdal (better). The text does not provide a specific dalil for either view; the opinions are based on the Imams' understanding of the spiritual benefits and risks. The practice of mujawara has been observed by many scholars throughout history. The commentary does not give a tarjih, so the mufta bihi position is not specified here.

Key Terms
المجاورة (al-mujawara): Residing in a sacred territory, specifically Mecca, after performing Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on residing in Mecca after Hajj (mujawara)?
A) Mustahabb
B) Makruh
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on mujawara: Abu Hanifa holds it makruh; the Sahibayn hold it is not makruh and even preferable.

Timing of the 'Arafah Stand and Catching Hajj
Definition of the valid time for the 'Arafah stand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi time for the stand at 'Arafah and explain the practical consequence of the Maliki disagreement.

Core Idea
The 'Arafah stand is valid only from noon (zawal) of the 9th to dawn of the 10th — standing earlier is invalid in the Hanafi school.

In this passage, the Hanafi position on the timing of the stand at 'Arafah is presented, along with a brief note that Imam Malik held a different view. Understanding the exact time window is crucial for performing Hajj correctly and recognizing valid scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the stand is valid from zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah to the appearance of fajr (dawn) on the 10th.
This includes both daytime and nighttime standing.
2
Identify the Maliki difference
Imam Malik said the time begins at sunrise, not zawal.
The text does not provide proofs for either view.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
A pilgrim standing between sunrise and zawal: valid in Maliki, invalid in Hanafi.
This practical difference affects millions of pilgrims annually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن أدرك الوقوف بعرفة ما بين زوال الشمس من يوم عرفة إلى طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر : فقد أدرك الحج)، سواء كان عالماً بها، أو جاهلاً. ولو وقف قبل الزوال: لم يُعتد به. وقال مالك (۱) : وقت الوقوف من طلوع الشمس من يوم عرفة.
His statement: (And whoever catches the stand at 'Arafat between the noon decline (zawal) of the sun on the day of 'Arafat and the dawn of the day of al-Nahr [the 10th] has caught Hajj), whether he is knowledgeable or ignorant. And if he stands before zawal, it is not considered. And Malik said: the time of standing is from sunrise on the day of 'Arafat.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the timing of the stand at 'Arafat and then contrasts it with the Maliki position. The Hanafi view is that the valid time for the stand (wuquf) at 'Arafat begins at zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah (Yawm 'Arafat) and extends until the appearance of fajr (true dawn) on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr). Anyone who stands within this period—whether they are aware of the time or ignorant—has completed the essential element of Hajj. Standing before zawal is invalid and not counted. Then the text notes that Imam Malik differed, holding that the time begins from sunrise on the 9th, not from zawal. The practical difference is that someone who stands between sunrise and zawal would have a valid Hajj according to Malik, but according to Hanafis, it would not count, and they would need to repeat the stand after zawal or compensate.

Key Terms
الوقف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi-'Arafat): The act of standing at the plain of 'Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; it is the most important rukn of Hajj.
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The moment when the sun passes its zenith (noon).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for the stand at 'Arafat begin?
A) At sunrise on the 9th
B) At noon (zawal) on the 9th
C) At sunset on the 9th
D) At dawn on the 10th

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the time for the 'Arafah stand as from noon (zawal) of the 9th to dawn of the 10th, contrary to the Maliki view which includes sunrise.

Arrival Tawaf: Ruling When Bypassing Mecca
Ruling that arrival tawaf drops if pilgrim bypasses Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the arrival tawaf when a pilgrim goes directly to Arafat and explain the qiyas used to justify the dropping of the tawaf.

Core Idea
Arrival tawaf is a sunnah tied to entering Mecca; if you bypass Mecca, it drops with no penalty.

In Hajj, the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) is a recommended act performed upon entering Mecca. But what if a pilgrim never enters Mecca and goes straight to Arafat? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the tawaf is no longer required, and no compensation is due. The ruling is based on a clear qiyas analogy with the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf). Determine its legal status in the Hanafi school: is it wajib or sunnah? According to the text, it is a sunnah, so omitting it does not require a compensatory sacrifice (dam).
2
Recognize the condition for its recommendation
The arrival tawaf is recommended only when the pilgrim enters Mecca. If the pilgrim bypasses Mecca and goes directly to Arafat, the condition for its recommendation is absent, so it is no longer recommended.
3
Analyze the qiyas analogy
The author analogizes to tahiyyat al-masjid (the two-rak'ah prayer of greeting the mosque). Just as tahiyyat al-masjid is not required if one does not enter the mosque, the arrival tawaf is not required if one does not enter Mecca. The illa (effective cause) is entering: both acts are tied to entering a sacred space.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the link is straightforward.
4
Apply the consequence of the act's status
Since the arrival tawaf is a sunnah, not a wajib, leaving it does not require any jabir (compensatory act). This distinguishes it from wajib acts in Hajj, which would require a dam if missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يدخل المُحْرِمُ مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات، ووقف بها على ما قدمناه: فقد سَقَط عنه طواف القدوم، ولا شيء عليه لتركه. قوله: (فإن لم يدخل المُحرِم مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات، ووقف بها على ما قدمناه: فقد سقط عنه طواف القدوم)؛ لأنه إنما يلزمه لدخول مكة، ولم يدخل، كما لا تلزمه تحية المسجد إذا لم يدخله. قوله: (ولا شيء عليه لتركه)؛ لأنه سُنَّةٌ، وبترك السنن لا يجب الجابر.
If the pilgrim does not enter Mecca and heads to Arafat and stands there as we have presented, then the arrival tawaf is dropped from him, and nothing is due upon him for leaving it. His statement: (If the pilgrim does not enter Mecca and heads to Arafat and stands there as we have presented, then the arrival tawaf is dropped from him) because it is only incumbent upon him for entering Mecca, and he did not enter, just as the greeting of the mosque is not incumbent upon him if he does not enter it. His statement: (and nothing is due upon him for leaving it) because it is a sunnah, and for leaving sunnahs, the compensatory (jabir) is not required.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a brief qiyas-based proof. The ruling: If a pilgrim in ihram goes directly to Arafat without first entering Mecca, the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) is no longer required. The author explains that the arrival tawaf is linked to entering Mecca; since the pilgrim did not enter, the obligation does not arise. He draws an analogy to the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid): if one does not enter the mosque, there is no obligation to perform the greeting prayer. Further, because the arrival tawaf is a sunnah (not a wajib), leaving it does not require any compensatory act (al-jabir, such as a dam). This is a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the optional nature of the arrival tawaf for those who bypass Mecca.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation performed upon entering Mecca for Hajj or Umrah, considered a sunnah in the Hanafi school.
الجابر (al-jabir): A compensatory act, such as a dam (sacrifice), required for leaving a wajib; not required for leaving a sunnah in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim goes directly to Arafat without entering Mecca, what is the ruling on the arrival tawaf?
A) It must be performed after Arafat.
B) It is dropped, and no compensation is required.
C) It is dropped, but a dam is required.
D) It is still required after returning to Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The arrival tawaf is a sunnah tied to entering Mecca; bypassing Mecca drops the tawaf without any penalty.

The Dispute on Prolonged Residence in Mecca (Al-Mujawarah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of al-mujawarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on al-mujawarah, state Abu Hanifa’s reasons for deeming it makruh, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa feared that prolonged stay in Mecca breeds complacency and magnifies sin; his students saw it as a virtue.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the ruling of prolonged residence (al-mujawarah) in Mecca. Imam Abu Hanifa considered it makruh, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), considered it not only permissible but superior (afdhal). Understanding this dispute reveals how jurists weigh spiritual benefits against potential harms.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa’s position
Identify that Abu Hanifa rules mujawarah as makruh (disliked).
Makruh here is likely makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa’s dalil
Examine the rational reasons: fear of boredom (al-malal), loss of reverence (qillat al-hurmah), loss of awe (suqut al-haybah), and increased gravity of sin (since sin in Mecca is far more severe).
These are talil (rational grounds), not textual proofs.
3
Identify the Sahibayn’s position
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold mujawarah is not makruh but afdhal (superior).
Their reasoning is not given in the text, but it likely relies on the general merit of residing in the Haram.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: one avoids settling in Mecca, the other considers it virtuous. Later Hanafi fatwa favors the Sahibayn’s view.
The mufta bihi is that mujawarah is recommended, not makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال: تكره المجاورة بمكة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لخوف الملل، وقلة الحرمة، وسقوط الهيبة، وخوف الوقوع في الذنب، فإن الذنب فيها عظيم القبح، منه في غيرها. أقبح وعندهما لا تكره المجاورة، بل هي أفضل.
He said: Residing (al-mujawarah) in Mecca is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, due to fear of boredom, lack of reverence, loss of awe, and fear of falling into sin, for indeed sin in it is of great ugliness, more ugly than in other places. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not disliked, rather it is superior.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of prolonged residence (al-mujawarah) in Mecca. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked) for several reasons: the risk of becoming bored with the sacred city, which may lead to a loss of reverence and awe for it, and the increased gravity of sin committed in Mecca compared to elsewhere — sin there is far more severe. Therefore, to protect oneself, it is better not to reside permanently. However, his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), hold the opposite view: they consider residing in Mecca not only not disliked but actually afdhal (better/superior). Their reasoning, though not explicitly given here, is likely based on the general merit of living in the sacred precincts and the opportunity for continuous worship. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is often the view of the Sahibayn, considering the many blessings of residing in Mecca, but the text does not explicitly state the tarjih.

Key Terms
المجاورة (al-mujawarah): Prolonged residence in Mecca, often with the intention of staying there for an extended period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa’s main reason for considering mujawarah makruh?
A) It is financially unwise
B) It leads to boredom and loss of reverence, and sins are more severe
C) It is forbidden by the Quran
D) It is only disliked if one is a non-resident

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school’s mufta bihi is that prolonged residence in Mecca is recommended, though Imam Abu Hanifa warned of spiritual risks.

Valid Time for Standing at Arafat and the Obligation to Extend
Rulings defining the valid time for standing at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the valid time for standing at Arafat, apply the condition of zawaal, and explain the obligation to extend to after sunset and its consequence.

Core Idea
Standing at Arafat is valid from zawaal to dawn; but if done by day, extension to after sunset is wajib, omitting it requires a dam.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position on the timing of the essential standing (wuquf) at Arafat. It specifies that the valid time begins at zawaal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and ends at dawn of the 10th. The text also addresses the dispute with the Maliki school and explains the obligation to prolong the standing until after sunset when one stands during the day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The standing at Arafat is a rukn (integral) of Hajj. Its omission invalidates the Hajj. However, the text distinguishes between the rukn itself and an additional obligation (wajib) regarding its timing.
2
Determine the valid time according to Hanafi school
The valid time for standing is from zawaal (noon when the sun passes the meridian) on the Day of Arafat (9th Dhul-Hijjah) until dawn (fajr) of the Day of Sacrifice (10th). Standing before zawaal is not counted.
Hanafi is stricter than Maliki who allows from sunrise.
3
Analyze the proof and its implication
The hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafat during the day has completed his Hajj' is cited to show that immediate departure after a daytime stand is sufficient for validity. This proves that the standing itself does not require staying until sunset.
The hadith is ahad, so it yields zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Note the Maliki dispute and the Hanafi response
Malik said the time starts from sunrise. The Hanafi response, implied by the text, is that the ruling is based on the established practice and the hadith's indication, though the hadith does not specify the start time; the start at zawaal is derived from other evidence.
The passage does not detail the Maliki proof but states the difference.
5
Distinguish between validity and the wajib of extension
If one stands during the day, it is wajib to extend the standing until after sunset. Omitting this extension does not invalidate the Hajj but requires a dam (sacrificial animal). If one stands only after sunset (at night), no extension is required.
The dam is for leaving a wajib, not for the rukn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدرك الوقوف بعرفة ما بين زوال الشمس من يوم عرفة، إلى طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر: فقد أدرك الحج. ولو وقف قبل الزوال: لم يُعتد به. وقال مالك: وقت الوقوف من طلوع الشمس من يوم عرفة. قال في «الهداية»: إذا وقف بعد الزوال، فأفاض من ساعته: أجزأه [؟] ساعة من ليل أو نهار عندنا؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من وقف بعرفة نهار: فقد تم حجه». إلا أنه إذا وقف من النهار وجب عليه أن يمد الوقوف إلى بعد الغروب، فإن لم يفعل فعليه دم. وإن وقف بعد الغروب: لم يجب عليه امتداد.
And whoever catches the standing at Arafat between the time of the sun's decline (zawaal) on the day of Arafat and the dawn of the day of sacrifice (yawm al-nahr) has caught the Hajj. And if he stood before zawaal, it is not counted. And Malik said: The time of standing is from sunrise on the day of Arafat. He said in Al-Hidayah: If he stands after zawaal and then departs immediately, it suffices him [؟] a part of the night or day according to us, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever stands at Arafat during the day, his Hajj is complete.' Except that if he stands during the day, he must extend the standing to after sunset; if he does not do so, then a dam is due upon him. And if he stands after sunset, extension is not required upon him.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the time for the essential standing (wuquf) at Arafat. The valid period begins at zawaal (noon when the sun passes the meridian) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah (the Day of Arafat) and ends at the dawn (fajr) of the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr, the Day of Sacrifice). Anyone who stands during this interval has validly performed the Hajj, whether or not they know it is Arafat. The text explicitly states that standing before zawaal does not count, contrary to the Maliki school which permits standing from sunrise. The author then cites Al-Hidayah to clarify that if one stands after zawaal and then immediately departs (without staying until sunset), the standing is still valid according to the Hanafi school, based on the hadith that whoever stands during the day has completed his Hajj. However, if one stands during the day, they must extend their stay until after sunset; if they fail to do so, a dam (sacrificial animal) is required. Conversely, if one stands only after sunset (i.e., at night), there is no requirement to extend until any specific time, so no dam is due for leaving early. This nuanced ruling distinguishes between the validity of the standing and the requirement to prolong it to after sunset when one stands during the day.

Key Terms
الوقوف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi-Arafah): The essential rite of standing at Arafat during the Hajj, which is a rukn; its valid time is from zawaal on 9th Dhul-Hijjah to dawn of the 10th.
يوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the Day of Sacrifice, when pilgrims slaughter animals and perform tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum required time for the standing at Arafat to be valid in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunrise to sunset
B) Zawaal to dawn of Yawm al-Nahr
C) Afternoon until midnight
D) The entire day of Arafat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets a precise timing for wuquf and distinguishes between the validity of the rukn and the wajib of extension, with a dam required for omitting the latter.

Ruling on Passing Through Arafat While Asleep or Unconscious
Ruling that passing through Arafat while asleep etc. suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the validity of standing at Arafat for a pilgrim who is asleep, unconscious, or unaware, and identify the condition that makes it valid.

Core Idea
Physical presence at Arafat fulfills the rukn of standing, even without awareness, if ihram was entered consciously.

This passage addresses a common concern: does a pilgrim need to be consciously aware of standing at Arafat for Hajj to be valid? The Hanafi school answers clearly: the rukn is physical presence, not awareness. However, this is conditional upon having entered ihram in a conscious state. Let us explore the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
The ruling is that passing through Arafat while asleep/unconscious/ignorant suffices for the standing. The object is the rukn of standing at Arafat.
The pilgrim does not need to be aware of the place or the act while present.
2
Locate the essential condition
The condition is that the pilgrim must have entered ihram while conscious. Without this, the ruling does not apply. The passage states: 'This is if he entered ihram while conscious, then he became unconscious at the time of standing.'
Consciousness at the start of ihram is required, but not during the standing itself.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The proof is an analogy to fasting: just as sleeping through a fast does not invalidate it because the rukn (abstention) occurred, so too unconsciousness does not invalidate standing because the rukn (presence) occurred.
The asl (original case) is the fasting person sleeping; the far' (new case) is the unconscious pilgrim at Arafat.
4
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the rukn is achieved by physical action or presence, and awareness is not a condition for the rukn's validity.
The commentator states: 'What is the rukn has occurred, namely the standing, and unconsciousness and sleep do not prevent it.'
5
Confirm the consensus
The commentator notes that this ruling is by consensus (ijma'), indicating its strength and universality among the schools.
This reinforces the reliability of the position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اجتاز بعرفة وهو نائم أو مغمى عليه، أو لم يعلم أنها عرفة: أجزأه ذلك عن الوقوف. * قوله: (ومن اجتاز بعرفة وهو نائم أو مغمى عليه، أو لم يعلم أنها عرفة: أجزأه ذلك عن الوقوف). وهذا إذا أحرم وهو مُفيقٌ، ثم أغمي عليه حال الوقوف: فإنه يجزئه الوقوف، إجماعاً؛ لأن ما هو الركن قد وجد، وهو الوقوف، فلا يمنعه الإغماء والنوم، كركن الصوم، وإنما اختل منه النية، وهي ليست بشرط لكل ركن.
And whoever passes through Arafat while he is asleep or unconscious, or does not know that it is Arafat, that suffices him for the standing. His statement: (And whoever passes through Arafat while he is asleep or unconscious, or does not know that it is Arafat, that suffices him for the standing). This is if he entered ihram while conscious, then he became unconscious at the time of standing: then the standing suffices him, by consensus, because that which is the rukn has occurred, namely the standing, and unconsciousness and sleep do not prevent it, like the rukn of fasting, and only the intention was missing, and intention is not a condition for every rukn.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof by qiyas (analogy). It addresses a situation where a pilgrim passes through the area of Arafat while asleep, unconscious, or ignorant of the place. The ruling is that this still counts as the required standing at Arafat. The commentator elaborates: This ruling applies only if the pilgrim entered ihram while conscious; then, if they become unconscious or sleep during the standing period, the standing is valid by consensus (ijma'). The reasoning is that the actual rukn — being present at Arafat — has been fulfilled. The commentator draws an analogy to the rukn of fasting: if a fasting person sleeps the entire day, the fast is still valid because the rukn (abstention) is present, even though intention (niyyah) might be compromised. Similarly, for standing at Arafat, intention is not a prerequisite for every rukn; the physical presence suffices. This clarifies that the essential element is the physical presence in Arafat, not the awareness or intention during the standing.

Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of an act of worship; its omission invalidates the act. For Hajj, the standing at Arafat is a rukn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is necessary for the standing at Arafat to be valid if the pilgrim is unconscious?
A) The pilgrim must be conscious at the time of standing
B) The pilgrim must have made ihram while conscious
C) The pilgrim must have made a specific intention for standing
D) It is never valid if unconscious

Key Takeaway
The standing at Arafat, as a rukn of Hajj, is fulfilled by physical presence in the area, even without awareness, provided the pilgrim entered ihram while conscious.
