Wuquf at Arafah in Exceptional States: Asleep, Unconscious, or Unaware
Ruling on validity of wuquf in exceptional states and its time extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of wuquf for a pilgrim who is asleep, unconscious, or unaware, and identify when a dam is required.

Core Idea
Wuquf is valid even if unconscious; but day wuquf requires extension to sunset or a dam.

This lesson clarifies that the rukn of wuquf is fulfilled simply by being present at Arafah, regardless of awareness. However, timing matters: daytime wuquf imposes an additional obligation to extend until nightfall. The passage from al-Quduri and its commentary from al-Hidayah provide the ruling and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exceptional states
The text explicitly mentions sleep, unconsciousness, and ignorance of Arafah. Note that all three share the absence of active awareness during the wuquf.
These states do not affect the validity of the rukn.
2
Determine the core ruling for these states
The matn states that passing through Arafah in any of these states suffices for wuquf. This is the general Hanafi position.
The commentary adds that this applies if the pilgrim entered ihram while conscious.
3
Distinguish between day and night wuquf
The commentary from al-Hidayah introduces a time distinction: if wuquf occurs after zawal (daytime), it is wajib to extend the standing until after sunset. If one stands after sunset, no extension is needed.
This distinction is based on the hadith cited.
4
Identify the consequence of failing to extend
If one stands during the day and departs before sunset, a dam (blood sacrifice) becomes wajib. This is a wajib compensation, not an invalidation.
The wuquf remains valid (sahih).
5
Analyze the rationale for unconsciousness
The commentary explains by consensus (ijma) that unconsciousness does not prevent the validity of wuquf because the pillar (presence) is realized. Analogy is made to fasting where intention is not required for every moment.
Intention (niyyah) is not a condition for every rukn in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اجتاز بعرفة وهو نائم أو مغمى عليه، أو لم يعلم أنها عرفة : أجزأه ذلك عن الوقوف . قال في «الهداية» (۱) : إذا وقف بعد الزوال، فأفاض من ساعته: أجزأه ساعة من من ليل أو عندنا؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من وقف بعرفة نهار : فقد تم حجه»(۲). إلا أنه إذا وقف من النهار وجب عليه أن يمد الوقوف إلى بعد الغروب، فإن لم يفعل فعليه دم. : وإن وقف بعد الغروب: لم يجب عليه امتداد. * قوله : (ومن اجتاز بعرفة وهو نائم أو مغمى عليه، أو لم يعلم أنها عرفة : أجزأه ذلك عن الوقوف). وهذا إذا أحرم وهو مُفيقٌ، ثم أغمي عليه حال الوقوف: فإنه يجزئه الوقوف، إجماعاً؛ لأن ما هو الركن قد وجد، وهو الوقوف، فلا يمنعه الإغماء والنوم، كركن الصوم، وإنما اختل منه النية، وهي ليست بشرط لكل ركن.
Whoever passes through Arafah while asleep, unconscious, or unaware that it is Arafah, that suffices him for standing. He said in al-Hidayah: If he stood after zawal (noon) and then departed immediately, a single hour from night or day suffices him according to us, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever stands at Arafah during the day, his Hajj is complete.' However, if he stood during the day, it is obligatory on him to extend the standing until after sunset; if he does not do so, then he owes a dam. And if he stood after sunset, extension is not obligatory. His statement: 'Whoever passes through Arafah while asleep or unconscious or unaware that it is Arafah, that suffices him for standing.' And that is if he assumed ihram while conscious, then lost consciousness during the standing: then the standing suffices him, by consensus; because the pillar has been realized, which is standing, and unconsciousness and sleep do not prevent it, like the pillar of fasting. Only the intention is missing, and it is not a condition for every pillar.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of wuquf at Arafah in exceptional circumstances. The matn states that if a person passes through Arafah while asleep, unconscious, or unaware that it is Arafah, his wuquf is valid. The commentator then expands by quoting al-Hidayah: if one stands after zawal and departs immediately, even a single hour of standing suffices, whether by night or day, based on the hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah during the day, his Hajj is complete.' However, if one stands during the day, it is wajib to extend the standing until after sunset; failure to do so requires a dam. If one stands after sunset (i.e., at night), extension is not required. The commentary further explains that the ruling for the unconscious person applies when he assumed ihram while conscious and then lost consciousness during the wuquf; this is valid by ijma because the actual pillar (wuquf) is present, and unconsciousness does not invalidate it, similar to fasting where the pillar is abstinence. The missing intention does not harm because niyyah is not a condition for every pillar according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; it is a rukn of Hajj.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep) required as compensation for certain violations in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim stands at Arafah during the day and departs immediately without waiting until sunset?
A) The Wuquf is invalid and Hajj must be repeated.
B) The Wuquf is valid but a dam is required.
C) The Wuquf is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The pilgrim must perform a second wuquf at night.

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafah is a rukn that can be fulfilled even when asleep, unconscious, or unaware, but day wuquf obligates extension to sunset.

Woman's Ihram: Head Covered, Face Uncovered
Ruling on woman's exceptions in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptions to the woman's ihram rulings (covering head, uncovering face) and apply the Hanafi proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
A woman in ihram must cover her head but uncover her face — because her face is the locus of her ihram.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar clarifies the unique rulings for women in ihram. While a woman is generally like a man in all Hajj rituals, two key differences emerge: she must keep her head covered (since it is awrah) and she must uncover her face (based on the Prophet's hadith). Understanding these exceptions is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Recognise that the matn states 'the woman in all that is like the man' — she is addressed by the same obligations and prohibitions of ihram except where specified.
This establishes the baseline: women follow men's rules unless an exception is proven.
2
Note the first exception: head covering
The matn says 'except that she does not uncover her head.' The commentary explains this is because the head is awrah and ihram does not permit exposing awrah.
Therefore, women may wear stitched garments, khimar, and khuffs — normally prohibited for men.
3
Understand the rationale for head covering
The head is considered awrah for a woman; ihram does not remove the obligation to cover awrah. Thus, covering the head becomes wajib during ihram.
This is a key difference from men, who must expose their heads.
4
Note the second exception: face uncovering
The matn says 'and she uncovers her face.' The commentary cites the hadith 'Ihram al-mar'ah fi wajhiha' — the ihram of a woman is in her face.
This indicates that covering the face would violate the state of ihram.
5
Examine the proof for face uncovering
The hadith is a sahih (though ahad) narration. The Hanafi school takes it as a proof that the face is not to be covered during ihram.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is interpret this hadith differently, allowing face covering with a light veil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرأةُ في جميع ذلك كالرجل، غير أنها لا تكشف رأسها، وتكشف وجهها . * قوله: (والمرأة في جميع ذلك : كالرجل)؛ لأنها مخاطبة كالرجال. * قوله: (غير أنها لا تكشف رأسها) ؛ لأنها عورة، والإحرام لا يبيح كشف العورات، ولهذا قالوا إن لها أن تلبس المخيط والخمار والخُفَّ. قوله: (وتكشف وجهها؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إحرام المرأة في وجهها».
And the woman in all that is like the man, except that she does not uncover her head, and she uncovers her face. His statement: 'The woman in all that is like the man' because she is addressed like men. His statement: 'except that she does not uncover her head' because it is awrah, and ihram does not permit uncovering awrah, and for this reason they said she may wear stitched garments, a khimar, and khuffs. His statement: 'and she uncovers her face' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The ihram of a woman is in her face.'
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage clarifies the woman's rulings during ihram. The matn states that a woman is like a man in all rulings of Hajj, except two matters: she does not uncover her head, and she uncovers her face. The commentary explains: she is like a man because she is also mukallaf (legally responsible). She does not uncover her head because it is awrah, and ihram does not permit exposing awrah. Therefore, she may wear stitched garments, a khimar (headcover), and khuffs (socks) — which are normally prohibited for men. She uncovers her face based on the hadith 'The ihram of a woman is in her face', meaning her face is not to be covered during ihram, but also not exposed to non-mahram — the correct understanding is that she should not wear a niqab or burqa, but she is not required to cover her face in ihram.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered; for a woman in ihram, the head is awrah.
مخيط (makhīt): Stitched garments; normally prohibited for men in ihram but permitted for women.
إحرام المرأة في وجهها (Ihram al-mar'ah fi wajhiha): Hadith indicating that a woman's ihram is observed in her face; thus her face must remain uncovered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cover it with a niqab.
B) Uncover it at all times.
C) Uncover it but may cover it when non-mahram pass by.
D) Cover it with a burqa.

Key Takeaway
A woman in ihram must cover her head (awrah) and uncover her face (based on hadith); covering the face intentionally requires fidyah.

Prioritizing Wuquf Over Isha Prayer When Time is Tight
Ruling on conflict between Isha prayer and going to Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim fears missing wuquf due to Isha prayer and explain the reasoning based on hardship (mashaqqa) and the Quranic principle of ease.

Core Idea
When extreme hardship threatens Hajj, the fard prayer may be abandoned to prevent greater harm.

What happens when two religious obligations collide? In Hajj, a pilgrim may find that the time for Isha prayer is so tight that performing it would cause him to miss wuquf at Arafah — the essential pillar of Hajj. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that prioritizes avoiding immense hardship over the more emphatic obligation of prayer. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the proof from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting obligations
Recognize that the pilgrim faces a choice between performing the fard Isha prayer and proceeding to Arafah for wuquf. Both are obligatory, but one must yield.
The conflict is between a daily prayer (fard) and the essential pillar of Hajj (wuquf).
2
State the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the pilgrim should leave the prayer and go to Arafah. This is the operative ruling.
The ruling is clear: prayer is sacrificed for Hajj in this exceptional case.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The text argues that although the prayer is more emphatic (ākad), missing Hajj entails extreme hardship (mashaqqa ʿaẓīma) — requiring wealth, distant travel, and a full year before makeup. Missing a prayer is easily made up.
The key factor is the gravity of hardship (mashaqqa) in making up Hajj vs. prayer.
4
Examine the proof
The author cites Quran 2:185, 'Allah intends ease for you,' to justify prioritizing the option that avoids severe hardship. This is a general principle supporting the ruling.
The dalil is a Qur'anic verse, but the ruling itself is derived through istihsan or consideration of hardship.
5
Consider cross-madhhab perspective
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) might argue that the prayer cannot be abandoned because it is a confirmed fard. The Hanafi position relies on the concept of extreme hardship overriding the normal hierarchy.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ضاق على المحرم وقت العشاء، بحيث لا يتسع لأربع ركعات، ولم يصل العشاء، وكان يخشى إذا اشتغل بالصلاة: فاته إتيان عرفة للوقوف فإنه يترك الصلاة ويذهب إلى عرفة ؛ لأن أداء فرض الصلاة وإن كان آكد : ففي فوات الحج مشقةٌ عظيمة؛ لأنه يحتاج في قضائه إلى مال خطير، وسفر بعيد، وعام قابل بخلاف فوت الصلاة، فإن قضاءها يسير، والله تعالى يقول: ﴿يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ . البقرة / ١٨٥ .
And if the time of Isha becomes tight for the muhrim such that it does not accommodate four rak'ahs, and he has not prayed Isha, and he fears that if he occupies himself with prayer, he will miss going to Arafah for standing, then he leaves the prayer and goes to Arafah; because although performing the obligatory prayer is more emphatic, in missing Hajj there is great hardship; for he would need significant wealth, distant travel, and a future year to make it up, unlike missing the prayer, for its makeup is easy. And Allah Almighty says: 'Allah intends ease for you' (al-Baqarah 2:185).
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical conflict: a pilgrim (muhrim) finds that the time for Isha prayer is so short that it does not allow for four rak'ahs, and he has not yet prayed Isha. If he prays first, he will miss wuquf at Arafah. The ruling is that he should abandon the prayer and proceed to Arafah. The reasoning is that although the fard prayer is more emphatic (akad) in principle, the hardship of missing Hajj is immense: making it up requires significant wealth, a long journey, and waiting a full year. In contrast, the makeup of a missed prayer is easy and can be done quickly. The author supports this by quoting the Quranic principle of ease (yusr). This ruling reflects the Hanafi approach of balancing obligations with maslaha and preventing hardship.

Key Terms
آكد (ākad): More emphatic or strongly emphasized; prayer has a greater emphasis normally.
قضاء (qaḍā’): Making up a missed religious duty (prayer or Hajj).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because the pilgrim is not in a state of wudu.

Key Takeaway
When Hajj is at stake, the Hanafi school permits sacrificing the fard prayer to avoid extreme hardship, based on the Quranic principle of ease.

Proxy Ihram for the Unconscious: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Disciples
Intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy ihram for unconscious

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on proxy ihram for an unconscious person and explain why Abu Hanifa differs from his two disciples.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, a proxy can pronounce ihram for the unconscious, because necessity overrides the requirement of personal intention.

This lesson explores a unique intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Hajj for a person who loses consciousness before ihram. Abu Hanifa holds that if someone else enters ihram on his behalf and he is brought through all the rites, his Hajj is valid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree, insisting on personal intention. We will examine the grounds of this disagreement and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling that proxy ihram suffices for the unconscious person.
The text says 'أجزأه عند أبي حنيفة' – it suffices according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples) disagree; they consider proxy ihram invalid.
The text says 'خلافاً لهما' – contrary to the two.
3
Analyze the underlying reasoning
Understand why Abu Hanifa allows proxy: unconsciousness prevents personal intention, so necessity permits delegation. The Sahibayn require personal intention as essential.
The passage does not give explicit reasoning, but later Hanafi works elaborate.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Learn that despite the dispute, the relied-upon position in the school is Abu Hanifa's view for ease and to avoid hardship.
Authorities like al-Marghinani prefer Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أغمي عليه قبل الإحرام، فأهل عنه أحدٌ من رفقته أو غيرهم، ووقفه بالمناسك كلها: أجزأه عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لهما. كذا في «الوجيز».
And if a person becomes unconscious before ihram, and one of his companions or someone else pronounces ihram on his behalf, and he performs the standing at all the rites, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). So in al-Wajiz.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of ihram for an unconscious person. The author cites the ruling from al-Wajiz. According to Abu Hanifa, if a person loses consciousness before entering ihram, and someone else (a companion or any other person) pronounces the intention and talbiyah on his behalf, and the unconscious person is then brought to all the rites of Hajj (including 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, etc.), his Hajj is valid and sufficient. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree, holding that it is not valid because ihram requires personal intention and consciousness. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as the mujtahidun consider the intention of the proxy sufficient when the person cannot form his own intention due to unconsciousness. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah (the known books of Imam Muhammad) and is cited in later works like al-Wajiz.

Key Terms
أهل عنه (ahalla 'anhu): To pronounce the talbiyah or enter the state of ihram on behalf of someone else.
أغمي عليه (ughmiya 'alayhi): To become unconscious, lose consciousness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For Abu Hanifa, a proxy's ihram suffices for the unconscious person, providing a practical concession; the two disciples require personal intention, but the preferred view follows Abu Hanifa.

Prioritizing 'Arafah over 'Asr Prayer When Time Is Tight
Ruling on prioritizing 'Arafah over 'Asr prayer when time is insufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the 'Asr prayer to attend 'Arafah when time is insufficient and explain the legal reasoning (istihsan) based on the Quranic principle of ease.

Core Idea
When obligations conflict, choose the one whose repetition causes greater hardship.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario on the day of 'Arafah: a pilgrim has not yet prayed 'Asr, but the time is so short that praying four rak'ahs would cause him to miss the standing at 'Arafah. The Hanafi school rules that he should leave the prayer and go to 'Arafah, making up the prayer later. This ruling is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) based on the Quranic verse 'Allah intends ease for you'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting obligations
Recognize that the pilgrim is faced with two obligatory acts: praying 'Asr (fard) and standing at 'Arafah (wajib in Hanafi). Determine which one takes priority under the given circumstances.
Both are obligations, but the urgency of the situation creates a conflict.
2
Apply the condition of time constraint
Check if the remaining time for 'Asr is insufficient to perform four rak'ahs (i.e., less than the time needed to pray with its prerequisites). If there is enough time, there is no conflict and he must pray first.
The condition is that the time 'does not accommodate four rak'ahs'.
3
Assess the hardship of missing each obligation
Compare the consequences: missing 'Asr requires a simple make-up (qada) later the same day. Missing the standing at 'Arafah voids the Hajj for that year, requiring repetition the next year with significant expense and travel.
The ruling emphasizes 'mashaqqah 'azimah' (great hardship) in repeating Hajj.
4
Derive the ruling via istihsan
Apply the principle that when obligations conflict, the one whose omission causes greater hardship is prioritized. This is an exception (istihsan) to the general rule that prayer takes precedence.
The Quranic proof: 'Allah intends ease for you' (2:185).
5
Conclude the ruling
The pilgrim leaves the 'Asr prayer and proceeds to 'Arafah. He must make up the missed prayer after the sunset or later.
This ruling is specific to 'Asr on the day of 'Arafah; other prayers do not override the standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ضاق على المحرم وقت العشاء، بحيث لا يتسع لأربع ركعات، ولم يصل العشاء، وكان يخشى إذا اشتغل بالصلاة: فاته إتيان عرفة للوقوف فإنه يترك الصلاة ويذهب إلى عرفة ؛ لأن أداء فرض الصلاة وإن كان آكد : ففي فوات الحج مشقةٌ عظيمة؛ لأنه يحتاج في قضائه إلى مال خطير، وسفر بعيد، وعام قابل بخلاف فوت الصلاة، فإن قضاءها يسير، والله تعالى يقول: ﴿يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ . البقرة / ١٨٥ .
And if the time for 'Asr prayer becomes too tight for a pilgrim, such that it does not accommodate four rak'ahs, and he has not prayed 'Asr, and he fears that if he occupies himself with prayer, he will miss coming to 'Arafah for the standing, then he leaves the prayer and goes to 'Arafah. Because even though performing the obligatory prayer is more emphatic, in missing Hajj there is great hardship, as he needs significant wealth, long travel, and a future year for its make-up, unlike missing the prayer, whose make-up is easy. And Allah Almighty says: 'Allah intends ease for you' [Quran 2:185].
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage discusses a conflict between an obligatory prayer ('Asr) and the obligation of standing at 'Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. The ruling is that if the time for 'Asr is so short that performing four rak'ahs would cause the pilgrim to miss the appointed time for 'Arafah (which ends at sunset for the standing), the pilgrim should forego the prayer and proceed to 'Arafah. The reasoning: missing Hajj requires repeating it the following year, which entails considerable expense and travel, while missing 'Asr can be made up easily the same day after sunset. The proof is the Quranic principle that Allah intends ease. In Hanafi fiqh, this is an application of istihsan: the easier path is chosen due to the hardship involved. Note that this ruling is specific to the 'Asr prayer on the day of 'Arafah; other prayers do not override the standing. Also, if there is enough time to pray before going, one must pray.

Key Terms
وقت العشاء (waqt al-'asha'): In this context, 'al-'asha' refers to the 'Asr (afternoon) prayer, as it is the prayer that has four rak'ahs and is performed on the day of 'Arafah before sunset.
ضاق عليه الوقت (daaqa 'alayhi al-waqt): The time becomes too tight for performing the prayer within its proper time window without missing another obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray 'Asr quickly with tayammum
B) Leave the prayer and go to 'Arafah
C) Combine 'Asr with Zuhr
D) Perform Hajj without standing at 'Arafah

Key Takeaway
When obligations conflict, the Hanafi school prioritizes the one whose omission causes greater hardship, based on the Quranic principle of ease.

Women's Exemptions and Obligations in Hajj
List of women's exemptions and obligations in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific modifications for women in Hajj and explain the underlying principle of 'awrah and modesty.

Core Idea
Women perform Hajj like men, but with modifications to preserve modesty and avoid uncovering 'awrah.

The general ruling for Hajj applies equally to men and women, but the Sharī‘ah has prescribed certain modifications for women to maintain modesty and prevent fitnah. This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah lists these unique exemptions and obligations, ranging from what she wears to how she performs ṭawāf and sa‘y.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Start with the opening statement: the woman is like the man in all obligations of Hajj. This establishes equality in the core acts.
The modifications are exceptions, not a separate set of rules.
2
List the Specific Modifications
Work through each ruling: head covered, face uncovered, no loud talbiyah, no raml, no running between green markers, no shaving, no touching the Black Stone in front of men, and the permission to drape cloth over the face.
Each modification stems from the principle of ‘awrah or avoiding fitnah.
3
Connect Each Ruling to Its Rationale
For each modification, note the reason given in the text: head is ‘awrah, voice is ‘awrah, raml risks uncovering, running is for showing strength, shaving is disfigurement, touching men is prohibited.
The hadīth 'Ihrām al-mar’ah fī wajhihā' is the key proof for uncovering the face.
4
Identify the Exception for Face Covering
Recognise that a woman may let a cloth down over her face without letting it touch the skin, as it is akin to shading with a howdah.
This is not a contradiction; it distinguishes between covering that touches (prohibited) and loose draping (permitted).

And the woman in all of that is like the man, except that she does not uncover her head, and she uncovers her face.

* His saying: 'And the woman in all that is like the man' because she is addressed (obligated) like men. * His saying: 'except that she does not uncover her head' because it is 'awrah, and ihram does not permit uncovering 'awrah, and for this they said that she may wear stitched garments, a headcover, and khuffs. His saying: 'and she uncovers her face' due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The ihram of a woman is in her face' (i.e., she must not cover it with a niqab, but may drape cloth without touching).

And she does not raise her voice with the talbiyah.
And she does not do raml in the tawaf, and she does not run between the two green markers.
And she does not shave her head, but she trims.
And if she lets something down over her face while making it (the cloth) touch it, it is permissible, because it is like the shade of the howdah (i.e., shading herself).

* His saying: 'And she does not raise her voice with the talbiyah' because her voice is 'awrah.
His saying: 'And she does not do raml in the tawaf' because it is not safe that some part of her body might become uncovered.
* His saying: 'And she does not run between the two green markers' i.e., she does not run in the middle of the valley, because that is for showing strength, and the woman is not of its people.
His saying: 'And she does not shave her head but trims' because shaving for women is disfigurement, like shaving the beard for men.

And she does not touch the Black Stone in the presence of men, because she is prohibited from touching them. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage collects the specific rulings that differentiate a woman's Hajj from a man's. The general principle is that women are obligated just as men are, but they have exemptions and modifications due to their nature and the rulings on 'awrah. (1) Head covering: The woman does not uncover her head during ihram because it is 'awrah; she may wear sewn garments, a khimar (headscarf), and khuffs (leather socks). (2) Face: She uncovers her face because the Prophet said 'The ihram of a woman is in her face,' meaning she must not cover it with a niqab or burqa that touches the skin, but she may drape cloth over it without contact. (3) She does not raise her voice in talbiyah because her voice is considered 'awrah (i.e., not permissible to raise in a way that attracts non-mahram men). (4) She does not do raml (quick walking with short steps) in tawaf and does not run between Safa and Marwah (specifically between the green markers in the valley), as raml is a display of strength intended for men. (5) She does not shave her head but only trims a portion (about the length of a fingertip) because shaving for women is considered mutilation (muthlah). (6) She does not touch the Black Stone (for istilam) in the presence of non-mahram men because she is forbidden from physical contact with them. Additionally, she may cover her face loosely with a cloth that does not touch the skin, as this is akin to shading oneself in a howdah. These rulings are consistent across the Hanafi school and are based on the principle of safeguarding 'awrah and modesty.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makhīṭ): Sewn garments; items of clothing that are stitched, such as shirts, trousers, or gowns.
الخمار (al-khimār): A head cover or veil that covers the head and neck, but not the face.
الرمل (al-raml): A brisk, marching-like walk with short steps, performed by men in the first three circuits of tawaf.
الميلين الأخضرين (al-mīlayn al-akhḍarayn): The two green markers placed at the middle of the valley between Safa and Marwah, indicating the area where men run (sa'y with raml).
التقصير (al-taqsīr): Trimming the hair by cutting a small portion (about a fingertip's length) from the tips.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women perform Hajj like men but with specific modifications to preserve modesty, and violating any wajib modification requires fidyah.

Specific Rulings for Women in Hajj: Modesty and Ritual Acts
States specific prohibitions and permissions for women performing Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five specific Hanafi rulings for women in Hajj (talbiyah voice, raml, sa'y pace, hair cutting, face covering, and touching the Black Stone) and explain the reasoning behind each prohibition or permission.

Core Idea
Women in Hajj must observe heightened modesty: no raised voice, no brisk walking, no head shaving, and no contact with men.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar details several special rules for women during Hajj. While many rituals are similar for men and women, the Hanafi school emphasizes modesty and avoidance of fitna. The rulings cover voice in talbiyah, gait in tawaf and sa'y, hair cutting, face covering, and proximity to the Black Stone. Each is based on a clear rationale rooted in the preservation of 'awrah and prevention of disfigurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition on raising voice in talbiyah
Read the text: she should not raise her voice. Note the reason: her voice is 'awrah. In Hanafi fiqh, a woman's voice is considered 'awrah (to be concealed) when non-mahram men may hear. Hence, she recites talbiyah in a low voice.
Men are encouraged to raise their voice in talbiyah; this contrast highlights the gender-specific ruling.
2
Understand the prohibition of raml in tawaf
Raml (brisk, proud walking) is a sunnah for men in the first three rounds of tawaf. For women, it is prohibited because it may expose parts of her body. The ruling aims at covering and modesty.
Raml in sa'y (between the two green milestones) is similarly prohibited for women.
3
Differentiate between shaving and trimming hair
Men are encouraged to shave their heads (or trim). For women, shaving is prohibited because it is considered mutilation (muthla). Women may only trim a small amount (qasr) to signify completion of ihram.
The comparison is made to shaving a man's beard, which is also prohibited as mutilation.
4
Recognize the permissibility of face covering
A woman in ihram may drape a cloth over her face (even if it touches her skin) as long as it is not tied like a niqab. This is analogous to seeking shade in a howdah, which is allowed.
In the Hanafi school, the face is not part of the 'awrah during ihram, but covering it is permissible if done loosely.
5
Identify the restriction on touching the Black Stone
Women should not approach the Black Stone to touch or kiss it if non-mahram men are present, because physical contact with them is prohibited. She may point from a distance.
This ruling is based on the general prohibition of unnecessary contact between non-mahram men and women.

Source Text

And if she drapes something over her face and it touches it, it is permissible, because it is like seeking shade with the howdah. * His statement: (And she should not raise her voice in talbiyah) because her voice is 'awrah. His statement: (And she should not do raml in tawaf) because it is not safe that something of her body might be uncovered by that. * His statement: (And she should not hasten between the two green milestones) meaning she should not do raml in the bottom of the valley, because that is for showing strength, and women are not among its people. His statement: (And she should not shave her head but should trim) because shaving for women is mutilation, like shaving the beard for men. Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, specifying rules for women in Hajj. [1] Raising voice in talbiyah: Since a woman's voice is considered 'awrah (something to be concealed) in the Hanafi school, she should not raise it—unlike men who are encouraged. [2] Raml in tawaf: Raml is walking with a brisk, proud gait, which may expose a woman's body; hence prohibited for her. [3] Hastening between the green milestones (in sa'y): Similarly, the fast pace (raml) in the valley of sa'y is for showing strength, which women are not required to do. [4] Shaving head: For men, shaving is a sunnah; for women, it is considered muthla (disfigurement), akin to shaving a man's beard. Women may only trim a small amount. [5] Draping cloth over face: A woman may cover her face with a cloth even if it touches her skin, as it is like seeking shade in a howdah (which is allowed). [6] Touching the Black Stone: In the presence of non-mahram men, she should not approach the Black Stone to avoid physical contact. All rulings aim at modesty and avoiding fitna.

Key Terms
ترمل (tarmulu): Walking briskly with a proud gait in tawaf or sa'y; specific to men.
مثلة (muthla): Disfigurement or mutilation; shaving a woman's head is considered akin to mutilation.
سدلت (sadaltu): To let down or drape a cloth over the face without tying it.

Key Takeaway
Women in Hajj must observe additional rules of modesty: they cannot raise their voice, do raml, shave their head, or touch the Black Stone in men's presence; they may cover their face loosely and must trim their hair instead of shaving.

Superiority of Qiran in the Hanafi School
Defines Qiran and presents Hanafi position with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds Qiran superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad, and evaluate the opposing proofs from the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
Qiran is superior because the Prophet himself performed it, as narrated by Anas ibn Malik.

This passage opens the chapter on Qiran by defining the term and establishing its superiority. It then presents a three-way inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafis hold Qiran best, Shafi'is prefer Ifrad, and Malikis prefer Tamattu'. The Hanafi proof is a direct hadith of Anas ibn Malik showing the Prophet performing Qiran. You will learn how this dalil establishes the Hanafi position and how the school answers opposing arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the explicit statement in the text: 'al-Qiranu 'indana afdalu min al-tamattu'i wa al-ifradi' (Qiran with us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad).
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Shafi'i holds Ifrad best; Maliki holds Tamattu' best. Note the difference: they disagree on which type is most meritorious.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The proof is the hadith of Anas: the Prophet (ﷺ) pronounced talbiyah for both 'umrah and hajj together. The phrase 'yuhillu bihima jamii'an' indicates simultaneous ihram, i.e., Qiran.
The hadith is a direct observation, not inferred from other actions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to opponents
The Hanafi response is implicit: the direct narration of Anas takes precedence over interpretations of the farewell hajj or the order to companions.
The text does not elaborate further; the strength lies in the explicit prophetic practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a Hanafi seeking maximum reward should choose Qiran, while a Shafi'i would choose Ifrad, and a Maliki would choose Tamattu'. All are valid but differ in preference.

باب القرآن
القرآن عندنا أفضل من التمتع والإفراد.
باب القرآن
هو مشتق من : اقتران الشيء بالشيء، في اللغة.
وفي الشرع: عبارة عن الجمع بين إحرام العمرة والحج وأفعالهما في سفر واحد. وكان ينبغي أن يُقدِّم القرآن؛ لأنه أفضل، إلا أنه قدم الإفراد؛ من حيث الترقي من الواحد إلى الاثنين، والواحد قبل الاثنين. قال رحمه الله: (القرآنُ عندنا أفضل من التمتع، والإفراد).

Chapter of Qiran
Qiran with us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad.
Chapter of Qiran
It is derived from the pairing of one thing with another, in language. And in sacred law, it is an expression for combining the ihram of 'umrah and hajj and their actions in one journey. And it was proper that he should present Qiran first because it is better, but he presented Ifrad first, from the perspective of ascending from one to two, and one is before two. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Qiran with us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad.' And al-Shafi'i said: Ifrad is better. And Malik said: Tamattu' is better than Qiran. For us (the proof): what Anas ibn Malik narrated: I was holding the reins of the she-camel of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and she was chewing her cud, and her saliva was flowing on my shoulder, while he was pronouncing talbiyah for both of them together.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Qiran in the commentary on al-Quduri. It first defines Qiran: linguistically from 'pairing', technically combining the ihram of 'umrah and hajj in a single journey, performing all actions together. The author notes that despite Qiran being superior, the text presented Ifrad first pedagogically, stepping from one to two. The core ruling: in the Hanafi school, Qiran is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad. The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i holds Ifrad best; Imam Malik holds Tamattu' best. The Hanafi proof is a hadith of Anas ibn Malik describing the Prophet (ﷺ) performing Qiran (pronouncing talbiyah for both hajj and 'umrah together). The Hanafis use this to establish Qiran's superiority. The other schools have their own proofs: Shafi'i argues the Prophet performed Ifrad in his farewell hajj; Maliki argues the Prophet ordered his companions to change to Tamattu'. The practical consequence: the Hanafi school recommends Qiran as the best form, while others recommend different forms.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qiran): Combining the ihram of 'umrah and hajj in one journey, performing all actions together.
تمتع (Tamattu'): Performing 'umrah and hajj separately in one journey, with a break of ihram between.
إفراد (Ifrad): Performing hajj alone without 'umrah in the same journey, or 'umrah separately.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Qiran is the superior form of Hajj, established by the Prophet's own practice as narrated by Anas ibn Malik.

Superiority of Qiran over Tamattu' and Ifrad
Ruling with proof on superiority of Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the most virtuous type of Hajj, explain the primary proofs from the Sunnah, and distinguish the correct scope of the comparison.

Core Idea
Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram) is best because of the Prophet's practice, additional sacrifice, and continuous ihram.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the preferred type of Hajj. The text defines Qiran, presents the ruling that it is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad, and supports it with hadith evidence and rational reasoning. It also addresses the differing views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, and clarifies the precise meaning of 'better than Ifrad'.

Guided Path
1
Define Qiran
Understand the linguistic and legal meaning of Qiran as combining the ihram of Umrah and Hajj in one journey with one ihram for both.
The term is derived from 'conjunction'.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school holds that Qiran is better (afdal) than both Tamattu' and Ifrad. This is a ruling of preference, not obligation.
The text says 'القرآن عندنا أفضل من التمتع والإفراد'.
3
Examine the primary proof
Analyze the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: The Prophet (PBUH) performed Hajj and Umrah together, saying 'Labbayk with Hajj and Umrah together'. This shows the practice of Qiran.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections.
4
Understand the additional proofs
Qiran involves an extra ritual (sacrifice) and continuous ihram from the miqat to completion, unlike Tamattu'. The hadith 'أفضل الحج : العَجُ والنَّج' (the best Hajj is loud voice and flowing blood) supports Qiran.
Sacrifice is required in Qiran but optional in Ifrad and Tamattu'.
5
Clarify the scope of superiority
The statement 'better than Ifrad' means better than performing Hajj and Umrah separately (each with its own ihram), not better than performing only one of them. If only one is performed, Qiran is unanimously better.
Analogous to four rak'ats being better than two, but only when comparing both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
القرآن عندنا أفضل من التمتع والإفراد.
باب القرآن
هو مشتق من : اقتران الشيء بالشيء، في اللغة.
وفي الشرع: عبارة عن الجمع بين إحرام العمرة والحج وأفعالهما في سفر واحد. وكان ينبغي أن يُقدِّم القرآن؛ لأنه أفضل، إلا أنه قدم الإفراد؛ من حيث الترقي من الواحد إلى الاثنين، والواحد قبل الاثنين. قال رحمه الله: (القرآنُ عندنا أفضل من التمتع، والإفراد).
وقال الشافعي : الإفراد أفضل.
وقال مالك: التمتع أفضل من القرآن.
لنا: ما روى «أنس بن مالك قال: كنت آخذاً بزمام ناقة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهي تَقْصَعُ بجرتها، ولعابها يسيل على كتفي، وهو يقول : لبيك بحجة وعمرة معاً». كذا في «النهاية».
ولأن في القران زيادة نسك، وهو إراقة الدم، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أفضل الحج : العَجُ والنَّج».
ولأن فيه استدامة الإحرام بهما من الميقات إلى أن يفرغ منهما، ولا كذلك التمتع. والمراد من قوله : أفضل من الإفراد أي من إفراد كل واحد منهما بإحرام على حدة، لا أن يكون المراد أن يأتي بأحدهما، لا غير؛ لأنه إذا لم يأت إلا بأحدهما : فالقران أفضل بلا خلاف، إذ لا يشك أحد أن الحج وحده، أو العمرة وحدها: لا يكون أفضل منهما جميعاً.
وهذا كما يقال في صلاة النفل : إن أربعاً أفضل من اثنين عند حنيفة: يُفهم من هذا بأن الإتيان بأربع بتسليمة واحدة: أفضل من الإتيان بهن بتسليمتين، أما إذا اقتصر على اثنتين لا غير، فلا خلاف لأحد أن الأربع أفضل. فعلم بهذا: أن قوله : القرآن أفضلُ من الإفراد، أي من إفراد الحج والعمرة بعد الإتيان بهما جميعاً، أما إذا لم يأت إلا بأحدهما: فلا خلاف حينئذ في أن القران يكون أفضل.
Chapter of Qiran. Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad. Chapter of Qiran. It is derived from the conjunction of a thing with a thing, in language. In sacred law: it is an expression for combining the ihram of Umrah and Hajj and their actions in one journey. And it was fitting that he should present Qiran first because it is better, but he presented Ifrad first due to ascending from one to two, and one is before two. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad.' And al-Shafi'i said: Ifrad is better. And Malik said: Tamattu' is better than Qiran. Our proof: what Anas ibn Malik narrated: 'I was holding the reins of the she-camel of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and it was chewing its cud, and its saliva was flowing on my shoulder, and he was saying: Labbayk with Hajj and Umrah together.' Thus in al-Nihayah. And because in Qiran there is an increase of ritual, which is shedding blood (sacrifice). He (peace be upon him) said: 'The best Hajj is the loud voice and the flowing of blood (sacrifice).' And because it involves continuous ihram for both from the miqat until finishing both, and Tamattu' is not like that. And the meaning of his statement 'better than Ifrad' is better than performing each of them separately with a separate ihram, not that the meaning is to perform only one of them; for if one performs only one of them, then Qiran is better without dispute, since no one doubts that Hajj alone or Umrah alone is not better than both together. And this is like what is said about supererogatory prayer: that four is better than two according to Hanifa, meaning that performing four with one taslim is better than performing them with two taslims. But if one restricts to two only, then without dispute four is better. Thus it becomes known that his statement 'Qiran is better than Ifrad' means performing Hajj and Umrah after doing both, whereas if one does only one of them, then there is no dispute that Qiran would be better.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by defining Qiran (القران) linguistically and legally. Linguistically, it means conjunction. Legally, it means combining the ihram for Umrah and Hajj and their actions in one journey. The author notes that logically Qiran should have been presented first because it is better, but the previous chapter presented Ifrad first due to ascending from one to two. The core ruling: according to the Hanafi school, Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram) is superior to both Tamattu' and Ifrad. The author then reports the opposing views: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Ifrad (performing Hajj alone) is best, and Imam Malik holds that Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj with a separate ihram) is best over Qiran. The Hanafi proof is threefold: (1) A hadith in which Anas ibn Malik describes the Prophet (PBUH) saying 'Labbayk with Hajj and Umrah together' while performing Qiran. (2) Qiran involves an additional ritual: sacrificing an animal (دم), and a hadith states that the best Hajj is characterized by loud voice (العج) and flowing blood (الثج). (3) Qiran maintains continuous ihram from the miqat until completion of both rituals, unlike Tamattu'. The author clarifies that 'better than Ifrad' means better than performing each separately, not that Qiran is better than performing only one of the two. If someone performs only Hajj or only Umrah, then Qiran is unanimously better because it includes both acts of worship. The author draws an analogy with supererogatory prayer: four rak'ats with one taslim is better than two, but if one only prays two, then four is clearly better. Thus the comparison is between Qiran and performing both separately, not between Qiran and a single ritual.

Key Terms
قرآن (qiran): Combining the ihram of Umrah and Hajj in one journey with one ihram for both.
إفراد (ifrad): Performing Hajj alone (without Umrah) in a single journey.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then Hajj with two separate ihrams in the same journey, with a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of Hajj is considered the most virtuous?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) They are all equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the most virtuous Hajj type due to the Prophet's practice, additional sacrifice, and continuous ihram, with the understanding that the comparison is with performing both rituals separately, not with a single one.

The Superiority of Qiran over Ifrad: A Qualified Preference
Clarifies the meaning of Qiran's superiority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view that Qiran is better than Ifrad only when both Hajj and Umrah are performed, and support this with the hadith and the analogy from supererogatory prayer.

Core Idea
Qiran is better than Ifrad only when both Hajj and Umrah are performed; not absolutely.

In this passage from the chapter on Qiran, the author clarifies an often-misunderstood statement: 'Qiran is better than Ifrad.' He explains that this superiority is not absolute but conditional—it applies only when the pilgrim intends to perform both Hajj and Umrah. If only one rite is performed, Qiran is obviously better, but that is a different comparison. The author supports this with a prophetic hadith and an analogy to supererogatory prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram). The ruling being discussed is that it is better (afdal) than Ifrad (performing them separately). Note that this is a matter of preference (sunnah ghayr muakkadah), not obligation.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'أفضل الحج العج والثج' (The best Hajj is the one with loud talbiyah and the shedding of blood). He also uses an analogy (qiyas) with supererogatory prayer: four rak'ahs with one taslim are better than two rak'ahs.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari (1534).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith indicates that the best Hajj involves a sacrifice (thaj), which is a required element of Qiran (since Qiran requires a dam). Thus Qiran is described as better. The analogy: just as more prayer is better, more acts of worship (Hajj + Umrah together) are better than separate acts.
4
Note the Crucial Qualification
The phrase 'Qiran is better than Ifrad' means better than performing Hajj and Umrah separately. If a person performs only Hajj or only Umrah, then Qiran is better without dispute because it combines both. But the comparison is not between Qiran and a single rite; it is between Qiran and doing both rites separately.
The author stresses that this is the intended meaning.
5
Distinguish from Tamattu'
The author also notes that Qiran involves continuous ihram from the miqat to the end, unlike Tamattu', which requires a break. This continuity is another reason for its superiority.
This point reinforces the advantage of Qiran.

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiran is a ruling with proof. It clarifies the meaning of the statement that Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is better than Ifrad (performing them separately). If a person performs only Hajj or only Umrah, then certainly Qiran is better because it combines both. The proof includes a hadith about the best Hajj and reasoning by analogy with supererogatory prayer. The author also compares to Tamattu' and notes that unlike Tamattu', Qiran maintains ihram continuously from the miqat.

The Qiran Procedure: Combining Hajj and Umrah in a Single Ihram
Describes Qiran from ihram to Umrah completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the steps of Qiran from ihram to sa'y and explain why Umrah actions are performed first according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, beginning with Umrah actions and remaining in ihram until Hajj.

The Qiran form of Hajj involves entering ihram with the intention for both Umrah and Hajj simultaneously. This lesson explains the exact procedure as described in the Hanafi classical texts, from the ihlal at the miqat to the performance of tawaf and sa'y upon entering Makkah. The commentator also clarifies the reasoning behind the order and notes a variant wording of the intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting action: ihlal (raising voice with talbiyah) for both Umrah and Hajj together at the miqat.
The pilgrim raises his voice (yuhillu) for Umrah and Hajj simultaneously, indicating the combined intention.
Ihlal is the act of entering ihram; the talbiyah is recited after the prayer.
2
Note the niyyah formula: the specific supplication said after the prayer.
The pilgrim says: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Some versions say 'Hajj and Umrah' first.
The commentary discusses the order of mentioning Hajj vs. Umrah, citing Quranic verses.
3
Understand the order upon entering Makkah: tawaf (with raml) followed by sa'y.
Upon entering Makkah, the pilgrim first performs tawaf around the Ka'bah (with raml in the first three circuits), then prays two rak'ahs, and then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah.
This tawaf is the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) for Umrah; it is followed by sa'y which is wajib for Umrah.
4
Recognize that these actions constitute the Umrah portion.
The tawaf and sa'y are the essential actions of Umrah. The pilgrim remains in ihram until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah for the Hajj rituals.
The pilgrim does not shave or exit ihram after Umrah; he remains in ihram for Hajj.
5
Appreciate the reason for precedence: the author explains why Umrah is mentioned first.
The commentator states that Umrah is mentioned first because Allah gave it precedence in Quran 2:196, and because its actions come before Hajj actions.
This reasoning is a Hanafi textual operation (takhrij al-manat) based on the sequence in the ritual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفةُ القِرآن : أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحج معاً من الميقات، ويقول عَقِيبَ الصلاة : اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني . فإذا دخل مكة : ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته. وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة. قوله: (وصفة القرآن أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحج معاً من الميقات). قدم العمرة؛ لأن الله تعالى قدمها بقوله: ﴿فَمَن تَمَنَّعَ بِالْعُمرة إلى الحج . البقرة / ١٩٦ ، ولأن أفعالها مقدمة على أفعال الحج. * قوله : (ويقول عَقِيبَ الصلاة: اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي) : أي اقطع موانعهما عني. * قوله: (وتقبلهما مني). وفي بعض النسخ: اللهم إني أريد الحج والعمرة: بتقديم ذكر الحج؛ تبركا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ . البقرة / ١٩٦. فمن مال إلى الأول قال : لأن أفعال العمرة مقدمة على أفعال الحج. * قوله: (فإذا دخل مكة: ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمل في الثلاثة الأول منها)؛ لأنه طواف بعده سعي، ويصلي ركعتي الطواف، (ويمشي فيما بقي على هنته). قوله: (ويسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة.
The description of Qiran: that one raises his voice with talbiyah for Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat, and says after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then when he enters Makkah, he begins by performing tawaf around the House seven circuits, walking briskly (raml) in the first three of them, and walking normally in the rest. Then he performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of Umrah. (The commentator says): His statement: 'The description of Qiran is that one raises his voice with talbiyah for Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat.' He mentioned Umrah first because Allah the Exalted gave it precedence in His statement: 'Then whoever performs Umrah before Hajj...' (Quran 2:196), and because its actions come before the actions of Hajj. His statement: 'And says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me' means remove obstacles from me. His statement: 'And accept them from me.' In some copies: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah' giving precedence to Hajj, seeking blessing from Allah's statement: 'And complete Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (Quran 2:196). Whoever inclines to the first says: because the actions of Umrah precede the actions of Hajj. His statement: 'Then when he enters Makkah, he begins by performing tawaf around the House seven circuits, walking briskly in the first three of them' because it is a tawaf followed by sa'y, and he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, 'and walks in the rest normally.' His statement: 'Then he performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah, and these are the actions of Umrah.'
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement describing the procedure for Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). It details the niyyah (intention) after prayer, entering Makkah, tawaf with raml in the first three circuits, sa'y, and explains the reasoning behind mentioning Umrah before Hajj. The author also notes a variant in the wording of the talbiyah. The procedure follows the Hanafi school: the Qiran pilgrim performs the actions of Umrah first, then remains in ihram until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah for Hajj.

Key Terms
الإهلال (al-ihlal): To raise one's voice with talbiyah at the miqat, indicating entering the state of ihram.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movements during the first three circuits of tawaf.
السعي (al-sa'y): Walking seven times between the hills of Safa and Marwah after tawaf.

Hajj al-Qiran: Procedure and Rulings on Order
Describes the procedure and secondary rulings of Hajj al-Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the procedure of Hajj al-Qiran and apply the Hanafi ruling on changing the order of tawafs and sa'y, including the intra-Hanafi disagreement on dam.

Core Idea
The qarin performs 'Umrah first, then Hajj; altering the order does not require a dam, but is considered wrong.

This lesson breaks down the description of Hajj al-Qiran from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah. We will walk through the correct sequence of rituals, the prohibition of shaving between the two, and what happens if the pilgrim performs the rituals out of order. A key intra-Hanafi dispute about the need for a sacrificial animal (dam) when the order is changed is also clarified.

Guided Path
1
Define Qiran and the intention
Identify the meaning of Qiran: combining 'Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram from the miqat. Note the recommended wording after prayer.
The author mentions two versions of the intention; the preferred one gives precedence to 'Umrah.
2
Describe the actions of 'Umrah for the qarin
Upon entering Makkah, the qarin first performs tawaf (with raml in first three circuits), two rak'ahs, then sa'y. This completes the 'Umrah.
Raml is done because this tawaf is followed by sa'y.
3
Describe the actions of Hajj for the qarin
After the 'Umrah, the qarin performs tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) and sa'y for Hajj, without shaving in between.
Shaving between 'Umrah and Hajj would be a violation of the Hajj ihram.
4
Examine the ruling on altered order
If the qarin performs Hajj tawaf before 'Umrah tawaf, or combines tawafs, the acts are still valid but he has done wrong. No dam is required by consensus within the Hanafi school.
The text explains the reasoning of Abu Hanifa vs. the two disciples.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say taqdim/ta'khir does not require dam as a general principle. Abu Hanifa says tawaf al-qudum is sunnah, so omitting or advancing it does not require dam. Both reach the same conclusion (no dam).
This is a disagreement in rationale, not outcome; the mufta bihi is no dam.

Source Text

باب القرآن

وصفةُ القِرآن : أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحج معاً من الميقات، ويقول عَقِيبَ الصلاة : اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني . فإذا دخل مكة : ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته.
وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة.
قوله: (وصفة القرآن أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحج معاً من الميقات). قدم العمرة؛ لأن الله تعالى قدمها بقوله: ﴿فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ﴾ [البقرة/196]، ولأن أفعالها مقدمة على أفعال الحج.
* قوله : (ويقول عَقِيبَ الصلاة: اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي) : أي اقطع موانعهما عني.
* قوله: (وتقبلهما مني). وفي بعض النسخ: اللهم إني أريد الحج والعمرة: بتقديم ذكر الحج؛ تبركا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ﴾ [البقرة/196].
فمن مال إلى الأول قال : لأن أفعال العمرة مقدمة على أفعال الحج. * قوله: (فإذا دخل مكة: ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُل في الثلاثة الأول منها)؛ لأنه طواف بعده سعي، ويصلي ركعتي الطواف، (ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته). قوله: (ويسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة.

ثم يطوف بعد السعي طواف القدوم، ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة للحج، كما بينا في حق المفرد.

ولا يحلق بين العمرة والحج ؛ لأن ذلك جناية على إحرام الحج. فإن حلق بعد طواف العمرة وسعيها، وبين طواف القدوم: فعليه دمان، ولا يحل من عمرته.
وفي هذا تصريح بأنه تقع جناية على الإحرامين جميعاً. فإن طاف القارنُ وسعى أولاً للحج ، ثم طاف وسعى للعمرة: فالأول للعمرة، والثاني للحج.
فإن طاف طوافين معاً لحجته ،وعمرته، ثم سعى بعده سعيين: أجزأه ؛ لأنه أتى بالمستحق عليه، وقد أساء بتأخير سعي العمرة، وتقديم طواف القدوم عليه، ولا دم عليه إجماعاً.
أما عندهما: فظاهر؛ لأن التقديم والتأخير في المناسك عندهما لا يوجب الدم.
وأما عند أبي حنيفة: فطواف القدوم سنة، وتركه قطعاً لا يوجب الدم، فتقديمه أولى. كذا في «الهداية».
Chapter of Qiran. The description of Qiran is: that one raises the talbiyah for 'Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat, and says after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend 'Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, doing raml in the first three of them, and walking normally in the remaining. And he performs sa'y after that between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of 'Umrah. His statement: (The description of Qiran is that one raises the talbiyah for 'Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat). He gave precedence to 'Umrah because Allah gave it precedence in His saying: 'Then whoever performs 'Umrah [and then] Hajj...' [2:196], and because its actions precede the actions of Hajj. * His statement: (And he says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend 'Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me) i.e., remove their obstacles from me. * His statement: (And accept them from me). And in some copies: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and 'Umrah' with mentioning Hajj first, seeking blessing from the saying of the Most High: 'And complete Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' [2:196]. Those who inclined to the first said: because the actions of 'Umrah precede the actions of Hajj. * His statement: (Then when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, doing raml in the first three of them) because it is a tawaf after which there is sa'y, and he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, (and walks normally in the remaining). His statement: (And performs sa'y after that between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of 'Umrah.) Then after the sa'y he performs the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) and sa'y between Safa and Marwah for Hajj, as we explained regarding the mufrid. And he should not shave (his head) between 'Umrah and Hajj, because that is an offense against the ihram of Hajj. If he shaves after the tawaf and sa'y of 'Umrah, and before the tawaf of arrival, then upon him are two animal sacrifices (dam), and he does not become free from his 'Umrah. In this there is an explicit statement that an offense occurs against both ihrams. If the qarin performed tawaf and sa'y first for Hajj, then performed tawaf and sa'y for 'Umrah, then the first is for 'Umrah and the second for Hajj. If he performed two tawafs together for his Hajj and his 'Umrah, then performed two sa'ys after them, it suffices him because he has done what is required of him, and he has done wrong by delaying the sa'y of 'Umrah and bringing forward the tawaf of arrival before it, but there is no animal sacrifice upon him by consensus. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent, because advancing and delaying in the rituals according to them does not necessitate an animal sacrifice. As for according to Abu Hanifa, the tawaf of arrival is a sunnah, and its abandonment absolutely does not necessitate an animal sacrifice, so advancing it is more appropriate. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah explains the rulings of Hajj al-Qiran, the combination of 'Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram. The commentator begins by stating the description (sifah) of Qiran: the pilgrim raises the talbiyah for both 'Umrah and Hajj from the miqat, and after a prayer (typically after a two-rak'ah prayer or after the obligatory prayer) he verbalizes his intention. The author notes that 'Umrah is mentioned first in the intention because Allah gave it precedence in the Quran (2:196) and because the actions of 'Umrah (tawaf and sa'y) precede the actions of Hajj. Some versions of the intention mention Hajj first, seeking blessing from the verse 'And complete Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah'. The preferred order is to mention 'Umrah first, as its actions come first. Upon entering Makkah, the qarin first performs 'Umrah: tawaf with raml in the first three circuits (since this tawaf is followed by sa'y), then sa'y between Safa and Marwah. After completing the 'Umrah, he performs the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) and then sa'y for Hajj — the same as a mufrid (one performing only Hajj) would do. However, the qarin does not shave his head between 'Umrah and Hajj because that would violate the ihram of Hajj. If he shaves after the tawaf and sa'y of 'Umrah but before the tawaf of arrival, he owes two dam (animal sacrifices) and his 'Umrah remains incomplete; this shows the offense affects both ihrams. The passage then addresses cases of altered order. If the qarin performs tawaf and sa'y first for Hajj then for 'Umrah, the first is counted for 'Umrah and the second for Hajj — the order is corrected. If he performs both tawafs together and then both sa'ys together, it is sufficient (ajza'ahu) because he has ultimately performed all required acts, but he has done wrong (asa'a) by delaying the 'Umrah sa'y and advancing the tawaf of arrival. However, no dam is required by consensus (ijma'an). The commentator then explains the intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), advancing and delaying rituals does not necessitate a dam in any case, so no dam here. According to Abu Hanifa, the tawaf of arrival is a sunnah, not wajib, so omitting it entirely does not require a dam; thus performing it early is even more permissible (awla). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that no dam is required, as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A person performing Hajj al-Qiran (combining 'Umrah and Hajj with one ihram).
رمل (raml): A brisk walk with shoulder movement (chest out) during tawaf, done by men in the first three circuits when the tawaf is followed by sa'y.
طواف القدوم (ṭawāf al-qudūm): Tawaf of arrival performed by a pilgrim upon entering Makkah, sunnah according to Abu Hanifa.
دم (dam): An animal sacrifice required as a penalty (jaza') for certain violations during Hajj or 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling (hukm) on shaving the head after the 'Umrah tawaf and sa'y but before the tawaf al-qudum during Hajj al-Qiran?
A) It is permissible and the 'Umrah is valid.
B) It requires one dam and the 'Umrah is valid.
C) It requires two dam and the 'Umrah is not completed.
D) It invalidates the entire Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The qarin may change the order of tawafs and sa'y without dam, but shaving between 'Umrah and Hajj incurs two dam and leaves the 'Umrah incomplete until Hajj tawaf is performed.

Sequence of Tawaf and Sa'y and Shaving Prohibition for Qarin
Stating the correct order of tawaf and sa'y and the prohibition of shaving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of tawaf and sa'y for a Qarin and explain the ruling and expiation for shaving between Umrah and Hajj.

Core Idea
Shaving between Umrah and Hajj is a crime against two ihrams, requiring two dams and leaving Umrah incomplete.

The Qarin pilgrim combines Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram. This passage clarifies the sequence of rituals after entering Mecca: first complete the Umrah tawaf and sa'y, then perform Tawaf al-Qudum, and finally the Hajj sa'y. It also rules on shaving in the interim, which is prohibited and incurs a serious penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pilgrim type and rulings
Recognise that the text addresses the Qarin pilgrim. Understand that the Qarin performs Umrah first, then Hajj, without a break in ihram.
2
Trace the correct sequence
Note the order: Umrah tawaf → Umrah sa'y → Tawaf al-Qudum → Hajj sa'y. This is the recommended sequence for the Qarin.
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah for the non-resident pilgrim.
3
Identify the prohibition and its reason
The text states shaving between Umrah and Hajj is a crime (jinaayah) against the ihram of Hajj. Shaving here is haram.
4
Apply the consequence of violation
If the Qarin shaves after Umrah tawaf/sa'y but before Hajj Tawaf, he owes two dams and his Umrah is not completed; he remains in ihram.
Two dams because the act violates both the Umrah and Hajj ihrams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يطوف بعد السعي طواف القدوم، ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة للحج، كما بينا في حق المفرد. ثم يطوف بعدها طواف القدوم، ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة، كما بينا في حق المفرد). ولا يحلق بين العمرة والحج؛ لأن ذلك جناية على إحرام الحج. فإن حلق بعد طواف العمرة وسعيها، وبين طواف القدوم: فعليه دمان، ولا يحل من عمرته. وفي هذا تصريح بأنه تقع جناية على الإحرامين جميعاً.
Then he performs Tawaf al-Qudum after the Sa'y, and performs Sa'y between Safa and Marwa for Hajj, as we explained regarding the Mufrid. Then he performs after that Tawaf al-Qudum, and performs Sa'y between Safa and Marwa, as we explained regarding the Mufrid. And he does not shave between Umrah and Hajj, because that is a crime against the ihram of Hajj. If he shaves after the Tawaf of Umrah and its Sa'y, and before Tawaf al-Qudum, then he owes two dams, and he is not released from his Umrah. And in this is an explicit statement that a crime is committed against both ihrams.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the correct sequence of rituals for a Qarin pilgrim. After completing Umrah (tawaf and sa'y), the Qarin should perform Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf) and then Sa'y for Hajj. This is the recommended order. The text then prohibits shaving (halq) between the Umrah and Hajj rituals, because that would be a violation of the ihram for Hajj. If one shaves after Umrah's tawaf and sa'y but before the Hajj tawaf, he commits a crime against both ihrams (the Umrah ihram and the Hajj ihram). As a result, he must offer two dams (blood sacrifices) as expiation, and his Umrah is not considered completed—he remains in ihram until he performs the remaining rituals. The phrase 'لا يحل من عمرته' means he does not exit the ihram of Umrah, so he must still complete Umrah properly.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca; for a Qarin, it is performed after the Umrah tawaf and sa'y, before the Hajj sa'y.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (slaughtering a sheep, cow, camel, or a share) required as expiation for certain violations of ihram.
جناية (jinaayah): A crime or transgression against the sanctity of ihram; here, shaving is considered a crime against the ihram of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must not shave between Umrah and Hajj; doing so violates both ihrams, necessitating two dams and leaving the Umrah incomplete.

No Dam for Qarin Reversing Tawaf Order
Ruling on a Qarin who performs Hajj tawaf before Umrah tawaf and the case of two tawafs together.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Qarin who performs Hajj tawaf before Umrah tawaf and explain the intra-madhhab reasoning for no dam.

Core Idea
Reversing tawaf order for a Qarin is valid but disliked; no dam required by consensus.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj: a Qarin who performs the tawaf of Hajj before the tawaf of Umrah, or performs both tawafs together. The source explains that the acts are valid, but the pilgrim has done wrong (asaa) by violating the preferred order. However, no compensatory sacrifice (dam) is owed. The lesson also unpacks the intra-Hanafi debate on why no dam is necessary, showing how different principles lead to the same conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Qarin performing Hajj tawaf before Umrah tawaf (or performing both tawafs together). The ruling is that it suffices (ajza'ah) but is makruh (asaa) and no dam is required.
The text uses 'أجزأه' (it suffices) and 'أساء' (he did wrong).
2
Understand the correction mechanism
If he performs tawaf and sa'y first for Hajj, then later for Umrah, the first set is reassigned to Umrah and the second to Hajj. This is because the intention at ihram is to combine both, so the order is retroactively corrected.
The text says 'فالأول للعمرة، والثاني للحج'.
3
Analyze the two scenarios
Scenario A: He performs one tawaf/sa'y set for Hajj then another for Umrah. Scenario B: He performs both tawafs together then both sa'ys. In both, the outcome is the same: valid, but blameworthy, no dam.
The text covers both scenarios with the same conclusion.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa argues no dam because Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, so omitting it entirely wouldn't require dam; advancing it is even less problematic. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that any advancement or delay in rituals does not incur dam. Despite different reasons, they agree on the ruling.
The text explicitly contrasts 'عندهما' (the two) and 'عند أبي حنيفة'.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
All Hanafi imams agree no dam, so the operative ruling is no dam. The text claims consensus ('إجماعاً') on this specific case.
The mufta bihi is clear despite the ikhtilaf in reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن طاف القارنُ وسعى أولاً للحج، ثم طاف وسعى للعمرة: فالأول للعمرة، والثاني للحج. فإن طاف طوافين معاً لحجته، وعمرته، ثم سعى بعده سعيين: أجزأه؛ لأنه أتى بالمستحق عليه، وقد أساء بتأخير سعي العمرة، وتقديم طواف القدوم عليه، ولا دم عليه إجماعاً. أما عندهما: فظاهر؛ لأن التقديم والتأخير في المناسك عندهما لا يوجب الدم. وأما عند أبي حنيفة: فطواف القدوم سنة، وتركه قطعاً لا يوجب الدم، فتقديمه أولى. كذا في «الهداية».
If the Qarin performs tawaf and sa'y first for Hajj, then performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah, then the first are for Umrah and the second are for Hajj. If he performs two tawafs together for his Hajj and Umrah, then performs two sa'ys afterward, it suffices him, because he has fulfilled what was required of him, and he has done wrong by delaying the sa'y of Umrah and advancing Tawaf al-Qudum over it, and there is no dam upon him by consensus. As for the two, it is apparent, because advancement and delay in rituals according to them do not necessitate dam. As for Abu Hanifa, Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah, and leaving it absolutely does not necessitate dam, so advancing it is even more [permissible]. Thus in Al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a Qarin performs the rituals out of order. First scenario: if he performs tawaf and sa'y first intending Hajj, then performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah, the first tawaf/sa'y are assigned to Umrah and the second to Hajj. This is because the intention at the start of ihram is to combine both, so the order is corrected. Second scenario: if he performs both tawafs together followed by both sa'ys, this is valid but he has committed a makruh act by delaying the sa'y of Umrah and advancing the Hajj tawaf. However, no dam is required, and the text claims consensus (إجماعاً) on no dam in this specific case. The dispute arises in the reasoning: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), any advancement or delay in rituals does not incur dam. According to Abu Hanifa, Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah, so omitting it entirely would not require dam, and advancing it is even less problematic. Thus, the mufta bihi is that no dam is owed. The source cited is Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): Here, Tawaf al-Qudum is classified as sunnah (recommended but not obligatory), so omitting it does not incur dam.
إجماعاً (ijma'an): By consensus; the text claims that all scholars agree there is no dam in this case.
أساء (asaa): He did wrong; indicates the action is makruh (disliked) though not requiring compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a Qarin performs two tawafs together first and then two sa'ys, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid and he must repeat both.
B) It suffices, but he has done wrong and owes a dam.
C) It suffices, but he has done wrong and owes no dam.
D) It is invalid and he owes a dam for each.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin may reverse or combine tawaf and sa'y without incurring dam, but it is disliked and should be avoided.
