Dam al-Qiran: Animal, Preference, and Order Penalty
Specifying animals, preference, and order penalty for dam al-qiran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permitted animals for dam al-qiran, explain the preference for more meat, and apply Abu Hanifa's ruling on delaying slaughter relative to shaving and rami.

Core Idea
Delay in prescribed order for dam al-qiran incurs an additional dam per Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from Al-Jundi details the sacrificial animal for a Qarin, the preference based on meat quantity, and the intra-Hanafi dispute over order violations. You will learn which animals suffice, what is better, and the ruling if the Qarin shaves before slaughtering or slaughters before throwing the jamrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify permitted animals
List the animals that can be used for dam al-qiran: a sheep, cow, camel, or a seventh of a cow or camel.
A seventh of a cow or camel is sufficient; it does not have to be a whole animal.
2
Understand the preference
Between a seventh of a camel and a whole sheep, whichever gives more meat is better because it benefits more poor people.
This is based on the principle of maximizing benefit to the needy.
3
Recognize the prescribed order
The correct sequence is: throw jamrah, then slaughter, then shave. Shaving before slaughter or slaughter before rami violates the order.
The prescribed order is an obligation according to Abu Hanifa.
4
Note Abu Hanifa's ruling
If the Qarin shaves before slaughtering, or slaughters before throwing the jamrah, an additional dam is wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
This is because the order itself is binding.
5
Note the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that no additional dam is required for such order violations, as advancement and delay do not necessitate a dam.
They view the order as recommended, not obligatory.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the school is Abu Hanifa's position, as reported in Al-Jundi.
Thus, a Qarin who delays slaughter incurs an extra dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رمى الجمرة يوم النحر : ذبح شاة، أو بقرة، أو بدنة، أو سُبْعَ بدنة، أو سبع بقرة، فهذا دم القرآن . فإن قيل : فما الأفضل: سبع بدنة، أو شاة؟ قيل: أيهما كان أكثر لحماً فهو أفضل؛ لأن بالكثرة: تكثر منفعة المساكين. فلو أن القارن حَلَقَ أَوَّلاً، ثم ذبح فعليه دم عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن عليه أن يذبح، ثم يحلق. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا شيء عليه؛ لأن التقديم والتأخير عندهما لا يوجب الدم. وكذا لو ذبح قبل الرمي: يجب عليه دم عند أبي حنيفة. كذا في «الجندي».
And when he throws the jamrah on the Day of Sacrifice, he slaughters a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow; that is the Dam of Qiran. If it is said: what is better: a seventh of a camel or a sheep? It is said: whichever has more meat is better, because with abundance the benefit to the poor increases. So if the Qarin shaves first, then slaughters, there is a dam upon him according to Abu Hanifa, because he must slaughter then shave. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: nothing is upon him, because advancement and delay according to them do not necessitate dam. Similarly, if he slaughters before throwing (the jamrah), a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa. Thus in Al-Jundi.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage covers dam al-qiran, the sacrifice required for a Qarin. The animal can be a sheep (shah), a cow (baqarah), a camel (badanah), or a seventh of a camel or cow. This is a complete ram (male sheep) or full animal or share. The text then answers a question: which is better, a seventh of a camel or a whole sheep? The answer: the one with more meat is better because it provides more benefit to the poor. This is a Fiqhi preference based on maslahah. Then there is a second ruling: if the Qarin delays the slaughter until after shaving (halq), according to Abu Hanifa he owes an additional dam because the correct order is slaughter then shave. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, following their principle that advancing or delaying rituals does not incur a dam. Similarly, if he slaughters before throwing the jamrah (rami), Abu Hanifa requires a dam. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's position, as stated in Al-Jundi. This difference only affects the dam penalty; the rituals are still valid.

Key Terms
دم القرآن (dam al-qiran): The blood sacrifice required from a pilgrim performing Hajj al-Qiran as thanksgiving for combining Hajj and Umrah.
رمى الجمرة (rama al-jamrah): Throwing pebbles at the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul-Hijjah); it is a wajib ritual.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head; a rite of exiting ihram for Hajj. For a Qarin, it should be after slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, if a Qarin shaves before slaughtering his dam, what is the ruling?
A) The Qarin must offer an additional dam.
B) No additional dam is required.
C) The Qarin must repeat the shaving after slaughter.
D) The slaughter is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Dam al-qiran must be from specified animals; preference is for more meat; violating the order of slaughter by shaving first or delaying rami incurs an additional dam per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Nature of Dam al-Qiran: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explaining the legal nature of dam al-qiran and the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies dam al-qiran as a thanksgiving sacrifice (dam nusuk) and state the practical consequence regarding eating from it.

Core Idea
Dam al-qiran is a thanksgiving sacrifice, not a penalty, so Hanafis allow eating from it.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the legal nature of the sacrifice required for a pilgrim performing Hajj al-Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah without a break). The Hanafi school views this dam as a voluntary expression of gratitude, akin to the udhiyah, while the Shafi'i school treats it as a compensatory offering for a perceived imperfection. This difference in classification leads to a clear practical divergence: whether the pilgrim may eat from the sacrificed animal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi classification of dam al-qiran: it is a sacrifice of thanksgiving (dam nusuk), not a compensatory penalty (dam jabr).
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i classifies dam al-qiran as dam jabr, a compensatory sacrifice for an imperfection in the pilgrimage.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: the combination of Hajj and Umrah is a departure from the ideal, so a compensation is needed.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the combination is a grace from Allah, not a violation; the dam is wajib as gratitude, so it is like udhiyah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is: Hanafis permit eating from the dam, Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وهذا دمُ القرآن، وهو دم نسك عندنا، شكراً لله تعالى على توفيق الجمع بين العبادتين، لا دمُ جَبرٍ، حتى يجوز الأكل منه عندنا؛ لأنه وجب شكراً الله تعالى، لا لارتكاب محظور، كالأضحية. وعند الشافعي: دم جبر، حتى لا يجوز الأكل منه عنده.
His statement: 'And this is the Dam of Qiran, and it is a sacrifice (dam nusuk) according to us, as thanksgiving to Allah Almighty for enabling the combination of the two acts of worship, not a dam of compensation (dam jabr), so that it is permissible to eat from it according to us, because it became obligatory as thanksgiving to Allah Almighty, not for committing a prohibited act, like the udhiyah. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a dam of compensation (dam jabr), so that it is not permissible to eat from it according to him.'
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage clarifies the legal nature of dam al-qiran. The Hanafi school holds that this dam is a 'dam nusuk' – a sacrifice of devotion and thanksgiving (shukr) for Allah's grace in enabling the pilgrim to combine Hajj and Umrah in one journey. Because it is not a penalty for any sin or violation (muharramat), the pilgrim is permitted to eat from it, similar to the udhiyah (sacrificial animal) on Eid. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that dam al-qiran is a 'dam jabr' – a compensatory sacrifice to make up for an imperfection in the pilgrimage. Consequently, according to the Shafi'is, it is not permissible for the pilgrim to eat from this sacrifice; rather, it must be given entirely in charity. The practical difference (thamarah) is whether the pilgrim can consume any of the meat. The Hanafi position, as stated here, permits it.

Key Terms
دم نسك (dam nusuk): A sacrifice offered as an act of devotion and thanksgiving; not a penalty.
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory sacrifice required for omissions or violations in Hajj; one may not eat from it.
شكراً (shukran): Thanksgiving; the dam is an expression of gratitude for the ability to combine two worships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on dam al-qiran?
A) Hanafis require a camel; Shafi'is require a sheep.
B) Hanafis allow eating from it; Shafi'is do not.
C) Hanafis require it before rami; Shafi'is after.
D) Hanafis consider it optional; Shafi'is consider it obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits eating from dam al-qiran because it is a thanksgiving sacrifice (dam nusuk), not a compensatory penalty (dam jabr).

The Qiran Sacrifice: Thank-Offering or Expiatory?
Explains the ruling on Qiran sacrifice and its nature as a thank-offering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi classification of the qiran sacrifice as a thank-offering (dam nusk) and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view as expiatory (dam jabr), including the practical consequence of permissibility to eat the meat.

Core Idea
The qiran sacrifice is a thank-offering for combining rites, not a penalty — hence it is permissible to eat from it.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah addresses the blood offering (dam) required from a pilgrim performing qiran (combining hajj and umrah). While the act is wajib, its nature is debated: the Hanafi school considers it a devotion (nusk) offered in thanks, analogous to the udhiya sacrifice, while the Shafi'i school views it as an expiatory offering (jabr). This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
Determine that the dam is wajib upon the qarin after throwing the pebble on the Day of Sacrifice. Note the specified animals: a sheep, cow, camel, or a seventh of a camel/cow.
This sacrifice is specific to the qarin mode of hajj.
2
Analyze the Hanafi talil for dam nusk
The dam is wajib as thanksgiving for combining the two acts of worship, not for a prohibited act. The evidence includes analogy (qiyas) to the udhiya sacrifice, which is also a thank-offering and permissible to eat.
The key phrase: 'شكراً لله تعالى على توفيق الجمع بين العبادتين'.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on order
Abu Hanifa requires an extra dam if the pilgrim shaves before sacrificing or slaughters before throwing; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not. Later tarjih follows the latter view.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the nature of the dam but its consequences for sequence violations.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i position and thamarah al-khilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the dam expiatory (dam jabr), hence prohibits eating from it. The practical difference is whether the meat can be consumed.
Both schools have valid proofs; the difference stems from different premises about the nature of qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رمى الجمرة يوم النحر : ذبح شاة، أو بقرة، أو بدنة، أو سُبْعَ بدنة، أو سبع بقرة، فهذا دم القرآن . قوله: (وإذا رمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر ذبح شاة، أو بدنةً، أو بقرة، أو سُبعَ بدنة، أو سبع بقرة، وهذا دم القرآن). فإن قيل : فما الأفضل: سبع بدنة، أو شاة؟ قيل: أيهما كان أكثر لحماً فهو أفضل ؛ لأن بالكثرة: تكثر منفعة المساكين. فلو أن القارن حَلَقَ أَوَّلاً ، ثم ذبح فعليه دم عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن عليه أن يذبح، ثم يحلق. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : لا شيء عليه؛ لأن التقديم والتأخير عندهما لا يوجب الدم. وكذا لو ذبح قبل الرمي: يجب عليه دم عند أبي حنيفة. كذا في «الجندي». قوله : وهذا دمُ القرآن، وهو دم نسك عندنا، شكراً لله تعالى على توفيق الجمع بين العبادتين، لا دمُ جَبرٍ، حتى يجوز الأكل منه عندنا؛ لأنه وجب شكراً الله تعالى، لا لارتكاب محظور، كالأضحية. وعند الشافعي: دم جبر، حتى لا يجوز الأكل منه عنده.
When one throws the pebble on the Day of Sacrifice: he slaughters a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow, and this is the blood of Qiran. His saying: (And when one throws Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, he slaughters a sheep, or a camel, or a cow, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow, and this is the blood of Qiran). If it is said: What is better: a seventh of a camel or a sheep? It is said: Whichever has more meat is better; because with abundance the benefit of the poor increases. If the qarin shaves first, then slaughters, a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa; because he must slaughter, then shave. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Nothing is due; because precedence and delay according to them do not necessitate the dam. Similarly, if he slaughters before throwing the pebbles: a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa. Likewise in al-Jundi. His saying: And this is the blood of Qiran, and it is a blood of devotion according to us, as thanks to Allah for the success of combining the two acts of worship, not a blood of expiation, so it is permissible to eat from it according to us; because it became obligatory as thanks to Allah, not for committing a prohibited act, like the udhiya. According to al-Shafi'i: it is a blood of expiation, so it is not permissible to eat from it according to him.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah explains the ruling on the blood offering required for the qiran (combining hajj and umrah). It begins by stating the types of animals that can be slaughtered: a sheep, a cow, a camel, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. The author then discusses preference: whichever has more meat is better because it benefits more poor people. Next, the text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the pilgrim shaves before sacrificing, Abu Hanifa requires a dam because the correct order is sacrifice then shave, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no penalty for this reordering. The same applies to slaughtering before throwing the pebbles. The main point is the nature of this dam: the Hanafi school views it as a blood of devotion (shukr) offered in thanks for successfully combining the two rites, similar to udhiya (sacrifice), and therefore it is permissible to eat from it. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i considers it a blood of expiation (jabr) for some deficiency, and thus it cannot be eaten. This is a key difference between the schools.

Key Terms
دم القرآن (dam al-quran): The blood offering required from a pilgrim performing qiran (combining hajj and umrah)
دم نسك (dam nusk): A sacrifice offered as an act of devotion and gratitude, like the udhiya
دم جبر (dam jabr): A sacrifice offered to compensate for a deficiency or violation of a prohibition in the rites
القارن (al-qarin): The pilgrim who combines hajj and umrah with one ihram

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is a fine for delaying the shaving.

Key Takeaway
The qiran sacrifice is a thank-offering (dam nusk) in the Hanafi school, permissible to eat, unlike the Shafi'i view which treats it as expiatory.

Substitute Fasting for the Qiran Sacrifice
Details the substitute fasting for the Qiran sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions, timing, and consequences of substitute fasting (sawm badal) for a qarin who cannot afford the hady.

Core Idea
If you cannot afford the Qiran sacrifice, fast three days ending on Arafah — miss that window and only the blood suffices.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the Hanafi ruling for a pilgrim performing Qiran who cannot afford the required sacrificial animal. The Qur'an (2:196) prescribes fasting three days as an alternative, but the jurists detail precise conditions: the fast must be performed during Hajj, the last day must be the Day of Arafah, and intention must be made at night. The text also clarifies what happens if the fast is missed or the pilgrim later becomes able to sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
The passage begins with the ruling for a qarin who cannot afford the sacrificial animal: he must fast three days during Hajj. Recognise that the fast is a substitute (badal) for the wajib hady.
2
Determine the timing conditions
The fast must be performed during Hajj, with the last day being the Day of Arafah. Note that it may be done before the 7th of Dhul Hijjah only if the pilgrim has entered ihram for Umrah. The preferred time is the day before Tarwiyah, Tarwiyah, and Arafah.
Intent at night is required, like other expiatory fasts.
3
Analyse the consequences of missing the fast
If the three days are missed until the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr), only the blood (dam) suffices. The text elaborates: if the pilgrim cannot afford the hady and performs tahallul, two dams may be required.
Also consider what happens if the pilgrim becomes able to afford the hady during the fast: the hady becomes obligatory and the fast is void.
4
Apply the ruling to edge cases
The passage addresses scenarios: if the pilgrim finds the hady after shaving but before completing the substitute fast, no hady is needed. Understand the principle that the ruling of the substitute does not change after tahallul.
This reflects the Hanafi preference (ta'khir) to delay the fast hoping to become able to sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يكن له ما يذبح : صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، آخرها يوم عرفة. فإن فاته الصوم حتى أتى يوم النحر : لم يُجْزِه إلا الدم . قوله: (فإن لم يكن له ما يذبح صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، آخرها يوم عرفة). ولا يجوز صومها إلا بنية من الليل، كسائر الكفارات. وهو مخيّر في الصوم: إن شاء تابعه، وإن شاء فرقه. ويجوز أن يصوم الثلاثة الأيام قبل يوم السابع من ذي الحجة إذا كان قد أحرم بالعمرة، ولا يجوز قبل إحرام العمرة، ولا بعد يوم عرفة. والأفضل أن يصوم قبل يوم التروية ويوم التروية ويوم عرفة؛ لأن الصوم بدل عن الهدي، فيستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته؛ رجاء أن يقدر على الهدي، كما يُستحب تأخير التيمم إلى آخر الوقت؛ رجاء أن يقدر على الماء. * قوله: (فإن فاته الصوم أي صوم الثلاثة الأيام، (حتى دخل يوم النحر لم يُجزه إلا الدم، أي دم القرآن فإن لم يقدر على الهدي، وتحلل فعليه دمان: دم للقرآن، ودم للتحلل قبل الهدي. وإن قدر على الهدي في خلال صوم الثلاثة، أو بعدها قبل يوم النحر : لزمه الهدي، وسقط عنه حكم الصوم. وإن وَجَدَ الهدي بعد ما حلق، قبل أن يصوم السبعة في أيام الذبح أو بعدها فلا هدي عليه؛ لأن التحلل بعد حصول المقصود بالحلق لا يغير حكم الخلف.
If he does not have what to slaughter: he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the Day of Arafah. If the fast passes him by until the Day of Sacrifice comes, nothing suffices him except the blood. His saying: (If he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the Day of Arafah). It is not permissible to fast them except with an intention from the night, like other expiations. And he has a choice in the fast: if he wishes, he may do them consecutively, and if he wishes, he may separate them. And it is permissible to fast the three days before the seventh of Dhul Hijjah if he has entered ihram for Umrah, and it is not permissible before the ihram for Umrah, nor after the Day of Arafah. The best is to fast the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, Yawm al-Tarwiyah, and Yawm Arafah; because the fast is a substitute for the sacrificial animal, so it is recommended to delay it to the end of its time, hoping that he might be able to afford the sacrificial animal, just as it is recommended to delay tayammum to the end of the time, hoping to find water. His saying: (Then if the fast escapes him, i.e. the fast of the three days, (until the Day of Sacrifice enters, nothing suffices him except the blood, i.e. the blood of Qiran). If he cannot afford the sacrificial animal and he performs the tahallul, then two dams are due: a dam for Qiran and a dam for tahallul before the sacrifice. And if he is able to afford the sacrificial animal during the three-day fast, or after it before the Day of Sacrifice, the sacrificial animal becomes obligatory for him and the ruling of the fast falls away. And if he finds the sacrificial animal after he has shaved, before he fasts the seven days in the days of slaughter or after them, then no sacrificial animal is required upon him; because the tahallul after achieving the goal by shaving does not change the ruling of the substitute.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage details the substitute fasting for a qarin who cannot afford the sacrificial animal. According to the Hanafi school, such a person must fast three days during the Hajj season, with the last day being the Day of Arafah. The intention must be made at night, as with other expiatory fasts. The fast may be performed consecutively or separately. It may be done before the seventh of Dhul Hijjah only if one has already entered ihram for Umrah; otherwise, it is not permitted before that, and not after the Day of Arafah. The preferred time is the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, Yawm al-Tarwiyah, and Yawm Arafah, because delaying is recommended in case one becomes able to afford the sacrifice, analogous to delaying tayammum. If one misses the three-day fast until the Day of Sacrifice, only the blood offering suffices. If one becomes able to afford the animal during the fast or before the Day of Sacrifice, the animal becomes obligatory and the fast is no longer valid. However, if one obtains the animal after having shaved (tahallul) but before completing the seven-day fast (for those who missed the second set), no animal is required because the purpose of tahallul has been achieved.

Key Terms
صوم بدل (sawm badal): Fasting in place of the sacrificial animal for one who cannot afford it
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal offered in Hajj, here the required dam for qiran
تحلل (tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram, typically by shaving or cutting hair

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any three days during Dhul Hijjah.
B) Before the 7th of Dhul Hijjah regardless of ihram.
C) Before the 7th only if in Umrah ihram, otherwise after the 7th ending with Arafah.
D) Anytime after the 7th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
The substitute fast for the Qiran sacrifice must be three days during Hajj ending on Arafah, with night intention; missing the window requires the dam.

Fasting Three Days as Substitute for Hady in Qiran
Ruling on three-day fast as substitute for hady with timing and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the three-day fast as a substitute for hady and apply the ruling when the pilgrim becomes able to sacrifice during the fasting period.

Core Idea
Three-day fast for hady is a substitute – if you can sacrifice, the fast drops; timing ends at Arafah.

In Qiran or Tamattu', if a pilgrim cannot afford a sacrificial animal, the obligation shifts to fasting three days. This lesson examines the exact timing, conditions, and the key rule: the fast is only valid when the pilgrim remains unable to sacrifice. If the means arise before the fast is complete, the obligation reverts to the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting three days as a substitute (badal) for the wajib hady. The ruling is wajib.
The substitute is triggered by inability to sacrifice.
2
List the conditions (shurut)
The fast requires niyyah from the night (like all expiatory fasts) and must be completed within the specified days of Hajj, ending at the day of Arafah.
Fasting before ihram for Umrah is invalid.
3
Understand the timing window
The fast can begin after entering ihram for Umrah (in Qiran/Tamattu') and must end by the day of Arafah. The preferred days are the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, but separation or earlier fasting is allowed.
The ruling allows flexibility.
4
Apply the substitution rule
If the pilgrim becomes able to sacrifice during the fasting period (before the day of Nahr), the fast is dropped and the hady becomes obligatory. If the fast is missed entirely until the day of Nahr, only blood (dam) suffices.
This includes cases where the means appear after some fasts have been completed.
5
Note the preferred practice (sunan)
It is recommended to delay the fast to the last days and to fast consecutively, analogous to delaying tayammum, in hope of being able to sacrifice.
This is not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
فإن لم يكن له ما يذبح : صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، آخرها يوم عرفة. فإن فاته الصوم حتى أتى يوم النحر : لم يُجْزِه إلا الدم .
قوله: (فإن لم يكن له ما يذبح صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، آخرها يوم عرفة).
ولا يجوز صومها إلا بنية من الليل، كسائر الكفارات.
وهو مخيّر في الصوم: إن شاء تابعه، وإن شاء فرقه. ويجوز أن يصوم الثلاثة الأيام قبل يوم السابع من ذي الحجة إذا كان
قد أحرم بالعمرة، ولا يجوز قبل إحرام العمرة، ولا بعد يوم عرفة. والأفضل أن يصوم قبل يوم التروية ويوم التروية ويوم عرفة؛ لأن الصوم بدل عن الهدي، فيستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته؛ رجاء أن يقدر على الهدي،
كما يُستحب تأخير التيمم إلى آخر الوقت؛ رجاء أن يقدر على الماء. * قوله: (فإن فاته الصوم أي صوم الثلاثة الأيام، (حتى دخل يوم النحر لم يُجزه إلا الدم، أي دم القرآن فإن لم يقدر على الهدي، وتحلل فعليه دمان: دم للقرآن، ودم للتحلل قبل الهدي.
وإن قدر على الهدي في خلال صوم الثلاثة، أو بعدها قبل يوم
النحر : لزمه الهدي، وسقط عنه حكم الصوم.
وإن وَجَدَ الهدي بعد ما حلق، قبل أن يصوم السبعة في أيام الذبح
أو بعدها فلا هدي عليه؛ لأن التحلل بعد حصول المقصود بالحلق لا يغير حكم الخلف.
Chapter of Qiran: If he does not have something to sacrifice, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the day of Arafah. If the fast is missed until the day of Nahr, only blood suffices for him. His statement: (If he does not have something to sacrifice, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the day of Arafah). It is not valid to fast them except with intention from the night, like other expiations. He has a choice in fasting: if he wishes, he may fast consecutively, and if he wishes, he may separate them. It is permissible to fast the three days before the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah if he has already entered ihram for Umrah, and it is not permissible before the ihram for Umrah, nor after the day of Arafah. The best is to fast before the day of Tarwiyah, the day of Tarwiyah, and the day of Arafah; because the fast is a substitute for the hady, so it is recommended to delay it to the end of its time, hoping that he might be able to afford the hady, just as it is recommended to delay tayammum to the end of the time, hoping to find water. * His statement: (If the fast is missed, meaning the fast of the three days, until the day of Nahr enters, nothing suffices him except blood, meaning the blood of Qiran. If he cannot afford the hady and he performs tahalul, then he owes two bloods: blood for Qiran and blood for tahalul before the hady. If he is able to afford the hady during the three days of fasting or after them before the day of Nahr, the hady becomes obligatory upon him and the ruling of fasting falls away. If he finds the hady after he has shaved, before he fasts the seven days during the days of slaughter or after them, there is no hady upon him; because tahalul after obtaining the purpose by shaving does not change the ruling of the substitute.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Qiran in the Hanafi fiqh text explains the ruling for a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran who cannot afford the sacrificial animal (hady). The matn states that such a person must fast three days during Hajj, ending on the day of Arafah. The sharh expands by clarifying that these fasts require intention from the night (niyyah min al-layl), like all expiatory fasts. The fasting person has the option to fast consecutively or separately, but the preferred practice is to fast on the days before the day of Tarwiyah, the day of Tarwiyah itself, and the day of Arafah. The reasoning given is that the fast is a substitute (badal) for the hady, so it is recommended to delay it until the end of its time in the hope that one might become able to sacrifice, analogous to the recommendation of delaying tayammum to the end of prayer time. If the fast is missed until the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul-Hijjah), then only a blood sacrifice (dam) is accepted. The commentary then addresses scenarios where the pilgrim finds the means to sacrifice during the fasting period: if the hady is found during the three days or before the day of Nahr, the obligation shifts to the hady and the fast is no longer required. If the hady is found after shaving (tahalul) but before or after fasting the seven days, no hady is due because the purpose (tahalul) has already been achieved through the substitute fasting.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-qiran): The combination of Hajj and Umrah in one ihram with one talbiyah.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered in Hajj as a ritual obligation.
الدم (ad-dam): A blood sacrifice as compensation for missing an obligation or violating ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The day of Arafah
B) The day of Nahr
C) The day of Tarwiyah
D) The seventh of Dhul-Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The three-day fast for hady is a substitute valid only within the period ending at Arafah; if the pilgrim becomes able to sacrifice before the fast is completed, the obligation returns to the sacrifice.

Fasting the Seven Days: In Makkah or After Returning Home?
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on timing of seven-day fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the seven days of fasting may be performed in Makkah after completing Hajj, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the interpretation of 'return' in Qur'an 2:196.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, 'return' means completion of Hajj rituals, not physical travel home.

This passage addresses a practical dispute: a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran who must fast ten days (three during Hajj and seven after). Where can those seven days be performed? The Hanafi school permits fasting them in Makkah after completing the Hajj rituals and after the prohibited days of Tashriq. The Shafi'i school restricts them to after physically returning to one's homeland. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of a single word in the Qur'an: 'return'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The matn says: 'Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family.' Identify the act (seven days of fasting) and the apparent condition (return to family).
The condition is the point of dispute.
2
Locate the dispute
The commentary presents two views: 'according to us (Hanafis), it is permissible to fast them in Makkah after completing Hajj' and 'according to al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible except after returning and arriving at the homeland.'
Note the key phrase 'after completing Hajj' — this is the Hanafi trigger.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is a linguistic interpretation: 'the meaning of 'return' is 'you have completed' (faraghtum) because completion is the cause of returning.' Understand that they take the word 'return' figuratively to mean 'finish the rituals'.
This is a use of majaz (figurative speech) in usul.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i position takes the word literally: 'return' means physical travel back to one's homeland. The fast is conditioned upon that.
This is the default literal interpretation (haqiqah).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a Shafi'i who stays in Makkah after Hajj, the seven days must be postponed until he returns home. For a Hanafi, he can complete them immediately in Makkah (after Tashriq). Understand how this affects the pilgrim's schedule.
This is the critical difference in real-life application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
ثم يصوم سبعة أيام إذا رجع إلى أهله .
وإن صامها بمكة بعد فراغه من الحج : جاز .
قوله : (ثم يصوم سبعة أيام إذا رجع إلى أهله)، يعني بعد ما مضت
أيام التشريق؛ لأن الصوم فيها منهي وليس صوم السبعة [الهدي؟]. كذا قال الجرجاني.
بدلاً عن الهدي، فإنه يجوز صومها مع وجود الهدي.
وإن لم يحلَّ حتى مضت أيام النحر ، ثم وجد الهدي: فصومه تام، ولا هدي عليه؛ لأن الذبح مؤقت بأيام النحر، فإذا مضت: فقد حصل المقصود، وهو إباحة التحلل، فصار كأنه تحلل، ثم وجد الهدي. قوله: (وإن صامها بمكة بعد فراغه من الحج: جاز عندنا)،
بعد مضي أيام التشريق. يعني
وعند الشافعي): لا يجوز، إلا بعد الرجوع، والوصول إلى الوطن؛
لأنه معلق بالرجوع.
ولنا : أن معنى : رجعتم أي فرغتم من أعمال الحج؛ لأن الفراغ سبب
الرجوع إلى أهله، فجاز الأداء بعد وجوب السبب.
Chapter of Qiran: Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family. And if he fasts them in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible. His statement: (Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family), meaning after the days of Tashriq have passed; because fasting on those days is prohibited. And the seven days' fast is not [?] so-and-so said al-Jurjani. as a substitute for the hady, for it is permissible to fast them even if the hady is present. And if he does not perform tahalul until the days of Nahr have passed, then he finds the hady, his fast is complete and no hady is due; because the slaughter is time-bound to the days of Nahr, so when they pass, the purpose has been achieved, which is the permission of tahalul, so it is as if he performed tahalul and then found the hady. His statement: (And if he fasts them in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible according to us), after the days of Tashriq have passed. He means: According to al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible except after returning and arriving at the homeland, because it is conditioned upon return. Our proof: The meaning of 'you return' is 'you have completed' the acts of Hajj, because completion is the cause of returning to his family, so performance is permissible after the cause becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Qiran, addressing the seven days of fasting that are part of the ten-day substitute for the hady. The matn states: 'Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family.' The commentary explains that 'return' means after the days of Tashriq (the three days after Nahr). It also notes a statement from al-Jurjani indicating that the seven-day fast is not a substitute for the hady (perhaps meaning it is an independent obligation that can be performed even if one has the hady). The commentary then discusses a scenario: if the pilgrim does not perform tahalul until after the days of Nahr have passed and then finds a hady, his fast is complete and no hady is due, because the slaughtering opportunity has expired and tahalul is already permitted. The main dispute emerges in the final section: according to the Hanafi school (عندنا), fasting the seven days in Makkah after completing Hajj is permissible (جائز). However, according to al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible except after physically returning to one's homeland (الوطن), because the obligation is conditioned upon return. The Hanafi response interprets the word 'return' (رجعتم) in the Quranic verse (2:196) as meaning 'completion' (فرغتم) of Hajj rituals, not physical return. Since completion is the cause (sabab) for returning, the fast is valid after the cause is present.

Key Terms
الرجوع (ar-ruju'): In this context, interpreted by Hanafis as completion of Hajj acts, not physical return.
أيام التشريق (ayyam at-tashriq): The three days following the day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul-Hijjah).
الوطني (al-watani): One's homeland, the place of residence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Physical arrival at one's homeland.
B) Completion of the Hajj rituals.
C) Departure from Makkah.
D) The beginning of the days of Tashriq.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits fasting the seven days in Makkah after Hajj because 'return' is interpreted as completion of rituals, not physical travel.

Ruling on Qarin Leaving for Arafat Without Entering Makkah
Ruling that a qarin becomes rafid for umrah by going directly to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a qarin who proceeds directly to Arafat without entering Makkah becomes a rejecter of his umrah and explain the consequence.

Core Idea
A qarin who skips Makkah and goes to Arafat nullifies his umrah; his ihram becomes for Hajj only.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of Qiran in Hanafi fiqh. It clarifies the crucial sequence for a pilgrim performing combined Hajj and Umrah: the umrah rites must be performed in Makkah before proceeding to Arafat. Skipping this step invalidates the umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is a qarin (pilgrim performing qiran) who does not enter Makkah but goes directly to Arafat.
The pilgrim intended combined Hajj and Umrah.
2
State the ruling
The qarin becomes raafidan (a rejecter) of his umrah at the moment of standing at Arafat.
The umrah is nullified (batil).
3
Understand the consequence
The umrah is nullified, but the ihram for Hajj remains valid. The pilgrim continues as a mufrid (Hajj only).
He must still complete Hajj.
4
Apply the rule
In practice, a qarin must ensure he enters Makkah, performs tawaf and sa'i of umrah, before proceeding to Arafat.
Otherwise, the umrah is lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
وإن لم يدخل القارن مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات : فقد صار رافضاً
لعمرته بالوقوف،
Chapter of Qiran: And if the qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, he becomes a rejecter of his umrah by the standing (at Arafat).
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This brief ruling from the chapter of Qiran states a critical rule for the pilgrim performing combined Hajj and Umrah (qiran). The essential acts of umrah (tawaf and sa'i) must be performed in Makkah before proceeding to Arafat. If the qarin skips entering Makkah and goes directly to Arafat, his umrah is considered abandoned (raafid: rejecter). The standing at Arafat (al-wuqoof) is a pillar of Hajj, but it does not substitute for the umrah rites. Consequently, he becomes a hajji only (mufrid), and his umrah is nullified. This ruling underscores the importance of performing umrah rites before joining the Hajj in qiran.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qarin): A pilgrim performing combined Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram.
رافضاً (raafidan): One who rejects or abandons; here, the umrah is abandoned by failing to enter Makkah.
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing at Arafat, a pillar (rukn) of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is nullified; he becomes a rejecter of his umrah.
C) He must return to Makkah after Arafat to complete it.
D) It is automatically combined with the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The umrah of a qarin who goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah is nullified; he becomes a hajji only.

Qarin Who Abandons Umrah by Going to Arafat
Ruling on a qarin who abandons Umrah by going to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a qarin becomes rafid of his Umrah and explain the required compensations (dam jabar and qada).

Core Idea
A qarin who stands at Arafat before completing four tawaf circuits abandons his Umrah and owes a compensatory sacrifice.

In Hajj, a qarin combines Umrah and Hajj with a single intention. If he proceeds directly to Arafat without completing his Umrah, a critical question arises: does he still hold qarin status? The Hanafi school provides a precise threshold based on the number of tawaf circuits performed. This lesson clarifies when the Umrah is considered abandoned and what obligations follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the qarin proceeding to Arafat without completing Umrah. The ruling is that if he stands at Arafat before completing four tawaf circuits, he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of his Umrah.
This applies only to qarin/mutamatti'; a mufrid (Hajj only) does not have this ruling.
2
Determine the conditions for rafid status
Two conditions must be met: (1) He has performed fewer than four circuits of Umrah tawaf before proceeding, and (2) he actually stands at Arafat (not merely heads there).
The text explicitly states that mere turning towards Arafat does not make him rafid; only standing does.
3
Identify the consequences
Once rafid: (a) the qiran sacrifice is cancelled, (b) he owes a compensatory dam (dam jabar, not to be eaten), and (c) he must make up the Umrah after the days of tashriq.
If he performed four or more circuits, he remains qarin, owes the qiran sacrifice, and completes the remaining tawaf and sa'y after ziyarah.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The correct view from Abu Hanifa is that only standing at Arafat makes one rafid, not merely intending or heading. Some transmissions suggested otherwise, but the relied-upon position is as stated.
The commentator provides an analogy with Friday prayer: proceeding after fulfilling an obligation (Zuhr) is permitted, but proceeding before fulfilling Umrah invalidates it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن لم يدخل القارنُ مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات: فقد صار رافضاً لعمرته بالوقوف).
وبطل عنه دمُ القران وعليه دم لرفض عمرته، وعليه قضاؤها .
هذا إذا توجه قبل أن يطوف لها أربعة أشواط ، أما إذا طاف لها أربعة أشواط، أو طاف لها، ولم يسع بين الصفا والمروة: فإنه لا يكون رافضاً، ويكون قارناً، ودم القران على حاله واجب، وعليه أن يقضي ما بقي من طواف العمرة بعد طواف الزيارة، ويسعى.
- ثم إنه لا يصير رافضاً بمجرد التوجه، هو الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة.
والفرق له بين مصلي الظهر يوم الجمعة إذا توجه إليها، وبين هذا التوجه : أن الأمر هناك بالتوجه وهو متوجه بعد أداء الظهر، والتوجه هنا عنه قبل أداء العمرة، فافترقا.
قوله: (وبطل عنه دم القرآن)؛ لأنه لما ارتفضت العمرة: صار كالمفرد، والمفرد لا دم عليه.
* قوله: (وعليه دم لرفض العمرة) ، وهو دم جبر، لا يجوز الأكل منه.
* قوله: (وعليه قضاؤها يعني بعد أيام التشريق؛ لأنه بشروعه فيها: أوجبها على نفسه، فقد وجد منه الوجوب، ولم يوجد منه الأداء، فلزمه القضاء.
His statement: (And if the qarin does not enter Mecca and proceeds to Arafat: then he has become an abandoner of his Umrah by standing at Arafat). And the blood sacrifice of qiran is cancelled for him, and he owes a blood sacrifice for abandoning his Umrah, and he owes its qada (making up). This is if he proceeds before performing four circuits (ashwat) of tawaf for it. But if he performed four circuits for it, or performed tawaf but did not sa'y between Safa and Marwa: then he is not an abandoner, he remains a qarin, and the blood sacrifice of qiran remains obligatory as before, and he must complete what remains of the Umrah tawaf after the tawaf of visitation (ziyarah), and perform sa'y. - Then, he does not become an abandoner merely by proceeding (to Arafat); that is the correct view of Abu Hanifa's madhhab. And the distinction for him between the one who prays Zuhr on Friday when he proceeds to the Friday prayer, and this proceeding: the command there is to proceed (to khutbah) while he has already performed Zuhr, whereas the proceeding here is before performing Umrah, so they differ. His statement: (And the blood sacrifice of qiran is cancelled for him) because when the Umrah is abandoned, he becomes like a mufrid (one performing only Hajj), and a mufrid owes no blood sacrifice. * His statement: (And he owes a blood sacrifice for abandoning his Umrah), and it is a dam jabr (compensatory blood), from which it is not permissible to eat. * His statement: (And he owes its qada, meaning after the days of tashriq; because by starting it, he made it obligatory upon himself, so obligation existed from him but performance did not, so qada became incumbent.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage deals with a qarin who bypasses Mecca and goes directly to Arafat, thereby abandoning his Umrah. The ruling hinges on the extent of Umrah performance before leaving: if he has not completed at least four tawaf circuits, he becomes an 'abandoner' (rafid) upon standing at Arafat. Consequently, the qiran sacrifice is waived (since qiran status ends), and he owes two things: a compensatory blood sacrifice (dam jabar) for the rejection, which cannot be eaten, and he must make up the Umrah after the days of tashriq. However, if he has performed four or more circuits, he remains a qarin; he still owes the qiran sacrifice, and he must complete the remaining tawaf after the ziyarah tawaf, and do sa'y. Notably, the commentator clarifies that mere turning towards Arafat does not make him rafid; only the actual standing (wuquf) does. He also draws an analogy with the Friday prayer: just as one who has prayed Zuhr may proceed to the khutbah, the action of proceeding is conditional upon having completed the prior act. Here, the qarin proceeds before completing Umrah, so it invalidates the Umrah.

Key Terms
رافض (rafid): One who abandons his Umrah after beginning it, by performing a prohibited or invalidating action.
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory blood sacrifice offered as a penalty for a violation, not permitted for eating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A qarin performs three circuits of Umrah tawaf, then proceeds to Arafat and stands. What is his status according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) He remains a qarin and owes the qiran sacrifice.
B) He becomes a rafid, the qiran sacrifice is cancelled, and he owes a dam jabr and qada of Umrah.
C) He becomes a mufrid and owes nothing.
D) His Hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A qarin becomes rafid only by standing at Arafat before completing four tawaf circuits; he then owes a dam jabar and must perform qada of Umrah.

Rulings on a Qarin Who Abandons His 'Umrah
Ruling on a Qarin abandoning 'Umrah before four tawaf circuits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Qarin who abandons 'Umrah before completing four tawaf circuits and explain the legal consequences (dam jabar, qada) and the qiyas distinction with the Friday Dhuhr prayer.

Core Idea
A Qarin who abandons 'Umrah before four tawaf circuits becomes a Mufrid, loses dam al-qiran, and owes dam jabar plus qada.

The Hajj chapter on Qiran (combining Hajj and 'Umrah with one ihram) presents a specific ruling when the pilgrim deliberately abandons the 'Umrah portion. This lesson unpacks the conditions under which the abandonment invalidates the Qiran and when it does not. A key qiyas (analogical reasoning) with the Friday Dhuhr prayer helps clarify the principle at work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
The passage distinguishes between abandonment before four tawaf circuits and after four circuits (or after tawaf but before sa'y). In the first case, the Qiran is invalidated; in the second, it remains valid.
2
Understand the criterion (four tawaf circuits)
The number four is the threshold: performing four circuits establishes the 'Umrah to a degree that mere intention to abandon cannot revoke it.
This is a Hanafi ruling; other schools may differ.
3
Trace the qiyas distinction with Friday Dhuhr
The text compares the Qarin who intends to abandon 'Umrah to a person who prays Dhuhr on Friday with the intention to attend Friday prayer. The difference lies in timing: in the Friday case, the obligation (attending Friday prayer) is separate and after Dhuhr; here, the intention to abandon occurs before completing the 'Umrah.
This qiyas shows that mere intention without action does not effect abandonment.
4
Note the Hanafi principle: intention alone does not break ihram
The correct view (al-sahih) from Abu Hanifa is that merely intending to abandon does not make one a rafid. This emphasizes the need for actual abandonment before the threshold.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Suppose a Qarin completes three tawaf circuits then decides to abandon 'Umrah. According to this passage, he falls under the first scenario: he must offer dam jabar and perform qada later.
The compensation dam jabar cannot be eaten from, unlike dam al-qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
وبطل عنه دمُ القرآن وعليه دم لرفض عمرته، وعليه قضاؤها.
هذا إذا توجه قبل أن يطوف لها أربعة أشواط، أما إذا طاف لها أربعة أشواط، أو طاف لها، ولم يسع بين الصفا والمروة: فإنه لا يكون رافضاً، ويكون قارناً، ودم القران على حاله واجب، وعليه أن يقضي ما بقي من طواف العمرة بعد طواف الزيارة، ويسعى.
- ثم إنه لا يصير رافضاً بمجرد التوجه، هو الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة.
والفرق له بين مصلي الظهر يوم الجمعة إذا توجه إليها، وبين هذا التوجه: أن الأمر هناك بالتوجه وهو متوجه بعد أداء الظهر، والتوجه هنا عنه قبل أداء العمرة، فافترقا.
منهي
قوله: (وبطل عنه دم القرآن)؛ لأنه لما ارتفضت العمرة: صار كالمفرد، والمفرد لا دم عليه.
* قوله: (وعليه دم لرفض العمرة)، وهو دم جبر، لا يجوز الأكل منه.
* قوله: (وعليه قضاؤها) يعني بعد أيام التشريق؛ لأنه بشروعه فيها: أوجبها على نفسه، فقد وجد منه الوجوب، ولم يوجد منه الأداء، فلزمه القضاء.
Chapter of Qiran. And the blood (sacrifice) of Qiran is annulled from him, and upon him is a blood (sacrifice) for abandoning his 'Umrah, and upon him is its makeup. This is if he left (i.e., abandoned) before performing four circuits of tawaf for it. As for if he performed four circuits for it, or performed tawaf for it and did not make sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then he is not an abandoner, and he remains a Qarin, and the blood of Qiran remains wajib upon him, and he must make up what remains of the tawaf of 'Umrah after the tawaf of visitation (tawaf al-ziyarah), and perform sa'y. Then, he does not become an abandoner merely by intending (to abandon); this is the correct view from the madhhab of Abu Hanifah. The distinction between the one who prays Dhuhr on Friday and intends (to go to the Friday prayer) and this intention is: in that case the command (to attend Friday prayer) is there, and he is intending after having performed Dhuhr, while here the intention is about leaving before performing the 'Umrah, so they differ. [Margin note?] His statement: (And the blood of Qiran is annulled from him) because when the 'Umrah is abandoned, he becomes like a Mufrid, and a Mufrid has no blood upon him. * His statement: (And upon him is a blood for abandoning the 'Umrah) – this is a compensatory blood (dam jabar), from which it is not permissible to eat. * His statement: (And upon him is its makeup) i.e., after the days of Tashriq, because by starting it he obligated it upon himself; thus obligation occurred from him, and performance did not occur, so makeup became binding.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Qiran (combining Hajj and 'Umrah with one ihram). It addresses the case of a Qarin who deliberately abandons his 'Umrah after having started it. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If he abandons before completing four circuits of tawaf for the 'Umrah, his Qiran is invalidated (he becomes like a Mufrid, one performing only Hajj). Consequently, the blood sacrifice for Qiran (dam al-qiran) is annulled, but he owes a compensatory blood sacrifice (dam jabar) for abandoning the 'Umrah, and he must make up the 'Umrah later (after the days of Tashriq). (2) If he has already performed four circuits of tawaf or has performed tawaf but not yet sa'y, he is not considered an abandoner; he remains a Qarin, the Qiran blood remains wajib, and he completes the remainder of the 'Umrah's tawaf after tawaf al-ziyarah and then does sa'y. The passage also clarifies that mere intention to abandon without action does not make him an abandoner. The author then provides a qiyas (analogical distinction) between this case and the one who prays Dhuhr on Friday after intending to attend Friday prayer—the difference is timing relative to performance. This demonstrates the precision of Hanafi fiqh in distinguishing between similar but legally distinct scenarios.

Key Terms
رفض العمرة (rafḍ al-'umrah): Abandoning the 'Umrah after having entered into it with ihram, before completing the required acts.
دم القرآن (dam al-qirān): The blood sacrifice (dam) required from a Qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together) as a thank-offering.
دم جبر (dam jabar): A compensatory blood sacrifice required for an omission or violation during the pilgrimage, from which the pilgrim may not eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a Qarin who abandons his 'Umrah become a Mufrid and lose the obligation of dam al-qiran?
A) If he abandons before performing tawaf completely.
B) If he abandons before completing four circuits of tawaf.
C) If he abandons after completing four circuits but before sa'y.
D) If he abandons after completing 'Umrah entirely.

Key Takeaway
For a Qarin, abandonment of 'Umrah before four tawaf circuits invalidates the Qiran and requires compensatory dam and qada; after four circuits, the Qiran remains valid and only completion is needed.

Superiority of Tamattu' Over Ifrad in the Hanafi School
Defines Tamattu' and presents the Hanafi preference for it over Ifrad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the superiority of Tamattu' over Ifrad, explain Abu Hanifa's opposing reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is the preferred form of Hajj in the Hanafi school, despite Abu Hanifa's own view that Ifrad is superior.

The proper understanding of Hajj types is incomplete without knowing which is most virtuous. This passage defines Tamattu' and then dives into a curious intra-Hanafi dispute: the school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) favors Tamattu', but the school's eponym, Abu Hanifa, himself held Ifrad to be superior. Let's unpack his reasoning and see why the later scholars overruled it.

Guided Path
1
Define Tamattu' technically
Extract the shar'i definition from the text: combining the ihram and actions of 'Umrah and Hajj in the months of Hajj without returning home (i.e., without valid sexual intercourse with one's family between them).
The linguistic meaning ('luxury') is secondary; focus on the technical definition.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the later ruling (Tamattu' superior) and Abu Hanifa's opposing view (Ifrad superior). Note the phrase 'hādhā huwa al-ṣaḥīḥ' indicates the later view is mufta bihi.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa argued that the Mutamatti's journey is for 'Umrah (sunnah), while the Mufrid's is for Hajj (fard). A journey for fard is better than a journey for sunnah.
The dalil is rational (qiyas) based on the relative virtue of the acts themselves.
4
Note the tarjih
Despite Abu Hanifa's logic, the later scholars declared Tamattu' superior. The text does not give their counter-dalil here, but the tarjih is established by 'hādhā huwa al-ṣaḥīḥ'.
The footnote clarifies that 'Umrah is sunnah (mufta bihi), which is relevant to the strength of Abu Hanifa's argument.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a pilgrim may choose either form, but the recommended one according to the mufta bihi is Tamattu'.
This affects reward, not validity. Both forms are valid Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
التمتع أفضل من الإفراد عندنا.
باب التمتع
قدم القرآن على التمتع؛ لأنه أفضل منه.
والتمتع في اللغة: الترفّه.
وفي الشرع: عبارة عن الجمع بين إحرام العمرة وأفعالها، أو أكثر أفعالها، وإحرام الحج وأفعاله في أشهر الحج، من غير إلمام صحيح بأهله.
* قال رحمه الله: (التمتع عندنا أفضل من الإفراد)، هذا هو الصحيح. وعن أبي حنيفة: أن الإفراد أفضل؛ لأن المتمتع سفره واقع لعمرته، بدليل أنه إذا فرغ من العمرة: صار مكياً في حق الميقات؛ لأنه يقيم بمكة حلالاً، ثم يُحرم للحج من المسجد الحرام.
والمفرد سفره واقع لحجته، والحج فريضة، والعمرة سنة، والسفر الواقع للفرض: أفضل من السفر الواقع للسنة.
(١) سيأتي في جناية الجماع في العمرة ص ٤٢٥ أن العمرة سنة، وكذلك هنا، لكن سيذكر المصنف في أحكام العمرة أواخر كتاب الحج ص٤٦٩ أن العمرة واجبة، مستدركاً على القدوري القائل بسنّيتها، ولهذا نبهت هنا، والمعتمد في المذهب سنيتها.
Chapter of Tamattu'. Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad according to us. Chapter of Tamattu'. Qiran is given precedence over Tamattu' because it is superior to it. Tamattu' in language means luxury/comfort. In Sacred Law: it is an expression for combining the ihram of 'Umrah and its actions, or most of its actions, and the ihram of Hajj and its actions in the months of Hajj, without having valid sexual intercourse with one's family. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad according to us), this is the correct view. And from Abu Hanifa: that Ifrad is superior, because the Mutamatti' has his journey occurring for his 'Umrah, as evidenced by the fact that when he finishes the 'Umrah, he becomes a Makkan with respect to the miqat, because he stays in Mecca as a non-muhrim, then he enters ihram for Hajj from al-Masjid al-Haram. The Mufrid has his journey occurring for his Hajj, and Hajj is a fard, while 'Umrah is a sunnah, and the journey that occurs for a fard is superior to the journey that occurs for a sunnah. (Footnote 1: It will come in the chapter on the penalty of intercourse during 'Umrah, p. 425, that 'Umrah is a sunnah, and likewise here. But the author will mention in the rulings of 'Umrah at the end of the book of Hajj, p. 469, that 'Umrah is wajib, correcting al-Quduri who said it is sunnah. For this reason, I have noted it here, and the relied-upon position in the madhhab is that it is sunnah.)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (between the later position and Abu Hanifa) on the relative virtue of Tamattu' vs. Ifrad in Hajj. It opens by defining Tamattu' linguistically and technically. The technical definition: combining the ihram and actions of 'Umrah with the ihram and actions of Hajj during the months of Hajj, without returning home (i.e., without having valid intercourse with one's family between the two). The text then states that according to the Hanafi school (the later view, which is the relied-upon position), Tamattu' is better (afdal) than Ifrad. However, it reports that Abu Hanifa himself held Ifrad to be superior. His reasoning: a Mutamatti's journey is primarily for 'Umrah (since he does 'Umrah first, then stays in Mecca as a non-muhrim, then begins Hajj from within the Haram), while a Mufrid's journey is for Hajj. Since Hajj is fard and 'Umrah is sunnah in the Hanafi view, the journey for the fard is better. Despite this, the later scholars favored Tamattu' based on other considerations (not detailed here). The footnote clarifies the status of 'Umrah: some texts say it is sunnah, others say wajib, but the relied-upon Hanafi view is that it is sunnah.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Technically: combining the ihram and actions of 'Umrah with the ihram and actions of Hajj during the months of Hajj without returning home (i.e., without valid intercourse with one's family between them).
الإفراد (al-ifrād): Performing Hajj alone, without 'Umrah, in one journey.
القران (al-qirān): Combining Hajj and 'Umrah with a single ihram.
أفضل (afḍal): More excellent, superior in reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, which type of Hajj is considered superior?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's final position is that Tamattu' is the most meritorious form of Hajj, despite Abu Hanifa's personal preference for Ifrad.

Definition and Two Types of Hajj Tamattu'
Defines tamattu', its types, and describes rituals with legal reasoning on ilmaam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tamattu' and distinguish between the two types of mutamatti' based on driving a hady and the effect of ilmaam.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is performing Umrah and Hajj in one journey without valid return; the hady is required only for those who return validly.

Welcome to the chapter on tamattu'. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira defines tamattu' linguistically and legally, breaking it into two types: one who drives a sacrificial animal (hady) and one who does not. We'll walk through the exact ritual sequence for the mutamatti' without hady, including the cutting of talbiyah and the absence of certain tawafs. We'll also examine the rarely-discussed Hanafi ruling on ilmaam (returning to one's family) – a point where even our own school has a subtle internal difference.

Guided Path
1
Define tamattu' legally
Find the definition in the passage: performing Umrah and Hajj in one journey without returning to one's family validly between them.
The root meaning is 'ease' or 'comfort'.
2
Identify the two types of mutamatti'
One who drives a hady and one who does not. The hady is a sacrificial animal brought from the miqat.
The ritual description in the passage is for the one who does not drive a hady.
3
Describe the ritual for the mutamatti' without hady
Step-by-step: ihram for Umrah from miqat, enter Mecca, tawaf, sa'i, shave/shorten, become halal, cut talbiyah at tawaf start, stay in Mecca, on 8th Dhul Hijjah ihram for Hajj from the mosque.
No tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr in Umrah, explained later.
4
Explain the cutting of talbiyah and the absence of tawafs
The talbiyah is cut when starting tawaf because the purpose is tawaf. In Umrah, the rukn tawaf is immediate, so no supererogatory tawaf (qudum) is needed; tawaf al-sadr is not repeated because the main pillar is tawaf itself.
This is in response to a question (فإن قلت).
5
Analyze the ruling on ilmaam (returning to family)
A valid ilmaam (staying overnight) breaks tamattu'; an invalid one does not according to Abu Hanifa. The text also discusses the status when driving a hady and a possible disagreement with Muhammad.
Intra-Hanafi difference – the relied upon position is Abu Hanifa's.

Chapter of Tamattu'. The mutamatti' is of two types: one who drives the hady (sacrificial animal) and one who does not drive the hady. The description of tamattu' is that he begins from the miqat, enters ihram for umrah, enters Mecca, performs tawaf for it, performs sa'i, and shaves or shortens hair, and he has become halal from his umrah. The aspect of the first statement: that in tamattu' there is a combination of two devotions, so it resembles qiran, then there is an additional rite, which is shedding blood. The Sunnah. And his travel is occurring for his hajj even if the umrah intervenes; because it is a follower of the hajj, like the intervention between Friday and proceeding to it. * His statement: (The mutamatti' is of two types: a mutamatti' who drives the hady, and a mutamatti' who does not drive the hady). And the meaning of tamattu' is: ease by performing the two rites in one journey, without him returning to his family between them with a valid return. He avoids the corrupt return, for it does not prevent the validity of tamattu' according to Abu Hanifa. And al-ilmaam is: stopping with one's family. And the correct ilmaam only occurs in the mutamatti' who does not drive the hady. As for when he drives the hady, his ilmaam is corrupt, unlike Muhammad. He prevents the validity of tamattu'. * His statement: (The description of the mutamatti' who does not drive the hady is that he begins from the miqat, enters ihram for umrah, enters Mecca, performs tawaf for it and sa'i, shaves or shortens, and becomes halal from his umrah). (1) This is the copy of Imam al-Haddad of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and it differs from what I have of al-Quduri's copies. And he cuts the talbiyah when he begins the tawaf, and stays in Mecca as halal. Then when it is the day of al-Tarwiyah, he enters ihram for hajj from the mosque. And this is the interpretation of umrah. If you say: why is there not in umrah tawaf al-qudum nor tawaf al-sadr? I say: As for tawaf al-qudum, because the mu'tamir when he arrives at the House is able to perform the tawaf which is a pillar in this rite, so he busies not with other than it, unlike hajj: for when he arrives he is not able to perform the tawaf which is a pillar of hajj, so he performs the supererogatory tawaf until the time for the tawaf which is a pillar comes. As for tawaf al-sadr, the main part of the pillar in umrah is tawaf, and that which is the main part of the pillar in the rite is not repeated at the sadr, like the standing in hajj; because one thing cannot be both the main part of the pillar in the rite and at the same time not a pillar in that rite. As in al-Nihayah. * His statement: (And he cuts the talbiyah when he begins tawaf, meaning when he touches the Black Stone; because the purpose of umrah is tawaf, so he cuts it when beginning it. * His statement: (Then he stays in Mecca as halal) until the time of ihram for hajj; because nothing of its actions remains upon him. His statement: (Then when it is the day of al-Tarwiyah, he enters ihram for hajj from the mosque).
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, opens the chapter on tamattu' (the form of Hajj where one performs Umrah first in the Hajj months and then later performs Hajj in the same year without returning home). The commentator begins by defining the two types of mutamatti': one who brings a sacrificial animal (hady) and one who does not. The core description of the tamattu' ritual is then given: the pilgrim starts from the miqat (the boundary where ihram is assumed) by entering ihram for Umrah, enters Mecca, performs tawaf and sa'i, then shaves or shortens the hair, becoming free from the state of ihram for Umrah. The pilgrim remains in Mecca in a non-ihram state. Then on the eighth day of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyyah), he enters ihram for Hajj from the mosque. The commentator explains that the purpose of cutting the talbiyah when starting tawaf is that the primary goal of Umrah is the tawaf. The passage also addresses a query: why does Umrah not have tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) or tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf)? The answer is that in Umrah, the rukn tawaf is performed immediately upon arrival, so there is no need for a separate supererogatory tawaf. In Hajj, the rukn tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah) is delayed, so a sunnah tawaf is performed upon arrival. Tawaf al-sadr is not repeated because the main pillar of Umrah is tawaf itself, and a single action cannot be both the main pillar and a separate rite to be performed again at departure. The commentator also notes a subtle point about 'ilmaam' (returning to one's family) between Umrah and Hajj: a valid return (where one stays overnight) prevents the tamattu' status, but a cursory or invalid return does not break the tamattu' according to Abu Hanifa. The text further indicates that the hady is required for one who has a valid return.

Key Terms
التّمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing umrah and hajj in one journey without returning home in between, with ease.
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): The pilgrim who performs tamattu'.
الإلمام (al-ilmaam): Returning to one's family between umrah and hajj.
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The supererogatory tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca for hajj.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed upon leaving Mecca.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk...' recited during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no tawaf al-qudum in Umrah?
A) Because Umrah is a smaller pilgrimage.
B) Because the rukn tawaf is performed immediately upon arrival.
C) Because the talbiyah is cut first.
D) Because the pilgrim goes directly to sa'i.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is the most convenient form of Hajj, but its validity depends on not returning home validly between Umrah and Hajj.

Rulings of Tamattu' in Hajj
Explanation of tamattu' rituals and their legal details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of tamattu' and the conditions for cutting talbiyah, performing ramal, and the obligation of dam, and distinguish tamattu' from ifrad.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires a dam; actions differ from ifrad due to prior 'umrah.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira details the rulings of tamattu', a form of Hajj where one first performs 'umrah, then later performs Hajj in the same year. The text explains the precise moments to cut talbiyah, why no arrival or farewell tawaf exists in 'umrah, and the obligation of the dam. It also clarifies how the mutamatti' differs from the mufrid in certain rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of tamattu'
Read the passage to determine the order: the pilgrim enters ihram for 'umrah, cuts talbiyah at the start of tawaf, completes 'umrah, stays halal, then enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (or earlier, which is better).
The time for ihram for Hajj is not strictly fixed; earlier is preferable.
2
Analyze why no tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr in 'umrah
The text explains that in 'umrah, the pilgrim performs the pillar (rukn) tawaf immediately upon arrival, so there is no need for a separate arrival tawaf. Similarly, the main pillar (tawaf) is not repeated at departure, so no farewell tawaf.
This is a legal reasoning (ta'lil) distinguishing 'umrah from Hajj.
3
Note the obligations and preferences
The mutamatti' does not perform tawaf al-tahiyyah after ihram for Hajj because he is like a Makkan. He performs ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'i after it, unless he already performed a voluntary tawaf and sa'i after ihram for Hajj before going to Mina.
Ramal and sa'i are not repeated if already performed after ihram.
4
State the dam ruling
The text explicitly states 'upon him is the dam of tamattu''. If unable, he fasts three days during Hajj and seven after returning home.
The dam is wajib, not fard, because it can be substituted by fasting.

Source Text

وهذا هو تفسير العمرة.

ولو كان هذا المتمتع بعد ما أحرم بالحج طاف تطوعاً، وسعى قبل أن يروح إلى منى لم يرمل في طواف الزيارة، ولا يسعى بعده؛ لأنه قد أتى بذلك مرة.

Chapter of Tamattu'. He cuts the talbiyah when he begins the tawaf, and stays in Makkah as halal. Then on the day of Tarwiyah, he enters ihram for Hajj from the mosque. This is the interpretation of 'umrah. If you said: Why is there no tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) and no farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) in 'umrah? I said: As for tawaf al-qudum, because the person performing 'umrah upon his arrival at the House is able to perform the tawaf that is a pillar (rukn) of this rite, so he does not occupy himself with other than it, unlike Hajj, for upon his arrival he is not able to perform the tawaf that is a pillar of Hajj, so he performs the supererogatory tawaf until the time of the tawaf that is a pillar comes. As for tawaf al-sadr, the main pillar in 'umrah is the tawaf, and whatever is the main pillar in a rite is not repeated at the time of departure, like the standing at 'Arafat in Hajj, because one and the same thing cannot be the main pillar of a rite while it is not a pillar in that rite. Thus in al-Nihayah. * His saying: (He cuts the talbiyah when he begins the tawaf, meaning when touching the Black Stone, because the purpose of 'umrah is tawaf, so he cuts it at its start. * His saying: (Then he stays in Makkah as halal) until the time of ihram for Hajj, because no action of 'umrah remains upon him. His saying: (Then on the day of Tarwiyah: he enters ihram for Hajj from the mosque). And he does what the mufrid pilgrim does. And upon him is the dam of tamattu'. If he cannot find it, he fasts three days during Hajj and seven when he returns to his family. This time is not binding; rather if he wishes, he may enter ihram for Hajj before the day of Tarwiyah, and the earlier his ihram for Hajj, the better, because it shows eagerness and desire for worship. Thus in al-Nihayah. And his saying: 'from the mosque' — the restriction to the mosque is for preference; as for permissibility, the entire Haram is a miqat. His saying: (And he does what the mufrid pilgrim does), except that he does not perform tawaf al-tahiyyah, because when he became halal he equals the Makkan, and there is no tahiyyah for the Makkan; likewise this. And he performs ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah and does sa'i after it, because it is his first tawaf in Hajj, unlike the mufrid, for he has performed tawaf al-qudum and sa'i. If this mutamatti' after entering ihram for Hajj performed a supererogatory tawaf and sa'i before going to Mina, he does not perform ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah and does not do sa'i after it, because he has already done that once. His saying: (And upon him is dam) i.e. dam al-tamattu'. His saying: (If he cannot find it: he fasts three days during Hajj and seven when he returns to his family).
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the rulings of tamattu' in Hajj. It begins with the rule that the mutamatti' cuts the talbiyah when he starts tawaf for 'umrah, because the purpose is tawaf. He then stays in Makkah in a halal state until the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhu al-Hijjah), when he enters ihram for Hajj from the mosque. The commentator also addresses a question: why is there no tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) in 'umrah? Because the 'umrah's own tawaf is its pillar, so there is no need for a separate arrival tawaf. Similarly, there is no farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) because the main pillar (tawaf) is not repeated at departure. The text also clarifies that the time for ihram for Hajj is not fixed to Yawm al-Tarwiyah; one may enter ihram earlier, and earlier is better. The mosque restriction is for preference; the entire Haram is valid. The mutamatti' then performs all actions of a mufrid pilgrim, except that he does not perform tawaf al-tahiyyah because after his 'umrah he is like a Makkan. He performs ramal (quick walking with shoulder movement) in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'i after it, because this is his first tawaf in Hajj. However, if he did a voluntary tawaf and sa'i after ihram for Hajj before going to Mina, then the ramal and sa'i are not repeated in tawaf al-ziyarah. Finally, the dam (sacrifice) is required for tamattu'; if unable, he fasts three days in Hajj and seven upon returning home.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim upon ihram; cut when starting tawaf in 'umrah.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing 'umrah first, then after a break performing Hajj in the same year with a dam.
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): A sacrifice (sheep or goat) required from the mutamatti' as a penalty for combining 'umrah and Hajj without returning to the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When he begins the tawaf by touching the Black Stone
C) After completing sa'i
D) Upon entering the Haram

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' cuts talbiyah at the start of tawaf, owes a dam (or fasting), and must observe special rules for ramal and sa'i.

Rulings for the Mutamatti' in Hajj Tamattu'
States rulings for a mutamatti' and compensation options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations of a mutamatti' in Hajj Tamattu', including the compensation (dam) and fasting alternatives, and distinguish the timing requirements for fasting.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' must sacrifice a dam; if unable, fast three days in Hajj and seven after returning.

This lesson explains the obligations of one performing Hajj Tamattu' (mutamatti'). It clarifies the requirement of the sacrificial animal (dam al-tamattu'), the fasting alternative, and the specific timing conditions for the fast. Understanding these rules ensures the validity of the tamattu' ritual and avoids common mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mutamatti' and His Actions
Recognize who is a mutamatti' and that he performs all actions of a mufrid except tawaf al-tahiyyah.
2
Understand the Compensation (Dam)
Note that the mutamatti' must offer a dam (sacrifice) as a wajib obligation.
3
Explore the Fasting Alternative
When unable to sacrifice, fasting three days during Hajj and seven after return is required.
4
Examine Timing Conditions for Fasting
Fasting must be within the months of Hajj and after entering ihram for Umrah but before entering ihram for Hajj (or at least after Umrah ihram). It cannot be before Umrah ihram.
5
Note Additional Rulings on Ramal and Sa'y
The mutamatti' performs ramal and sa'y in tawaf al-ziyarah unless he had already performed a supererogatory tawaf with sa'y.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وقوله: من المسجد التقييد بالمسجد : للأفضلية، وأما الجواز: فجميع الحرم ميقات.

- ويرمل في طواف الزيارة، ويسعى بعده؛ لأنه أول طواف له في الحج، بخلاف المفرد ؛ لأنه قد طاف للقدوم وسعى.
