Chapter of Tamattu'. And he does what the single pilgrim does. And upon him is the blood (sacrifice) of tamattu'. If he does not find (an animal), he fasts three days during Hajj, and seven when he returns to his family. This time is not necessary, but if he wishes, he may enter into ihram for Hajj before the day of Tarwiyah, and entering ihram earlier is better, because it shows haste and desire for worship. Ibid. in 'al-Nihaya'. And his saying: from the mosque, the restriction to the mosque is for virtue, but permissibility: all of the Haram is a miqat. His saying: (and he does what the single pilgrim does), except that he does not perform the circumambulation of greeting, because when he became halal, he and the Makkan are the same, and there is no greeting for the Makkan, likewise this. And he performs ramal in the circumambulation of visitation, and performs sa'y after it, because it is his first circumambulation in Hajj, unlike the single pilgrim because he has already performed the circumambulation of arrival and sa'y. And if this mutamatti', after he had entered ihram for Hajj, performed a supererogatory circumambulation and sa'y before going to Mina, he does not perform ramal in the circumambulation of visitation nor sa'y after it, because he has already done that once. His saying: (and upon him is blood): that is the blood of tamattu'. His saying: (If he does not find (an animal), he fasts three days during Hajj, and seven when he returns to his family). And it is permissible for him to fast these three after the ihram of Umrah before the ihram of Hajj, on condition that it be during the months of Hajj. And it is not permissible to fast them before the ihram of Umrah, but if he fasts them after the ihram of Umrah before he performs circumambulation for it, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri explains the rulings for the mutamatti' (one performing Hajj Tamattu'). It begins by stating that the mutamatti' performs all the actions of a single pilgrim (mufrid) except that he does not perform the circumambulation of greeting (tawaf al-tahiyyah) because after completing Umrah and becoming halal, he is like a resident of Makkah. However, he does perform ramal (quick pace) in the tawaf al-ziyarah (circumambulation of visitation) and sa'y after it, as it is his first circumambulation in Hajj. If he had performed a supererogatory tawaf with sa'y before going to Mina, then he omits ramal and sa'y in tawaf al-ziyarah. The passage then addresses the compensation (dam) required for tamattu': the mutamatti' must slaughter a sacrificial animal (dam al-tamattu'). If he cannot afford it, he must fast three days during the Hajj season (specifically after entering ihram for Umrah before ihram for Hajj, and within the months of Hajj) and seven days after returning home. The fast cannot begin before the ihram of Umrah, but if started after ihram and before tawaf for Umrah, it is valid. The commentator also notes that entering ihram for Hajj earlier (before the day of Tarwiyah) is better, and that the miqat for ihram from the mosque is for virtue, but permissibility applies to the entire Haram.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Hajj Tamattu', i.e., performs Umrah first, then breaks ihram, then performs Hajj later in the same journey.
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) required as compensation for tamattu'.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only after completing both Umrah and Hajj
D) Anytime during the year

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' must either sacrifice a dam or, if unable, fast three days during the Hajj months (after Umrah ihram) and seven days after returning home.

Driving a Sacrificial Animal in Tamattu'
Explains the ruling for a mutamatti' who drives a hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' driving a hady and identify the condition for becoming muhrim via taqlid.

Core Idea
Driving a hady in tamattu' is better but taqlid must occur in Hajj months to be valid.

The passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains that a mutamatti' may drive a sacrificial animal as an additional act of devotion. This is considered superior to tamattu' without driving. However, a crucial condition from al-Nihaya is that the marking (taqlid) and setting out (tawajjuh) must take place within the months of Hajj for the animal to count as a hady of tamattu' and for the driver to become muhrim through it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is driving a hady in tamattu'. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended) and considered afdal (better) than not driving.
The obligation of the dam remains wajib regardless.
2
Find the condition for ihram via hady
From al-Nihaya: ihram through the hady only occurs if taqlid (marking) and tawajjuh (setting out) happen in the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, first 10 of Dhu al-Hijjah).
If taqlid occurs outside those months, the animal becomes nafl (supererogatory) and does not make one muhrim until one catches up and walks with it.
3
Apply the condition
If the mutamatti' marks and sets out within the Hajj months, he becomes muhrim immediately. Otherwise, he does not become muhrim until he physically catches the animal and proceeds with it.
4
Understand the textual ordering
The author presents tamattu' without driving first, even though driving is better, because driving is an additional attribute, and presenting the essence (the basic form) takes precedence.
This is a stylistic choice, not a valuation of importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أراد المتمتع أن يسوق الهَدْيَ : أحرم، وساق هَديه .
فإن كانت بدنةً : قلدها بمَزادة، أو نعل،
وهذا هو الوجه الثاني من التمتع ، وهو أفضل من الأول الذي لم يسق. وإنما قدم الوجه الأول على هذا، مع أن هذا أفضل ؛ لأن هذا وصف زائد، وتقديم الذات: أولى من تقديم الصفات.
قال في «النهاية»: إذا ساق المتمتع الهدي: ففيه قيد لا بد من معرفته، وهو: أنه في هدي المتعة إنما يصير محرماً بالتقليد والتوجه إذا حصلا في أشهر الحج. أما إذا لم يحصلا فيها : لا يصير مُحرِماً، ما لم يُدرك الهدي، ويسير معه؛ لأن تقليد هدي المتعة في غير الأشهر لا يُعتد به، ويكون تطوعاً، وهدي التطوع ما لم يدركه، ويسير معه : لا يصير محرماً.
قوله: (فإن كانت بدنةٌ : قلَّدها بمَزادة): أي قطعة من أدم، (أو نَعْل)، أو شيء من لحاء الشجر.
And if the mutamatti' wants to drive the sacrificial animal, he enters ihram and drives his sacrificial animal. If it is a camel (badanah), he marks it with a mazada (piece of leather) or a sandal. This is the second type of tamattu', and it is better than the first in which he does not drive. And the first type was presented before this, even though this is better, because this is an additional attribute, and presenting the essence takes precedence over presenting attributes. He said in 'al-Nihaya': When the mutamatti' drives the hady, there is a condition that must be known, which is that in the hady of tamattu', he only becomes muhrim by the marking (taqlid) and heading (tawajjuh) if they occur in the months of Hajj. But if they do not occur in them, he does not become muhrim, unless he catches up with the hady and walks with it, because the marking of the hady of tamattu' outside the months is not considered, and it becomes supererogatory, and the supererogatory hady, as long as he does not catch it and walk with it, does not make him muhrim. His saying: (If it is a camel, he marks it with a mazada): meaning a piece of leather, or a sandal, or something from the bark of a tree.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of the mutamatti' who chooses to drive sacrificial animals (hady) along with his ihram. This is considered a superior form of tamattu' because it involves an additional act of worship. The commentator explains that if the mutamatti' drives a camel (badanah), he should mark it (taqlid) with a piece of leather (mazada), a sandal (na'l), or tree bark. The key legal point from 'al-Nihaya' is that for the hady of tamattu', the mutamatti' only becomes bound by the ihram for Hajj through the taqlid and setting out (tawajjuh) if these actions take place within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah). If taqlid occurs outside these months, it is not valid for tamattu' and the animal becomes a supererogatory (nafl) offering. In that case, the mutamatti' does not become muhrim until he catches up with the animal and walks with it. The reason the first type (without driving) is mentioned first in the text is that it is the essential form, while driving is an additional attribute; it is more important to present the essence first.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal (camel, cow, sheep, or goat) driven to the Haram for offering.
تقليد (taqlid): Marking a sacrificial animal by placing a leather strap, sandal, or bark around its neck to indicate it is destined for sacrifice.
بدنة (badanah): A large sacrificial animal, specifically a camel or cow, for offering in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is necessary for a mutamatti' driving a hady to become muhrim via the hady?
A) The hady must be a camel
B) The taqlid and setting out must occur within the months of Hajj
C) The hady must be a sheep
D) The mutamatti' must fast for three days

Key Takeaway
To become muhrim through a hady in tamattu', the marking and setting out must occur within the months of Hajj; otherwise the animal becomes a supererogatory offering and does not induce ihram until caught.

The Superiority of Taqlid over Tajlil for the Mutamatti's Hady
Explains rulings for a mutamatti' who brings hady, including taqlid and ish'ar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taqlid and ish'ar for the mutamatti's hady and explain why taqlid is preferred over tajlil.

Core Idea
Taqlid is the preferred marker for hady because it is explicitly sanctioned by the Quran and serves exclusively as a sign of sacrifice.

The mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hady) must mark it to indicate its status. The Hanafi school teaches that garlanding (taqlid) is superior to covering (tajlil) and that ish'ar is recommended for camels. This lesson unpacks the proofs and reasoning behind these preferences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the mutamatti' does with the hady and the hukm level. The passage states that taqlid is recommended (mandub).
Taqlid is not wajib; it is a recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited for taqlid. The Quranic verse 5:2 mentions 'al-qala'id' (garlands), proving its legality.
The verse is a prohibition, but mentioning garlands indicates they are a recognized practice.
3
Compare taqlid and tajlil
Analyze why taqlid is preferred: it is from Quran and serves only as a marker, whereas tajlil is from Sunnah and has other purposes.
Tajlil also protects from flies and weather, diluting its specific function.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ish'ar
Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah. The text presents the Sahibayn's view.
Ish'ar is only for camels, not cows or sheep.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: taqlid is recommended; for ish'ar, the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is preferred.
Later Hanafi works adopt this view.

Chapter of Tamattu'
If the mutamatti' wants to bring the hady, he enters ihram and brings his hady. If it is a badanah (camel/cow), he garlands it with a leather strip or a sandal.
- It is permissible to fast these three days after the ihram of 'umrah before the ihram of hajj, on condition that it is during the months of hajj.
- It is not permissible to fast them before the ihram of 'umrah. If he fasts them after the ihram of 'umrah before performing tawaf for it, it is permissible.
[Regarding tamattu' with bringing hady:]
His saying: (If the mutamatti' wants to bring the hady, he enters ihram and brings his hady.) This is the second aspect of tamattu', and it is superior to the first where he does not bring [hady]. The first aspect was presented before this one despite this one being superior because this one has an additional description, and presenting the essence is more appropriate than presenting the attributes.
He said in al-Nihayah: When the mutamatti' brings the hady, there is a condition that must be known: In the hady of tamattu', he only becomes muhrim by taqlid and direction if they occur during the months of hajj. If they do not occur during them, he does not become muhrim until he [catches up with] the hady and walks with it; because taqlid of hady tamattu' outside the months is not considered and becomes supererogatory (tatawwu'), and [for] supererogatory hady, he does not become muhrim until he catches up with it and walks with it. This is not with him. [Unclear]
His saying: (If it is a badanah, he garlands it with a leather strip): meaning a piece of leather, or a sandal, or something from tree bark.
And he marks the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
And taqlid is preferable to tajlil (covering) because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran, Allah Almighty said: "And [do not violate] the hady nor the garlands" [al-Ma'idah 5:2]. Thus the legality of taqlid is established by the Book and the Sunnah.
And tajlil is only established by Sunnah, and it is not specifically intended for marking alone; rather it shares other meanings: repelling flies, and repelling heat and cold.
And taqlid is specifically for marking, without sharing.
And the picture of taqlid is that one ties on the neck of his badanah a piece of leather or a sandal, and the meaning is that this [animal] is prepared for bloodshed, so its skin will soon become like this piece of leather, so that it is not prevented from water and fodder when it is known that it is a hady. This is only for what is lost from its owner, like camels and cows. As for sheep, it is lost if its owner is not with it, so it is not garlanded.
And it is better that he first make talbiyah, then garland; because he becomes muhrim by garlanding and direction with it, so presenting talbiyah is better so that his commencement of ihram is with it, not with garlanding.
His saying: (And he marks the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
And ish'ar is not recommended for other than camels.
- Its description: That one pierces the base of the hump on the right side with a needle or a spearhead until blood comes out, then smears the hump with it, as a notice to people that it is a sacrifice to Allah.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah explains the rulings for a mutamatti' performing Hajj al-Tamattu' who chooses to bring a sacrificial animal (hady). The text begins by stating the basic ruling: if the mutamatti' wishes to bring the hady, he enters ihram and brings it. If the animal is a camel or cow (badanah), he should perform taqlid (garlanding) by tying a piece of leather or a sandal around its neck.

The commentary then clarifies that this type of tamattu' (with hady) is the second and superior form, as it involves an additional act of devotion. The author explains why the simpler form was mentioned first: it is the essence, and the additional description is secondary.

A crucial condition is mentioned from al-Nihayah: for the hady of tamattu', the taqlid and the intention to travel must occur within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah). If taqlid is performed outside these months, it does not count as the hady of tamattu' but as a supererogatory offering, and the person does not become muhrim until he physically meets the animal and proceeds with it.

The commentary then contrasts taqlid with tajlil (covering the animal). While both are forms of marking the hady, taqlid is preferred because it is explicitly mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:2), whereas tajlil is only known from the Sunnah. Moreover, taqlid serves exclusively as a marker, whereas tajlil also serves other purposes like protecting from flies and weather. Thus, taqlid is more specific to the purpose of indicating that the animal is a sacrifice.

The text then describes the method of taqlid: a piece of leather or a sandal is tied around the animal's neck, symbolizing that the animal's skin will soon be like that severed piece. This ensures that the animal is not prevented from water or fodder by someone who recognizes it as a hady. This practice applies only to animals that may wander away from the owner, such as camels and cows; sheep are not garlanded because they would be lost if left unattended.

It is recommended to perform talbiyah (the pilgrim's proclamation) before taqlid, because the person becomes muhrim through taqlid and the intention to travel, so starting with talbiyah is more appropriate.

Finally, the text mentions ish'ar (marking by cutting the hump and smearing blood) for a badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Ish'ar is only recommended for camels, not for cows or sheep. The method is to make an incision on the right side of the hump's base to draw blood, then smear it over the hump as a visible sign that the animal is dedicated to Allah.

The Hanafi position is that taqlid is mustahabb for the hady of tamattu', and it is superior to tajlil. For ish'ar, it is considered permissible and recommended according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but Abu Hanifa considers it makruh because it involves mutilation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that ish'ar is permissible but not mandatory.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlīd): To hang a piece of leather or a sandal around the neck of an animal to mark it as a sacrificial offering.
تجليل (tajlīl): Covering the sacrificial animal with a cloth or blanket as a marker.
إشعار (ishʿār): Making an incision on the hump of a camel to draw blood and smearing it as a marker.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran during Hajj.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow (male or female) suitable for sacrifice; plural budun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred method of marking a hady for a mutamatti'?
A) Tajlil (covering)
B) Taqlid (garlanding)
C) Ish'ar (incising)
D) None, it is not required

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is the recommended method for marking the hady of tamattu' due to its Quranic sanction and exclusive function.

Taqlid: Its Ruling and Description
Explains the ruling and procedure of taqlid for hady.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for taqlid and describe its procedure for camels and cows versus sheep.

Core Idea
Taqlid is better than tajlil because it is mentioned in the Quran and serves solely for identification.

In Hajj Tamattu', the sacrificial animal (hady) must be marked. Two methods are taqlid (garland) and tajlil (covering). This lesson explains why taqlid is preferred, its Quranic basis, and how it is performed. The commentary clarifies that taqlid is only for large animals like camels and cows, not for sheep.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of marking hady
Recognize that taqlid and tajlil are both ways to mark a sacrificial animal. Taqlid involves placing a garland, tajlil involves covering with a cloth.
2
Compare their evidences
Taqlid is mentioned in the Quran (5:2), while tajlil is only established by the Sunnah. This makes taqlid stronger in proof.
The Quranic verse prohibits violating the qala'id, indicating its legitimacy.
3
Determine the purpose
Taqlid is exclusively for identification, whereas tajlil also serves to repel flies, heat, and cold. Exclusivity makes taqlid more appropriate for marking.
4
Describe the taqlid procedure
Tie a piece of leather or sandal around the neck of the animal to signal it is for sacrifice, so it is not denied water and fodder.
This is done for camels and cows, not sheep because sheep would wander off if left unattended.
5
Note the recommended order
First pronounce the talbiyah, then perform taqlid, because ihram should be entered with the talbiyah, not with the garland.
This order is preferred but not obligatory.

Chapter of Tamattu'. And he makes ish'ar for the camel according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Taqlid is better than tajlil because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran. Allah Almighty said: 'And do not [violate] the hady nor the garlands.' [Al-Ma'idah 5:2]. Thus the legality of taqlid is established by the Book and the Sunnah. Tajlil is only established by the Sunnah and it is not specifically intended for notification alone; rather, it shares other meanings: repelling flies, and repelling heat and cold. Taqlid is specifically for notification, without sharing. The image of taqlid is that one ties on the neck of his sacrificial animal a piece of leather or a sandal. The meaning is that this [animal] is prepared for bloodshed, so its skin will soon become like that piece of leather, so that it is not prevented from water and fodder when it is known that it is a hady. This is only for what is out of its owner's sight, like camels and cows; as for sheep, it would be lost if its owner is not with it, so it is not made to wear a garland. It is better to first say the talbiyah then put the garland, because he becomes a muhrim through the garland and proceeding with it, so preceding the talbiyah is better so that his commencement of ihram is with it, not with the garland. His saying: 'And he makes ish'ar for the camel according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.' Ish'ar is not recommended for other than camels. Its description: that he pierces the lower part of the hump on the right side with a needle or spearhead until blood comes out, then he smears the hump with that, as a notification to people that it is a sacrifice for Allah Almighty. And it is: that he splits its hump on the right side. And Abu Hanifa does not make ish'ar. * His saying: 'And it is: that he splits its hump on the right side.' In Al-Hidayah: the more correct is the left side, i.e., the more correct in the narration, because the hadaya were coming towards the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and he would enter between every two camels from the direction of their heads, and the spear was in his right hand inevitably, so his thrust would first fall on the left side of the camel. If the camel is stubborn, it is permissible to split whichever side he wishes according to his ability. * His saying: 'And Abu Hanifa does not make ish'ar.' He only mentioned their saying before his saying because he held that the fatwa is on their saying. In Al-Hidayah it is mentioned that ish'ar is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them it is good (hasan). Abu Ya'la reported the piercing on the left side in his Musnad, and Muslim (1243) reported the piercing on the right side; see the narrations in Nasb al-Rayah 3/116.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah is a commentary on the matn of Al-Quduri, explaining two ways of marking the hady (sacrificial animal) in Hajj Tamattu': taqlid (placing a garland) and ish'ar (making a cut to draw blood). The commentary begins by presenting the ruling on ish'ar from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is recommended, then immediately compares taqlid and tajlil (covering the animal with a cloth). The author proves the preference for taqlid through the Quranic verse (5:2) where 'qala'id' (garlands) are mentioned, establishing its legitimacy by both Book and Sunnah, while tajlil is only from Sunnah and serves multiple purposes (repelling flies, heat, cold), not exclusively for identification. Taqlid is solely for identification. The description of taqlid is given: tying a piece of leather or sandal on the neck of a camel or cow to signal it is a hady, so it is not denied water or fodder. This is not done for sheep as they would wander off. Then the order of actions: first talbiyah, then taqlid, because ihram should be entered with talbiyah, not with the garland. Returning to ish'ar, the text states it is only for camels (not other animals) and describes the act: piercing the lower hump on the right side with a needle or spear until blood appears, then smearing it as a mark. On page 401, the commentary clarifies that the description 'yashuqqu sanamaha' (he splits her hump) is from the right side, but Al-Hidayah notes the more correct narration is the left side, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) approaching the animals from the front and using his right hand. If the camel is difficult, either side is permissible. Finally, the dispute: Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn consider it hasan (good). The commentator notes that the author mentioned the Sahibayn's view first because he held that the fatwa is on their opinion, indicating that the operative position is that ish'ar is recommended, not disliked.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Placing a garland (piece of leather or sandal) around the neck of the sacrificial animal to mark it as a hady.
تجليل (tajlil): Covering the sacrificial animal with a cloth (jil) as a mark, but not specifically for identification alone.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as a sacrifice in Hajj.
تلبية (talbiyah): The chant 'Labbaik Allahumma Labbaik...' uttered upon entering the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is a recommended sunnah for marking hady in camels and cows, based on Quranic evidence, and it should be performed after the talbiyah.

Ish'ar: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Practice
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar and the practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on ish'ar for camels, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is recommended (hasan) for camels according to the Sahibayn, but disliked (makruh) by Abu Hanifa; the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn.

Ish'ar is another method of marking the hady, specific to camels. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute over its ruling. This lesson examines the different positions, the practical procedure, and a detail about which side of the hump to incise, based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh (disliked); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it hasan (good).
2
Identify the tarjih
The fatwa is on the opinion of the Sahibayn because the author of the matn mentioned their view first and held that fatwa is based on their saying.
Tarjih: the process of preferring one opinion over another within a madhhab.
3
Describe the procedure of ish'ar
Pierce the lower part of the hump on the right (or left) side with a needle or spearhead until blood comes out, then smear the hump with the blood.
This is done to notify people that the animal is a sacrifice.
4
Analyze the side issue
Al-Hidayah states that the left side is more correct based on the Prophet's practice, but if the camel is stubborn, either side is permissible.
The Prophet (ﷺ) would approach from the front and strike the left side with his right hand.
5
Note the scope
Ish'ar is only for camels, not for cows or sheep.

روى الطعن في الجانب الأيسر أبو يعلى في مسنده، وروى الطعن في الجانب الأيمن مسلم (١٢٤٣) ، ينظر للروايات نصب الراية ١١٦/٣.
Chapter of Tamattu'. And he makes ish'ar for the camel according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Taqlid is better than tajlil because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran. Allah Almighty said: 'And do not [violate] the hady nor the garlands.' [Al-Ma'idah 5:2]. Thus the legality of taqlid is established by the Book and the Sunnah. Tajlil is only established by the Sunnah and it is not specifically intended for notification alone; rather, it shares other meanings: repelling flies, and repelling heat and cold. Taqlid is specifically for notification, without sharing. The image of taqlid is that one ties on the neck of his sacrificial animal a piece of leather or a sandal. The meaning is that this [animal] is prepared for bloodshed, so its skin will soon become like that piece of leather, so that it is not prevented from water and fodder when it is known that it is a hady. This is only for what is out of its owner's sight, like camels and cows; as for sheep, it would be lost if its owner is not with it, so it is not made to wear a garland. It is better to first say the talbiyah then put the garland, because he becomes a muhrim through the garland and proceeding with it, so preceding the talbiyah is better so that his commencement of ihram is with it, not with the garland. His saying: 'And he makes ish'ar for the camel according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.' Ish'ar is not recommended for other than camels. Its description: that he pierces the lower part of the hump on the right side with a needle or spearhead until blood comes out, then he smears the hump with that, as a notification to people that it is a sacrifice for Allah Almighty. And it is: that he splits its hump on the right side. And Abu Hanifa does not make ish'ar. * His saying: 'And it is: that he splits its hump on the right side.' In Al-Hidayah: the more correct is the left side, i.e., the more correct in the narration, because the hadaya were coming towards the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and he would enter between every two camels from the direction of their heads, and the spear was in his right hand inevitably, so his thrust would first fall on the left side of the camel. If the camel is stubborn, it is permissible to split whichever side he wishes according to his ability. * His saying: 'And Abu Hanifa does not make ish'ar.' He only mentioned their saying before his saying because he held that the fatwa is on their saying. In Al-Hidayah it is mentioned that ish'ar is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them it is good (hasan). Abu Ya'la reported the piercing on the left side in his Musnad, and Muslim (1243) reported the piercing on the right side; see the narrations in Nasb al-Rayah 3/116.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah is a commentary on the matn of Al-Quduri, explaining two ways of marking the hady (sacrificial animal) in Hajj Tamattu': taqlid (placing a garland) and ish'ar (making a cut to draw blood). The commentary begins by presenting the ruling on ish'ar from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is recommended, then immediately compares taqlid and tajlil (covering the animal with a cloth). The author proves the preference for taqlid through the Quranic verse (5:2) where 'qala'id' (garlands) are mentioned, establishing its legitimacy by both Book and Sunnah, while tajlil is only from Sunnah and serves multiple purposes (repelling flies, heat, cold), not exclusively for identification. Taqlid is solely for identification. The description of taqlid is given: tying a piece of leather or sandal on the neck of a camel or cow to signal it is a hady, so it is not denied water or fodder. This is not done for sheep as they would wander off. Then the order of actions: first talbiyah, then taqlid, because ihram should be entered with talbiyah, not with the garland. Returning to ish'ar, the text states it is only for camels (not other animals) and describes the act: piercing the lower hump on the right side with a needle or spear until blood appears, then smearing it as a mark. On page 401, the commentary clarifies that the description 'yashuqqu sanamaha' (he splits her hump) is from the right side, but Al-Hidayah notes the more correct narration is the left side, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) approaching the animals from the front and using his right hand. If the camel is difficult, either side is permissible. Finally, the dispute: Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn consider it hasan (good). The commentator notes that the author mentioned the Sahibayn's view first because he held that the fatwa is on their opinion, indicating that the operative position is that ish'ar is recommended, not disliked.

Key Terms
إشعار (ish'ar): Making an incision in the hump of a camel to draw blood as a mark that it is a sacrificial animal.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as a sacrifice in Hajj.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj.
سنام (sanam): Hump of a camel, where the incision for ish'ar is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Right
B) Left
C) Either
D) Both

Key Takeaway
Ish'ar is recommended (hasan) for camels according to the mufta bihi, and the preferred side for the incision is the left side of the hump.

Preferred Side for Cutting the Hump (Shaqq al-Sanam)
Explains the preferred side for cutting the hump of the sacrificial camel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred side for cutting the hump of the sacrificial camel, explain the dalil from the Prophet's practice, and identify the exception for difficult animals.

Core Idea
Left side is sunnah for cutting the hump; the right side is less preferred.

In Hajj, the method of slaughtering the sacrificial animal carries specific sunnan. A key detail is the side from which the hump is cut. The matn initially instructs the right side, but the sharh in Al-Hidayah corrects this based on a stronger narration of the Prophet's practice. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical concession for untamed animals.

Guided Path
1
State the initial ruling in the matn
The matn of Al-Quduri says to cut the hump from the right side. Identify this as the starting point of the discussion.
This ruling is found in the base text before the correction.
2
Identify the correction from Al-Hidayah
The sharh from Al-Hidayah states that the more correct (al-ashbah) is the left side. Understand that this correction overrides the matn based on a stronger narration.
The term 'al-ashbah' indicates the preferred opinion in the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the dalil from the Prophet's practice
The Prophet (ﷺ) would walk between the camels from the front, holding a spear in his right hand, so his first strike would naturally fall on the left side of the animal. This physical description establishes the sunnah of cutting from the left.
The dalil is fi'li (action-based) and is considered zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah.
4
Note the exception for difficult animals
If the camel is difficult (untamed), it is permissible to cut from whichever side is easier. This shows that the ruling is sunnah, not obligatory, and necessity permits flexibility.
The exception is based on ability and prevents hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع. * قوله : (وهو: أن يَشقَ سَنَامَها من الجانب الأيمن). وفي «الهداية»(۱): الأشبه : هو الأيسر، أي الأشبه إلى الصواب في الرواية ؛ لأن الهدايا كانت مقبلةً إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكان يدخل بين كل بعيرين من قبل الرؤوس، وكان الرمح بيمينه، لا محالة، فكان يقع طعنه أولاً على يسار البعير. فإن كانت البدنةُ صعبة: جاز أن يَشقَّ من أي الجانبين شاء على حسب قدرته.
Chapter of Tamattu'. His statement: (It is: to cut its hump from the right side). And in Al-Hidayah: The more correct is the left side, meaning more correct to the truth in the narration; because the sacrificial animals were brought facing the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he would enter between every two camels from the direction of their heads, and the spear was in his right hand, inevitably, so his stab would first fall on the left side of the camel. If the camel is difficult (untamed), then it is permissible to cut from whichever side he wishes according to his ability.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling on how to perform shaqq (cutting the hump) of the sacrificial camel (hady) in the context of tamattu'. The matn initially states that it is from the right side, but the sharh from Al-Hidayah corrects this, indicating that the more authentic practice is from the left side. The reasoning is based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ): when he received sacrificial animals, he would walk between them from the front, holding the spear in his right hand. Thus, the initial strike would naturally fall on the left side of the animal. However, if the animal is difficult (not tame), it is permitted to cut from whichever side is easier, based on necessity. This shows the Hanafi approach of preferring the sunnah practice but allowing flexibility for practicality.

Key Terms
شق السنام (shaqq al-sanam): cutting the hump of the sacrificial camel
الأشبه (al-ashbah): the more correct or preferable opinion
البدنة (al-badanah): a sacrificial camel

D) The front

Key Takeaway

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ish'ar (Marking the Hady)
Dispute between Hanafi authorities and Shafi'i on ish'ar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions on ish'ar, identify the dalil for each, and explain why the mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Ish'ar: conflict between ritual benefit and animal welfare; Hanafis differ on which prevails.

This passage addresses the ruling on ish'ar — cutting or branding the hump of a sacrificial camel to mark it as hady. While some consider it a recommended practice, Abu Hanifa viewed it as a prohibited mutilation. The commentary explains the reasoning on both sides and concludes which opinion is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa says makruh, the Sahibayn say hasan. Note that the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
The commentator mentions the Sahibayn's view first because it is the fatwa.
2
Identify the opposing school
The Shafi'i school considers ish'ar sunnah based on a narration that the Prophet performed it.
This sets up the cross-madhhab dimension.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that ish'ar is more binding than taqlid (necklace) because it cannot be removed, making it more effective for identification.
They acknowledge that it resembles muthla but consider it hasan because of the benefit.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa prioritizes the prohibition of muthla (causing unnecessary pain to animals) over the benefit. He cites the Prophet's prohibition of harming animals except for food.
This is a classic example of ta'arud (conflict) and tarjih (preference).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, those following Abu Hanifa will only use taqlid, while those following the Sahibayn or Shafi'i may perform ish'ar.
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, so ish'ar is considered hasan in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (ولا يُشعر عند أبي حنيفة). إنما ذكر قولهما قبل قوله ؛ لأنه كان يرى الفتوى على قولهما. ذكر في «الهداية» (۳) : أن الإشعار مكروه عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما حسن. وعند الشافعي (۱) : سنةٌ ؛ لأنه مروي عن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام). ولهما: أن المقصود من التقليد أن لا يُهاج ولا يُؤذى إذا ورد ماء أو كلاً، أو يُردَّ إذا ضلَّ، فإنه في الإشعار أتم؛ لأنه ألزم؛ لأن القلادة قد تُحل أو تسقط، والإشعار لا يُفارقها، فكان ألزم لها من التقليد. ولأن التقليد مباين لها يحتمل المزايلة، والإشعار متصل بها، لا يحتمل الانفصال. فمن هذا الوجه ينبغي أن يكون سُنَّةً، إلا أنه عارضه كونه مثلة، فقالا : بحسنه. ولأبي حنيفة : أنه مثلةٌ، والمثلة منهي - ولو وقع التعارض بكونه مثلة وكونه سنة: فالترجيح للمُحرم؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن إيلام الحيوان، إلا لمأكله» (۳). وهذا إيلام لغير مأكلة.
His statement: (And he does not do ish'ar according to Abu Hanifa). He mentioned their statement (Sahibayn) before his statement because he saw that the fatwa is according to their statement. It is mentioned in Al-Hidayah that ish'ar is makruh according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Sahibayn) it is hasan. According to Al-Shafi'i: it is sunnah because it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Their proof (for Sahibayn): the purpose of taqlid is that it is not disturbed or harmed when it goes to water or pasture, or that it is returned if it strays; this is more complete in ish'ar because it is more binding; since the necklace may be untied or fall off, while ish'ar does not leave it, so it is more binding than taqlid. And because taqlid is separate from it and may be detached, while ish'ar is attached to it and cannot be separated. From this perspective, it should be sunnah, except that it is opposed by the fact that it is mutilation (muthla), so they (Sahibayn) said it is hasan. And Abu Hanifa's proof: it is muthla, and muthla is prohibited - and if there is a conflict between it being mutilation and it being sunnah, the prohibition takes precedence; because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited causing pain to animals except for eating. And this is causing pain without eating.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling of ish'ar (marking the sacrificial camel by cutting or branding its hump to indicate it is for sacrifice). The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa, ish'ar is not done (i.e., it is not recommended). The commentator notes that the author mentioned the Sahibayn's view before Abu Hanifa's because he considers the fatwa to be on their view. In Al-Hidayah, Abu Hanifa's view is that ish'ar is makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it hasan (good). Imam Al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah (recommended) based on a narration from the Prophet. The passage then details the reasoning of the Sahibayn: ish'ar is more effective than taqlid (hanging a necklace) for identifying the sacrificial animal because it is permanent and cannot be lost. Despite this, Abu Hanifa argues that ish'ar is a form of mutilation (muthla), and mutilation is prohibited in Islam. He cites the principle that the Prophet forbade harming animals except for eating, and since the scar of ish'ar is not for consumption but for identification, it falls under prohibited harm. Thus, Abu Hanifa prioritizes avoiding mutilation over the benefit of permanent identification. The Sahibayn acknowledge that it resembles muthla but consider it hasan due to its ritual purpose and the fact that it was practiced by some Companions. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the author is the view of the Sahibayn, but Abu Hanifa's view is also considered.

Key Terms
الإشعار (al-ish'ar): marking the sacrificial camel by cutting or branding its hump
التقليد (al-taqlid): hanging a necklace or sandal around the camel's neck to mark it as sacrificial
المثلة (al-muthla): mutilation or disfigurement of an animal

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is not mentioned in the Quran
B) It causes unnecessary pain and is a form of mutilation
C) It is only for camels and not for cows
D) It is not practiced by the Companions

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that ish'ar is hasan (recommended) due to its binding nature, despite Abu Hanifa's view that it is makruh due to mutilation.

Ruling on Ish'ar in Tamattu'
Inter-madhhab dispute on ish'ar for mutamatti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi reasoning for the ruling on ish'ar (marking sacrificial animals) and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When a reported sunnah conflicts with a general prohibition, the Hanafi school prioritizes the prohibition.

In the chapter on tamattu', the ruling on ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal by slitting its hump and smearing blood) is a point of ikhtilaf. The Shafi'i school holds it to be sunnah because it is reported from the Prophet. The Hanafi school, however, considers it a form of mutilation (muthlah), which is prohibited. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning, including the intra-Hanafi variation between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the overall Hanafi ruling on ish'ar. Note the difference between Abu Hanifa (haram) and the Sahibayn (hasan, i.e., commendable but not sunnah). The mufta bihi is makruh tanzihan.
The Hanafi school does not consider ish'ar as sunnah, unlike the Shafi'i.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds ish'ar to be sunnah because it is a practice reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The Shafi'i rely on the reported action of the Prophet as evidence.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is simply the narration that the Prophet performed ish'ar. They consider this sufficient to establish sunnah status.
No specific hadith text is quoted in the passage, but it is referenced as 'mawri 'an al-nabi'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that although ish'ar is reported, it involves mutilation (muthlah), which is prohibited by a general hadith forbidding causing pain to animals except for eating. Since ish'ar is not for eating, the prohibition overrides the reported practice.
The Hanafi school uses a principle of preference when conflicting evidences exist.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'i pilgrims will perform ish'ar as a sunnah; Hanafi pilgrims will avoid it (or at best consider it disliked).
This affects the actual practice of a mutamatti' during Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
وعند الشافعي (۱) : سنةٌ ؛ لأنه مروي عن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام). ولهما: أن المقصود من التقليد أن لا يُهاج ولا يُؤذى إذا ورد ماء أو كلاً، أو يُردَّ إذا ضلَّ، فإنه في الإشعار أتم؛ لأنه ألزم؛ لأن القلادة قد تُحل أو تسقط، والإشعار لا يُفارقها، فكان ألزم لها من التقليد.
ولأن التقليد مباين لها يحتمل المزايلة، والإشعار متصل بها، لا يحتمل الانفصال.
فمن هذا الوجه ينبغي أن يكون سُنَّةً، إلا أنه عارضه كونه مثلة، فقالا : بحسنه. مثلة،
ولأبي حنيفة : أنه مثلةٌ، والمثلة منهي -
ولو وقع التعارض بكونه وكونه سنة: فالترجيح للمُحرم؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن إيلام الحيوان، إلا لمأكله».
وهذا إيلام لغير مأكلة.
Chapter of Tamattu'. According to al-Shafi'i: (it is) sunnah, because it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the purpose of taqlid (garlanding) is that it should not be disturbed nor harmed when it comes to water or pasture, nor should it be turned away if it goes astray. Indeed, in ish'ar (marking with blood) it is more complete, because it is more binding; for the garland may be untied or fall off, while ish'ar does not leave it, so it is more binding for it than taqlid. And because taqlid is separate from it, subject to separation, while ish'ar is attached to it, not subject to disconnection. From this aspect, it should be sunnah, except that it is opposed by its being a mutilation (muthlah). So they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is commendable (hasan) despite being a mutilation. And for Abu Hanifa: it is a mutilation, and mutilation is prohibited. If there is a conflict between its being a mutilation and its being sunnah, the precedence is given to prohibition, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade causing pain to animals except for the purpose of eating. And this is causing pain for other than eating.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling of ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal by making a slit on its hump and smearing blood) for the mutamatti'. The Shafi'i school holds it to be sunnah because it is reported from the Prophet. However, the Hanafi school, through the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, first establishes that ish'ar is more binding than taqlid (garlanding) because it is less likely to be removed. From this perspective, it would be sunnah. But they note that it is a form of mutilation (muthlah), which is prohibited. Thus they rule it as hasan (commendable) but not sunnah. Abu Hanifa goes further, stating clearly that it is a mutilation and therefore prohibited. The text then gives the Hanafi preference: when there is conflict between the prophetic action (sunnah) and the prohibition of causing pain, the prohibition takes precedence. The evidence is the hadith forbidding causing pain to animals except for eating, and ish'ar is not for eating. Therefore, the Hanafi view is that ish'ar is at least makruh, and according to Abu Hanifa, it is haram. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that ish'ar is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful) based on the combination of the two opinions.

Key Terms
إشعار (ish'ār): Marking the sacrificial animal by making a slit on its hump and smearing blood, to distinguish it as a sacrificial animal.
تقليد (taqlīd): Placing a garland around the neck of the sacrificial animal, also to mark it.
مثلة (muthlah): Mutilation; cutting or injuring the body of an animal unnecessarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school does not consider ish'ar as sunnah?
A) Because the hadith reporting it is weak
B) Because it is a form of mutilation, which is prohibited
C) Because it is only allowed for the people of Mecca
D) Because it requires a special type of animal

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ish'ar is at best makruh tanzihan because the prohibition of mutilation overrides the reported practice of the Prophet.

Sequence and Obligations of the Mutamatti' in Tamattu'
Sequence of actions and obligations for the mutamatti' in tamattu' Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of acts performed by the mutamatti' upon entering Mecca and identify the obligation of dam (sacrificial blood) for tamattu'.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' remains in ihram after umrah until Hajj; the dam is wajib.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah clarifies the essential steps for the mutamatti' after entering Mecca. It details that he performs tawaf and sa'y for umrah but must not exit ihram until he intends Hajj. The commentator expands on the permissibility of delaying the Hajj ihram and emphasizes that the dam is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial actions
The mutamatti' upon entering Mecca performs tawaf and sa'y for umrah. This is the first step of tamattu'.
2
Note the requirement to remain in ihram
He does not become halal after umrah; he must remain in ihram until the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) when he intends ihram for Hajj.
3
Examine the flexibility in timing
If he delays the Hajj ihram to the day of Arafah, it is permissible. Advancing the ihram is better due to eagerness.
4
Recognize the obligation of dam
He must offer a dam (a sacrificial animal) as compensation for tamattu', based on Quran 2:196.
5
Understand the exit from both ihrams
When he shaves on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), he exits both the umrah and Hajj ihrams simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإن قدَّم الإحرام قبله : جاز .
وعليه دم التمتع .
فإذا حَلَق يوم النحر : فقد حَلَّ من الإحرامين .
وليس لأهل مكةَ تَمَتَّعُ، ولا قرآن،
ولأن الإحرام يُحرم ما كان مباحاً، فأما أن يُبيح ما كان محظوراً : فلا ،
والإشعار مكروه قبل الإحرام: فكذا بعده.

قوله: (فإذا دخل مكة: طاف وسعى أولاً، وطوافه وسعيه هذا
* قوله: (ولم يتحلل حتى يُحرم بالحج يوم التروية).
هذا ليس بلازم، حتى لو أحرم يوم عرفة : جاز.
قوله: (فإن قدَّم الإحرام قبله : (جاز)، وكلَّما عجل: فهو أفضل؛ لما فيه من المسارعة.
قوله: (وعليه دم) ، وهو دم التمتع ، وقد فعله بالهدي الذي ساقه. * قوله: (فإذا حلق يوم النحر : فقد حل من الإحرامين جميعاً): أي
إحرام العمرة والحجة جميعاً.
[تمتع المكي : ]

When he enters Mecca: he performs tawaf and sa'y, and does not become halal until he enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah. And if he advances the ihram before that, it is permissible. And upon him is the sacrificial blood (dam) of tamattu'. So when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he has exited from both ihrams. And it is not permissible for the people of Mecca to perform tamattu', nor qiran. And because ihram prohibits what was permissible, it does not permit what was prohibited. And ish'ar is makruh before ihram, likewise after it. For the umrah. He said: (When he enters Mecca: he performs tawaf and sa'y first, and his tawaf and sa'y are for umrah. * He said: (And he does not become halal until he enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah.) This is not binding, so if he enters ihram on the day of Arafah, it is permissible. He said: (And if he advances the ihram before it, it is permissible), and the earlier he does it, the better, because of haste. He said: (And upon him is sacrificial blood), which is the blood of tamattu', and he does it with the sacrificial animal he drove. * He said: (So when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he has exited from both ihrams): i.e., the ihram of umrah and the ihram of Hajj together. [Tamattu' of the Meccan:] He said: (And it is not permissible for the people of Mecca to perform tamattu', nor qiran).
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage enumerates the key rulings of tamattu' Hajj. Upon entering Mecca, the mutamatti' performs tawaf and sa'y for umrah, but does not shave or exit ihram; rather, he remains in ihram until the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (day of Tarwiyah) when he intends ihram for Hajj. If he delays this ihram until the day of Arafah, it is also valid. He must offer a dam (sacrificial animal) for tamattu'. On the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (day of Nahr), when he shaves, he exits both the umrah and Hajj ihrams. People of Mecca or those residing in the Haram may not perform tamattu' or qiran; they must perform ifrad. The commentary clarifies that the tawaf and sa'y are specifically for umrah, not for Hajj, and that the requirement to remain in ihram is not absolute; one can delay the ihram for Hajj until later. Additionally, ish'ar (marking the animal) is makruh both before and after ihram, consistent with the previous discussion on its ruling.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing umrah in the months of Hajj and then performing Hajj in the same year after exiting ihram for umrah but without returning home.
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The obligatory sacrifice (blood) that the mutamatti' must offer as compensation for combining umrah and Hajj in one journey.
الإحرام (al-ihrām): The state of consecration for Hajj or umrah, involving specific prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the mutamatti' do upon entering Mecca?
A) He performs tawaf, sa'y, and immediately shaves to become halal
B) He performs tawaf and sa'y for umrah and remains in ihram until the day of Tarwiyah
C) He only performs sa'y and then waits for Hajj
D) He performs tawaf for Hajj directly

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' performs umrah upon entering Mecca, remains in ihram until Hajj, and must offer a dam.

Prohibition of Tamattu' for Meccans and Ruling on Ish'ar
Prohibition of tamattu' for Meccans and ruling on ish'ar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Meccans are prohibited from performing tamattu' or qiran and state the ruling on ish'ar.

Core Idea
A Meccan cannot combine umrah and Hajj due to lack of travel; ish'ar is makruh before and after ihram.

This passage then addresses a key restriction: residents of Mecca may not perform tamattu' or qiran. The reason is that the essential requirement of travel is absent for them, as ihram prohibits what was permissible but does not permit what was prohibited. Additionally, the commentator clarifies that ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal) is makruh both before and after entering ihram, consistent with previous rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Meccans
The text states clearly that it is not permissible for the people of Mecca to perform tamattu' or qiran. They must perform ifrad (separate Hajj only).
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that ihram prohibits what was permissible but does not permit what was prohibited. This implies that tamattu'/qiran are based on the concession for travelers; Meccans are not travelers, so the concession does not apply.
3
Apply to cross-madhhab difference
Note that the Shafi'i school allows Meccans to do tamattu', but the Hanafi school prohibits it. This difference stems from different interpretations of the underlying rationale.
4
Examine the ruling on ish'ar
The text adds that ish'ar (marking the animal) is makruh both before and after ihram. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that ish'ar in general is disliked.
5
Connect to the broader context
These rulings ensure that the rituals are performed according to the Sunna, respecting the special status of the Haram and avoiding innovations.

تمتع (tamattu'): Performing umrah in the months of Hajj and then performing Hajj in the same year after exiting ihram for umrah but without returning home.
قرآن (qiran): Entering ihram for both umrah and Hajj simultaneously with one nīyah.
إشعار (ish'ār): Marking a sacrificial animal by making a cut on its hump or side to indicate it is a hady.
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but leaving it is rewarded.
